1401 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


In Interest of Polovchak


No. 80-2857


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


104 Ill. App. 3d 203; 432 N.E.2d 873; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 3906; 59 Ill. Dec. 929



December 30, 1981, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 23, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. JOSEPH C. MOONEY, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent parents sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which declared their minor child a minor in need of supervision and a ward of the court pursuant to the procedures set forth in the Juvenile Court Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, para. 701-1, et seq. (1979).


OVERVIEW: The child ran away from home and stayed with his older sister and cousin at his cousin's apartment because he did not want to return with his parents to the Ukraine. On appeal, the court reversed. The court found that a full and complete evidentiary hearing was conducted because all of the parties testified and were allowed to present witnesses and conduct thorough cross-examinations, and the parents were not prevented from presenting any evidence. The court also found that the trial judge weighed all of the evidence presented according to the required legal standards. The court determined that although a single isolated act by a minor in Illinois could be sufficient to establish that the minor was beyond the control of his parents provided the minor's conduct was seriously harmful and points to grave danger, the child's conduct in this case did not rise to that level because the child's action was an exaggerated manifestation of parent-child conflict, and was not sufficiently serious to warrant a finding that he was beyond his parents' control. Additionally, the child, having gone to live with his sister and cousin, was not placed in a situation of grave danger.


OUTCOME: The court reversed in favor of the parents in the action by the state to declare the parent's child a minor in need of supervision and a ward of the court.

 

1402 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Duewel v. Lahman


No. 81-144


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


103 Ill. App. 3d 220; 430 N.E.2d 662; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 3843; 58 Ill. Dec. 630



December 29, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County; the Hon. PAUL W. SCHNAKE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant county appealed the judgment from the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), which denied its motions for directed verdicts and judgment notwithstanding the verdict. Defendant camper owner appealed from the jury's verdicts finding him guilty of negligence and contributory negligence in a personal injury action filed against him by plaintiffs, a married couple, after their car struck the camper at an intersection missing a stop sign.


OVERVIEW: The camper owner was not familiar with the road that he was driving on, but he felt that he was on a preferred highway. The appellate court found that under the circumstances, the camper owner should have been prepared to yield to traffic from the right. There was evidence that he saw the car right before it hit his van; there were no skid marks. He either did not look to the right as he approached the intersection or he was traveling too fast when he entered it. The court found that the camper owner was negligent and contributorily negligent. The camper owner contended that the county's failure to replace the stop sign was the proximate cause of the accident. On appeal, the court found that the negligence of the camper owner and the county was the proximate cause of the accident. The court rejected the county's argument that it lacked notice of the missing sign in time to replace it. The court found that the highway department staff cut grass near the intersection earlier on the day of the accident when the stop sign was missing. The court affirmed all aspects of the circuit court's judgment but remanded for a redetermination of the damages awarded to the car driver's wife.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court and remanded for a redetermination of damages for the plaintiff wife jointly against the county and the camper owner. The court affirmed the judgment against the county for the camper owner's wife and affirmed the judgment setting aside the verdict for damages against the camper owner.

 

1403 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Williamson v. Doyle


No. 81-2516


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


103 Ill. App. 3d 770; 431 N.E.2d 1198; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 3879; 59 Ill. Dec. 441



December 29, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. JOSEPH SCHNEIDER, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner citizen sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) sustaining a decision of respondent municipal electoral board rejecting a petition that proposed a referendum petition on the subject of whether the municipality should adopt an ordinance providing a procedure for recall of elected officials.


OVERVIEW: The citizen proposed that the referendum question be placed on the general election ballot in the city, but the municipal electoral board objected, arguing that the referendum was not authorized by Ill. Const. art. VII, as required under § 28-7 of the Election Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 46, para. 28-7 (1979). Ill. Const. art. VII gave voters the power by referendum to adopt or alter forms of local government and establish public offices. Affirming the trial court's decision, the court held that the enactment of a recall procedure was not one of the proper uses of a referendum under Ill. Const. art. VII, § 7(3), which applied to non home rule units. Further, the court concluded that the omission of this use of a referendum by the constitution's drafters had not been inadvertent. Thus, the court determined that the trial court had been correct in finding that recall had not been made a fundamental right of the body politic in Ill. Const. art. VII, § 7(3) and in resisting the citizen's efforts to have the referendum issue placed on the ballot.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

1404 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Betts v. Dep't of Registration & Educ.


No. 81-456


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


103 Ill. App. 3d 654; 431 N.E.2d 1112; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 3866; 59 Ill. Dec. 355



December 28, 1981, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 1, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. JAMES C. MURRAY, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff pharmacists sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which affirmed the order of defendant, the department of registration and education (department), which revoked the pharmacists' licenses.


OVERVIEW: The pharmacists argued that the department violated their rights to due process because hearings in the matter of their license suspensions were held in the presence of an appointed hearing officer and at least one member of the board, instead of a quorum of the board. The pharmacists argued that by failing to have a quorum present during each session, the board did not have power to act. The court held that in the absence of a statutory provision to the contrary, it was not necessary that those persons who were ultimately charged with making findings of fact, conclusions of law, and recommendations or administrative decisions be personally present to hear evidence presented during an administrative proceeding. The department director appointed a hearing officer to expedite the hearing of evidence and required that at least one member of the board was present for each session. Each board member was furnished with a transcript of the proceedings, which they each considered before making their decisions. The court held that the actions taken by the department director did not prejudice the due process rights of the pharmacists and affirmed the ruling of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the revocation of the license of one of the pharmacists and reversed and remanded the matter pertaining to the revocation of the license of the other pharmacist.

 

1405 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Easter


No. 80-393


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


102 Ill. App. 3d 974; 430 N.E.2d 612; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 3794; 58 Ill. Dec. 580



December 23, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. ROBERT MASSEY, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed her conviction from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), where a jury found defendant guilty of voluntary manslaughter, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-2 (1977), and armed violence, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 33A-2 (1977). Defendant challenged the sufficiency of the indictment, the application of the armed violence statute, proof of her guilt, the jury instructions, and the grand jury proceedings.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that her conviction for armed violence based on the predicate felony of voluntary manslaughter should be reversed because the indictment did not adequately charge the offense. The court agreed and noted that the indictment made no reference to either of the alternative statutory provisions regarding voluntary manslaughter and failed to set for the nature and elements of the offense. Defendant next argued that the indictment should have been dismissed due to prosecutorial misconduct during the grand jury proceedings. Because the record was incomplete on the issue, the court resolved doubts caused by the incompleteness against defendant and presumed that the trial court ruled correctly. The court also determined that the jury's determination that defendant was guilty of voluntary manslaughter was not so unreasonable as to raise reasonable doubt of defendant's guilt. Finally, the court rejected defendant's contention that she was denied a fair trial because the trial court did not give a "forcible felony" jury instruction on her theory of self-defense. The court held that the giving of the instruction would not likely have affected the trial's outcome.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for armed violence and affirmed her conviction for voluntary manslaughter. Because the trial court might have been influenced by the armed violence conviction in sentencing defendant for voluntary manslaughter, the court remanded the case for a new sentencing hearing on the voluntary manslaughter conviction alone.

 

1406 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Evergreen Park v. Russell


No. 80-2060


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


102 Ill. App. 3d 723; 430 N.E.2d 587; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 3756; 58 Ill. Dec. 555



December 21, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. ROGER SEAMAN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which found him guilty of two violations of Village of Evergreen Park, Ill., Ordinance § 20-137 for parking a motor home, which was a prohibited vehicle, overnight on a certain street on two different occasions. He contended that the ordinance under which he was convicted was unconstitutional and that the village failed to prove a prima facie case.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of two violations of § 20-137 for parking a recreational vehicle in his street after certain hours, and he was fined. The trial court denied defendant's motion for a directed finding that the parking tickets failed to apprise defendant of what, if any, aspect of the ordinance was violated, that the ordinance was unconstitutional and vague, and that the village had failed to prove its cause of action. The court first found that the ordinance, which banned overnight parking, was a reasonable exercise of a municipality's police power and was constitutional. It served a public purpose, and neither the ordinance nor the parking tickets were vague. Further, the officer's issuance of parking tickets to a recreational vehicle, which came within the definition of "motor home," constituted a prima facie proof of a violation, and defendant did not introduce any evidence to rebut either the commission of a violation or that he was not the owner of the vehicle. The court held that the testimony of the officer concerning his radio check as to ownership was sufficient proof of ownership.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and fines for illegal parking.

 

1407 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Moore


No. 80-2429


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


105 Ill. App. 3d 264; 434 N.E.2d 300; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 3908; 61 Ill. Dec. 147



December 15, 1981, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 3, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. DANIEL J. WHITE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of robbery.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended that his arrest without a warrant was illegal in that police used a subterfuge to lure him from his home and effect the arrest in a public place, he was denied the effective assistance of counsel, and the trial court improperly excluded evidence tending to prove that defendant had not been identified as the robber prior to his arrest. The court affirmed. The court found that the police did not conceal their identities or the fact that they were investigating a robbery, and the subterfuge allegedly used did not violate fundamental fairness. The court determined that defendant's arrest, based on probable cause, was legal and the motion to quash the arrest and suppress evidence was properly denied. The court also found that defense counsel's failure to object to evidence of computer records did not prejudice defendant and could not have been grounds for reversal. The court concluded that the person who identified defendant as the robber had made no statement or identification inconsistent with her in-court identification and testimony.


OUTCOME: The conviction for robbery was affirmed.

 

1408 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Kulpa


No. 80-1159


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


102 Ill. App. 3d 571; 430 N.E.2d 164; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 3733; 58 Ill. Dec. 222



December 14, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. LAWRENCE I. GENESEN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) which, following a jury trial, convicted defendant of three counts of aggravated battery. The trial court found that the offense was accompanied by exceptionally brutal and heinous behavior indicative of wanton cruelty and sentenced defendant under the extended term provision of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para 1005-5-3.2(b)(2) (Supp. 1978).


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his former brother-in-law got into a fight. During the fight, defendant drew a knife and stabbed the brother-in-law. While the brother-in-law attempted to escape and was crawling away, defendant continued to stab him. The brother-in-law was stabbed 26 times. A psychiatrist testified that defendant was paranoid and that, at the time of the attack, he was suffering from a mental disease. Defendant contended that the trial court abused its discretion in sentencing him to an extended term of imprisonment and in refusing to give jury instructions and jury verdict forms on each count of aggravated battery. Defendant also argued that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-5-3.2(b)(2) was unconstitutional. The court held that there was ample evidence to sustain the extended term sentence where the offense was accompanied by exceptionally brutal behavior indicative of wanton cruelty. The court also found that the trial court did not err in refusing to give the jury instructions and verdict forms because, where a general verdict was returned, defendant was considered guilty on each count. Finally, the court determined that the extended sentencing was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1409 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Havens v. Miller


Nos. 81-2464, 81-2465, 81-2466, 81-2467 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


102 Ill. App. 3d 558; 429 N.E.2d 1292; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 3732; 57 Ill. Dec. 929



December 11, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. JOSEPH SCHNEIDER, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgments reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant individual sought review of judgments from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that denied petitions for judicial review after appellee Educational Officers Electoral Board overruled objections to the nomination petitions that appellees, candidates for a school board, filed for positions on an election ballot under Ill. Const. art. 13, § 2 (1970), and the Illinois Election Code § 10-4, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 46, para. 10-4 (1979).


OVERVIEW: The candidates filed verified statements of economic interests with the secretary of the school board, who forwarded them to the county clerk two days after the filing deadline expired. Paragraph 10-4 required each sheet of a nomination petition to include a sworn statement from the circulator. A circulator did not certify under oath that he believed that the signers gave their correct residence addresses. Reversing, the court said that the objections should have been sustained. The court could not have said that the sanction of removing the candidates from the ballot was not rationally related to the legitimate state interest in protecting the integrity of the electoral process by helping to ensure that candidates would have strictly complied with the requirements of the election laws. Removal did not deprive the candidates of their right to due process of law. After the candidates failed to comply with the mandatory requirements of para. 10-4, each sheet of their nomination petitions was invalid. There was a complete failure to comply with that requirement of para. 10-4.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgments that overruled the objections with directions to remove the candidates from the ballot.

 

1410 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Turner v. Thompson


No. 80-2371


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


102 Ill. App. 3d 838; 430 N.E.2d 157; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 3774; 58 Ill. Dec. 215



December 11, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. JOHN J. MORAN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff tenant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which entered judgment in favor of the landlords in the tenant's action to recover damages for personal injuries sustained when the tenant fell on the landlords' premises. The circuit court also ruled in favor of the landlords on a counterclaim and awarded the landlords unpaid rent and damages to the premises.


OVERVIEW: The tenant brought an action against the landlords in negligence and nuisance to recover damages for injuries sustained when the tenant fell down the stairs behind the landlords' building. The landlords filed a counterclaim for unpaid rent and damages to the premises. The jury awarded both parties damages in a general verdict and found the tenant contributorily negligent in an answer to a special interrogatory. The circuit court vacated the general verdict and entered judgment in favor of the landlords on both the complaint and counterclaim. The tenant appealed, contending that the special interrogatory was improper because it was incapable of controlling the general verdict. On appeal, the court reversed, remanded, and held that because the tenant's contributory negligence was irrelevant to her action for damages for a public nuisance, the jury's special finding in response to that special interrogatory could not have been inconsistent with the general verdict rendered in favor of the tenant and was, therefore, not in proper form. Consequently, the circuit court's order vacating the general verdict and entering judgment on the special finding was in error.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the cause with directions to enter judgment in favor of tenant in the tenant's action to recover for personal injuries sustained when the tenant fell on the landlords' premises.

 

1411 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Glover-El


No. 80-1377


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


102 Ill. App. 3d 535; 430 N.E.2d 147; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 3728; 58 Ill. Dec. 205



December 10, 1981, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 7, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. THOMAS R. FITZGERALD, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that convicted him of armed robbery, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 18--2 (1977).


OVERVIEW: The evidence revealed that defendant and an accomplice robbed a store as well as several customers present at the time. Police arrested defendant several days later after finding him in a house where a kidnapped girl was reported to have been held. Defendant allegedly permitted the police to search the home for the girl, and police discovered a gun that linked defendant to the robbery. Defendant was arrested without a warrant later that day, and based upon testimony from his accomplice and others, he was convicted of armed robbery. In affirming the conviction, the court held that the trial court's finding that defendant gave consent for the search of the home was reasonable; however, it also ruled that there were no exigent circumstances to justify the warrantless entry to arrest defendant; thus, the arrest was illegal. However, based upon the overwhelming evidence of defendant's guilt, the court concluded that the trial court's failure to have suppressed evidence seized during the illegal arrest did not constitute reversible error. The court also found that the trial court properly allowed an amendment to the indictment to correct a miswriting.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for armed robbery.

 

1412 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Gutansky v. Advance Mortg. Corp.


No. 80-2905


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


102 Ill. App. 3d 496; 430 N.E.2d 122; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 3720; 58 Ill. Dec. 180



December 3, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. JOSEPH M. WOSIK and the Hon. JOSEPH T. LAVORCI, Judges, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mortgagors challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) denying their attempt to certify a class action against the appellee mortgagee.


OVERVIEW: The mortgagors paid a secured debt owed to the mortgagee, who did not release the mortgage within the 30 days required by statute. The mortgagors filed an action to recover the statutory penalty for themselves and others similarly situated. The mortgagee argued that the action could not be maintained as a class action because a class action could not be brought to recover a penalty and there was no common question of law or fact. The trial judge found in favor of the mortgagee. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that, as a matter of law, there was no predominant common question. The court found that the mortgagee conceded in its brief on appeal that it did not dispute the validity of the claim and thus, the common questions were settled.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court denying the mortgagors' request to certify their claim as a class action was affirmed.

 

1413 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Indiana H. B. R. Co.


Nos. 80-2237, 80-2534 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


102 Ill. App. 3d 811; 430 N.E.2d 104; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 3772; 58 Ill. Dec. 162



December 1, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. WILL E. GIERACH, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant railroad appealed orders from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which assessed fines against the railroad after the trial court found the railroad guilty of obstructing public travel at a railroad highway grade crossing for a period in excess of 10 minutes in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 114, para. 70 (1979).


OVERVIEW: The railroad claimed that the statute was unconstitutional as an unreasonable burden on interstate commerce. Affirming, the court said that the trial court did not err in ruling that a moving train violated the statute, which included moving as well as standing trains. The statute, construed to prohibit moving as well as standing trains from obstructing a railroad highway grade crossing for a period in excess of 10 minutes, was not an unconstitutional and unreasonable interference with interstate commerce. There was a reasonable basis for the enactment of the statute: to protect the health, safety, and welfare of the citizens of Illinois from the danger of being cut off from emergency police, fire, and ambulance services. Trains blocking main thoroughfares for extended periods of time created safety problems and obstructed the flow of interstate highway traffic. Although the statute might have imposed some burdens on the railroad, the burdens had to be weighed against a significant countervailing safety interest. The statute's impact on interstate commerce was not such that it materially restricted the free flow of commerce across state lines.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders.

 

1414 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Clark


No. 80-435


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


102 Ill. App. 3d 414; 429 N.E.2d 1255; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 3709; 57 Ill. Dec. 892



November 30, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. BRIAN L. CROWE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a bench trial in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), defendant was convicted of deviate sexual assault and two counts of armed robbery and concurrently sentenced to an extended term of 50 years. Defendant argued on appeal that he was not proved sane beyond a reasonable doubt, the extended term sentencing statute was unconstitutionally vague, and the trial court abused its discretion in imposing the sentences.


OVERVIEW: Defendant broke into the victims' home and held a gun to the head of a one-year-old while threatening to kill him if the parents failed to do as he ordered. After the husband's hands and feet were tied the wife was told to disrobe. The wife was thrown to the floor and forced to commit a deviate sexual act while husband and child watched. Defendant then ransacked their home. The court held that the state met its burden of proving defendant legally responsible at the time of the incident. The evidence suggested a deliberate, rational approach to the offense. And, although here was evidence that defendant suffered from a mental disease or defect, the court found nothing to suggest that it deprived defendant of the ability to appreciate the criminality of his conduct or conform his conduct to the requirements of the law. The court also held that the extended term statute was not unconstitutionally vague in its use of the phrase "exceptionally brutal or heinous behavior indicative of wanton cruelty." Finally, the court held that that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in imposing sentence. Accordingly, the convictions and sentence were affirmed.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and the sentences were affirmed.

 

1415 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Murphy


No. 80-2108


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


102 Ill. App. 3d 448; 430 N.E.2d 94; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 3714; 58 Ill. Dec. 152



November 30, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. FRANCIS J. MAHON, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which transferred them from a youth correctional center to an adult facility pursuant to the Unified Code of Corrections, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, paras. 1003-10-7(a), § 1005-8-6(c) (1979).


OVERVIEW: Defendants were juveniles, tried as adults, and convicted after pleas of guilty to the crimes of rape, deviate sexual assault, armed robbery, and aggravated kidnapping. Defendants were sentenced to the Department of Corrections for 14 years on each charge, to run concurrently. Hearings were held by the circuit court on three separate petitions filed by the State, after defendants reached age 17, to transfer one or both of them from the juvenile to the adult division of the Department of Corrections. Affirming, the court held that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague and was legislatively intended to provide for a fair and impartial transfer decision. The court also held that the facts determined at the first two hearings were not collateral estoppel and were properly received at the last hearing because new evidence was considered.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

 

1416 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Baker


No. 79-463


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


101 Ill. App. 3d 1114; 428 N.E.2d 1188; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 3635; 57 Ill. Dec. 508



November 24, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Tazewell County; the Hon. ARTHUR H. GROSS, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Circuit Court of Tazewell County (Illinois), revoking his probation and sentencing him to a term of imprisonment of 364 days on his convictions for aggravated assault and unlawful use of weapons. A plea of guilty had been negotiated in exchange for a one year probationary term, conditioned on defendant's voluntary commitment for psychiatric treatment and 90 days in the county jail.


OVERVIEW: After his conviction, defendant left the hospital where he was undergoing psychiatric treatment without permission. At his revocation hearing, he rejected the services of the court-appointed attorney, despite being informed that he would be left without an attorney at the hearing due to the denial of his motion for a continuance to secure new counsel, and he failed to cross examine the State's witnesses or offer any evidence in his defense. On appeal, defendant contended that he had not effectively waived his right to counsel at the hearing and that his bail bond deposit was improperly taxed for the public defender's services. Because the State concurred in the latter contention, the court reversed that portion of the judgment below. Further, as to the waiver of counsel, the court ruled that the trial court failed to adhere to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-6-4(c) requiring it to determine in open court that defendant understood the purpose and nature of the procedure, his right to confront and cross examine witnesses, and the sentence that could be imposed. Thus, it could not be concluded that defendant's decision to waive counsel was knowingly and understandingly made.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order revoking defendant's probation and remanded the cause for a new probation revocation hearing.

 

1417 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Carter


No. 80-1851


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


102 Ill. App. 3d 796; 430 N.E.2d 31; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 3770; 58 Ill. Dec. 89



November 20, 1981, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 23, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. ROBERT J. COLLINS, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of four counts of violating the Franchise Disclosure Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 121 1/2, para. 716 (1979) and sentenced him to three years' imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was chairman of the board and shareholder in a corporation that was in the business of selling franchise restaurants and bakeries. Prior to the Illinois Attorney General's approval of the corporation's application to register in accordance with the Franchise Disclosure Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 121 1/2, para. 701 et seq. (1979), defendant negotiated the sale of a franchise. Defendant failed to escrow the monies in accordance with the Act, and the corporation went bankrupt. On appeal, the court held that the legislature unconstitutionally delegated authority to the Attorney General to exempt persons from criminal sanctions of the Act. The court found defendant knew that a franchise registration had not been approved at the time the franchise agreement was executed but did not know about the State's demand that he submit an escrow agreement for the franchisee's monies. Thus, the court held that such evidence was insufficient to support defendant's conviction for violating the fraudulent practice provision of the Franchise Disclosure Act.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of conviction.

People v. Bush


No. 80-70


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


103 Ill. App. 3d 5; 430 N.E.2d 514; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 3816; 58 Ill. Dec. 482



November 19, 1981, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 5, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County; the Hon. JOHN J. HOBAN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of the murders of a woman and her son and sentenced defendant to consecutive terms of natural life imprisonment, pursuant to the Unified Code of Corrections, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-8-1(a)(1) (1979).


OVERVIEW: After defendant was convicted of two murders and sentenced to consecutive terms of natural life imprisonment, defendant sought review. On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court erred in informing prospective jurors that the state would be seeking the death penalty and by asking them how this would affect their deliberations. Defendant also argued that he was denied a fair trial by the admission of expert testimony regarding blood type, by the admission of certain rebuttal testimony regarding defendant's prior use of knives, and that the consecutive life sentences were excessive and unconstitutional. The court affirmed, holding that the trial court did not err in admitting rebuttal testimony that contradicted defendant's statement on cross-examination as to his dislike for knives. The court held that the rebuttal testimony was patently relevant to the question of defendant's believability and veracity and that the jury was entitled to accept or reject the evidence. The court also held that while the trial court placed emphasis on the nature of the offense and the protection of society, it did consider the requisite factors in imposing the consecutive life sentences.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions of murder and the consecutive terms of natural life imprisonment.

Starnawski v. License Appeal Com.


No. 80-2685


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


101 Ill. App. 3d 1050; 428 N.E.2d 1102; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 3626; 57 Ill. Dec. 422



November 17, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. JAMES P. MURRAY, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff tavern owner appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which upheld the decision of defendant License Appeal Commission of the City Of Chicago (city) to revoke the owner's liquor license. In prior administrative hearings, a deputy commissioner recommended the revocation of the owner's liquor license, and the local liquor control commissioner for the city revoked the owner's license.


OVERVIEW: A police officer asked a bartender at the owner's premises where all the women were, and the bartender procured a prostitute for the police officer. The owner claimed that she was unaware of the bartender's activities and was not working because of the illness of a child. The police officer testified at the administrative hearing, but there was no testimony from the prostitute. The local liquor control commissioner for the city revoked the owner's license and refused to provide the owner with a copy of the deputy commissioner's report which recommended the revocation of the license. The lower court affirmed the administrative decision, and the court affirmed the judgment of the lower court. The court held that the refusal of the local liquor control commissioner to provide the owner with a copy of the deputy commissioner's recommendations did not violate the owner's due process rights because administrative officers were free to consult with non-investigating staff personnel. The court held that the police officer's testimony concerning his conversation with the prostitute was not inadmissible hearsay because the officer was a participant in the conversation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court, which affirmed the decision of the city to revoke the owner's liquor license.

People v. Denby


No. 80-284


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


102 Ill. App. 3d 1141; 430 N.E.2d 507; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 3814; 58 Ill. Dec. 475



November 17, 1981, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 21, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Madison County; the Hon. JOHN W. DAY, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with murder, armed violence, and involuntary manslaughter. Following a jury trial, the Circuit Court of Madison County (Illinois) convicted defendant of armed violence. Defendant was found not guilty of involuntary manslaughter, and a mistrial was declared as to the murder count due to the jury's inability to reach a verdict. Defendant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of armed violence. On appeal, the court held that defendant's oral motion for a new trial preserved all errors of record. However, the court did not address defendant's claim regarding the constitutionality of the armed violence statute because that issue was not raised at trial. The court found that the information specifically stated that the underlying felony upon which the armed violence charge was based was voluntary manslaughter, and that the jury was properly instructed. The court held that the jury's verdicts were not legally inconsistent. The court also held that statements defendant made to a police detective, while he was being returned to his cell, were properly admitted into evidence because he was afforded both an opportunity to confer with counsel and an opportunity to exercise his right to silence. In light of the clarity and detail of defendant's recollection of the events prior to the argument with the deceased, the court was not persuaded that his claimed alcoholic amnesia warranted a reversal Absent a showing that the decedent's statements were somehow connected to defendant or the crime, they were irrelevant and properly excluded.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Chicago v. Scandia Books, Inc.


No. 80-2313


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


102 Ill. App. 3d 292; 430 N.E.2d 14; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 3690; 58 Ill. Dec. 72



November 12, 1981, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 29, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. GEORGE A. HIGGINS, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, adult book store and manager, appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that permanently enjoined them from operating an adult bookstore as defined in the Chicago Adult Use Ordinance, of the City of Chicago, Ill., Municipal Code ch. 194C, §§ 2, 3, 4.1(4) (1977).


OVERVIEW: The adult book store and manager argued that the Chicago Adult Use Ordinance (ordinance), City of Chicago, Ill., Municipal Code ch. 194C, § 3A (1977) was unconstitutionally vague and violated due process. The court affirmed the permanent injunction that prohibited the adult book store from operating at its current location. The court held that the ordinance did not violate any rights under U.S. Const. amend. I because the ordinance reasonably regulated that business, and the ordinance was narrowly drawn to prevent a decrease in property values, an increase in crime, neighborhood decline, and other adverse effects on business and residential districts. Further, the ordinance's primary control feature that precluded an adult bookstore from operating within a 1000 feet of any residentially zoned district, City of Chicago, Ill., Municipal Code ch. 194C, § 4.1(2) (1977) of the ordinance, was no greater than necessary. Moreover the terms "substantial or significant" in § 3A were not too vague because each had been construed as having an ascertainable meaning in numerous other statutory schemes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that permanently enjoined the adult book store and the manager from operating an adult bookstore.

People v. Petrovic


No. 80-1899


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


102 Ill. App. 3d 282; 430 N.E.2d 6; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 3689; 58 Ill. Dec. 64



November 6, 1981, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 6, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. ROBERT MASSEY, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence of six years' imprisonment for armed violence and a concurrent three year term for aggravated battery which was entered by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), contending that the trial court failed to grant defendant a continuance, and that he was improperly sentenced.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted and sentenced to six years' imprisonment for armed violence and for aggravated battery and he appealed, contending that the trial court erred in failing to grant him a continuance to obtain a necessary witness, in failing to grant an evidentiary hearing on his motion for rehearing on his motion for new trial, in allowing testimony as to a telephone conversation, and that he was improperly sentenced. The court held that the failure of defendant to make an offer of proof prevented the state from stipulating to the testimony of the unavailable witness, and the testimony would have been cumulative because defendant had presented three other alibi witnesses. The court concluded that the enhancement of the offense of battery to aggravated battery was based on the use of a deadly weapon, and that the presence of the weapon also served as the basis for the armed violence charge. Thus, the armed violence conviction and sentence imposed thereon was improper and defendant's conviction for armed violence was reversed and his sentence vacated. The conviction and sentence for aggravated battery was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for armed violence and his sentence thereon was vacated. The conviction and sentence for aggravated battery was affirmed.

People v. Piper


No. 80-902


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


101 Ill. App. 3d 296; 427 N.E.2d 1361; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 3507; 56 Ill. Dec. 815; 27 A.L.R.4th 539



October 30, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. ROBERT COX, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed from the order of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which granted defendant's motion to suppress the weapons evidence that arose from the discovery by police of weapons in his truck during the course of a routine traffic accident investigation. The trial court found that the weapons evidence was the product of an illegal search, where the police opened defendant's truck door without permission.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with three offenses that arose from the discovery by police of weapons in his truck during the course of a routine traffic accident investigation: unlawful use of weapons in that he knowingly carried a loaded firearm in his vehicle, unlawful use of weapons in that he knowingly possessed a bludgeon, and possession of a firearm without the requisite firearm owners identification card. The trial court, after a hearing, granted defendant's motion to suppress, and the state appealed. The question was whether opening the door of a vehicle by police to examine the vehicle identification number on the door post in the course of a routine accident investigation without asking permission of the driver constituted an illegal search. The court affirmed the trial court because there was a reasonable privacy interest involved, a search occurred, and the search did not fall within the "automobile exception" because there was no evidence of the exigencies that supported such searches where criminal conduct was suspected. No neutral criteria supported an administrative or regulatory search.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order, which granted defendant's motion to suppress the evidence discovered when the police opened the door to defendant's truck, without permission, to obtain the vehicle identification number, during the routine investigation of an accident.

 

1424 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Hart


No. 80-542


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


101 Ill. App. 3d 343; 427 N.E.2d 1352; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 3514; 56 Ill. Dec. 806



October 30, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County; the Hon. BRADNER C. RIGGS, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois) convicting her of obscenity.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, an employee at an adult bookstore, was convicted of obscenity, and sentenced to 30 days in the county jail and fined $ 1,000. On appeal, the court reversed, finding that reversible error occurred when the jury was instructed that the state did not have to produce expert testimony on the question of whether or not the movies at the adult bookstore were obscene. The court explained that the instruction was unnecessary surplusage, that it served no purpose but to lessen the credibility of the testimony given by defendant's witnesses, and that it greatly increased the likelihood that the jurors might have impermissibly applied a personal, rather than a statewide, community standard. The right of defendant to introduce her own evidence tending to establish that the materials were not obscene should not have been offset by the instruction as to the state's corresponding non-duty. The court further found that the state failed to provide sufficient evidence that defendant made the movies available for viewing by the general public. Accordingly, the state failed to provide the jury with sufficient evidence of defendant's scienter.


OUTCOME: The order convicting defendant of obscenity was reversed.

Walgreen Co. v. Illinois Liquor Control Com.


No. 80-641


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


101 Ill. App. 3d 216; 427 N.E.2d 1307; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 3492; 56 Ill. Dec. 761



October 22, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Kankakee County; the Hon. JOHN F. MICHELA, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the Illinois Liquor Control Commission (commission), appealed from the order of the Circuit Court of Kankakee County (Illinois) finding that Ill. Liquor Control Commission R. 24 was unconstitutionally void. The commission also appealed from the order enjoining it from enforcing Rule 24.


OVERVIEW: The commission cited plaintiff licensee for committing 208 violations of Rule 24 by advertising that it accepted credit cards for liquor sales. The licensee filed for review in the circuit court, which found that Rule 24 was unconstitutionally void and enjoined the commission from enforcing it. On appeal, the court modified the order and affirmed. The court found that the commission only sought to enforce the third paragraph of Rule 24 and held hat the third paragraph was severable from the rest of the rule. The court determined that the commission failed to demonstrate that restricting the licensee's right to advertise protected the public health, safety, or welfare or that it promoted restraint in the purchase or consumption of alcoholic beverages. Further, the licensee's right to free speech prevailed over the commission's regulation, which did not bear a substantial relation to the interests that the Liquor Control Act sought to protect. Finally, the court held that the trial court properly granted injunctive relief because the licensee showed that it would have suffered irreparable harm if Rule 24 had been enforced and that it was without an adequate remedy at law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part the order finding that the commission rule prohibiting the licensee from advertising that it accepted credit cards for the sale of alcoholic beverages was void and enjoining the commission from enforcing that portion of the rule.

Meylor v. Boys


No. 80-333


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


101 Ill. App. 3d 148; 427 N.E.2d 1023; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 3480; 56 Ill. Dec. 618



October 20, 1981, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 23, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County; the Hon. ROBERT C. GILL, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner state employee appealed from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois), which dismissed his petition for a writ of certiorari. The employee filed his petition against respondents, the Director of the Illinois Department of Personnel and others, asking that the rules and regulations of the Department that the director relied on as the basis for his refusal to consider the employee's grievance on the merits be ruled illegal.


OVERVIEW: The employee filed a grievance after he was suspended from work for three days without pay. At each step of the grievance procedure his case was denied consideration because he insisted upon being represented by private counsel. The employee was informed that as he was represented by a collective bargaining agent, he was required by Ill. Dep't Personnel R. 3-45 and the collective bargaining agreement to be accompanied or represented by the exclusive bargaining representative. On appeal, the court found that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 127, para. 63b108c(1) provided the Department with the authority to establish a plan for resolving employee grievances and that, under Ill. Dep't Personnel R. 3-45, an employee could only be represented by the exclusive bargaining representative unless there was no such representative. The court held that this rule did unlawfully delegate to the bargaining agent the Department's decision-making power. The court further rejected the employee's claims that to require him to accept representation by the collective bargaining agent violated his rights to due process and equal protection. The court thus concluded that Rule 3-45 was valid and constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court denying the employee's petition for a writ of certiorari.

People v. Simon


Nos. 79-2468, 80-274 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) for three counts of delivery of cocaine in violation of Ill. Rev. Will County Bd. of Review v. State Property Tax Appeal Bd.


No. 80-342


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


100 Ill. App. 3d 506; 426 N.E.2d 1238; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 3355; 55 Ill. Dec. 864



September 30, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Will County; the Hon. THOMAS W. VINSON, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff county board of review assessed valuation of certain commercial property owned by defendant taxpayers. The taxpayers appealed, and defendant Illinois Property Tax Appeal Board (PTAB) lowered the assessed valuations. The board of review appealed to the Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois). The circuit court reversed in part the decision of the PTAB, and the PTAB appealed.


OVERVIEW: The PTAB determined fair market value and then applied a factor of 29.57 percent based upon the county's urban weighted median level of assessments for 1977. The circuit court affirmed the fair market values, but ruled that the PTAB exceeded its authority in applying a multiplier of 29.57 percent instead of the statutory factor of 33 1/3 percent. On appeal, the court reversed the circuit court's judgment and affirmed the decision of the PTAB. The court held: (1) since the PTAB was required to determine the correct assessment of property, the PTAB acted within its authority by taking into account the 1977 urban weighted median level of assessments; (2) the 29.57 percent figure was prima facie evidence that the level of assessments of like property within the county was lower than the 33 1/3 percent figure used by the board of review for the assessment of the taxpayer's property; (3) the PTAB had authority to grant relief from the disparity in levels of assessments within the county; and (4) the PTAB could utilize a level of assessment figure that was derived from a one-year sales ratio study when necessary to reach an equitable result.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court and affirmed the decision of the PTAB.

Robertson v. Travelers Ins. Co.


No. 79-599


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


100 Ill. App. 3d 845; 427 N.E.2d 302; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 3416; 56 Ill. Dec. 222



September 28, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County; the Hon. PATRICK J. FLEMING, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee brought an action against defendant, workmen's compensation insurer of the employer, alleging that it had caused the employee severe mental anguish and that it had committed the tort of "outrage" by its handling of the employee's workmen's compensation claim. The Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois) entered a judgment in favor of the employee, and the insurer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The insurer argued that the tort of outrage was barred by the Illinois Insurance Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 73, para. 767 (1979), or Workmen's Compensation Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 48, para. 138-1 et seq. (1979). The court affirmed the judgment, holding that the claims were allowed. The employee was not an insured, but was a third-party claimant on a policy issued by the insurer. The remedies of the Insurance Code were not available to third-party claimants. Therefore, the statute could not preclude the employee's suit. The employee was also entitled to recovery beyond the scope of the Workers' Compensation Act concerning an injury which would be compensable under the Act. The employee sued his employer's workmen's compensation insurer for injuries which occurred while he was engaged in the line of his duty. He sought compensation for injuries resulting from conduct which occurred after he had ceased to work for the employer and claimed that the insurer committed fraud. The complaint alleged that the insurer acted with the intent to injure him and that the insurer did more than simply delay payment, allegations beyond the requirements of the Workers' Compensation Act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment holding the insurer liable in outrage. The court reversed portions of the judgment relating to damages and remanded.

People v. Pace


No. 80-602


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


100 Ill. App. 3d 213; 426 N.E.2d 983; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 3315; 55 Ill. Dec. 658



September 10, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. ROBERT L. MASSEY, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which found defendant guilty of seven counts of theft in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 16-1 (1979), one count of unlawful use of weapons in violation of § 24-1, and three counts of armed violence in violation of § 33A-2.


OVERVIEW: Defendant stole paintings from an art institute where he worked. He was found guilty of theft, unlawful use of weapons, and armed violence. He appealed his convictions, and the court affirmed the decision of the trial court. The court held that § 33A-2 was not unconstitutionally vague. Section 33A-2 did not require that a weapon facilitate the underlying offense, but the mere fact that defendant carried the weapon while he committed the felony was sufficient to come within the language of the statute. The court ruled that men of common intelligence did not have to guess at the meaning of § 33A-2, and it did not differ as to its application. The court determined that the penalty to remedy the evil was not so disproportionate to the seriousness of the offense such that it shocked the moral sense, or that it was cruel or degrading. The penalty did not violate Ill. Const. art. I, § 11. The court found that the trial judge specified the reasons for the sentences imposed in accord with § 1005-4-1(c). The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in sentencing defendant for his crimes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which convicted defendant of theft, unlawful use of weapons, and armed violence.

OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of voluntary manslaughter after he killed a man in a fight in a tavern. In re Custody of Myer


No. 17034


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


100 Ill. App. 3d 27; 426 N.E.2d 333; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 3280; 55 Ill. Dec. 358

DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner father challenged the order of the Circuit Court of McLean County (Illinois), which, on the motion of respondent mother, dismissed the father's petition for visitation rights with their child.


OVERVIEW: The father filed an action for visitation with his child. The mother, who had never been married to the father, opposed the action. The trial court dismissed the petition on the ground that no cause of action was recognized for the initiation of an original proceeding by a parent seeking visitation rights with his child when he never had custody, had never been married to the natural mother, and the parties had never lived together as a family. The court reversed the order of the trial court. The court held that the language of §§ 601, 603 of the Illinois Marriage and Dissolution of Marriage Act was sufficiently broad to encompass a custody proceeding without a marriage relationship. The court held that the rights of a putative father who had acknowledged parentage of a child were recognized under the law and that by that acknowledgement, he assumed burdens along with benefits. The court ruled that the fiction of habeas corpus was no longer a proper vehicle to enforce paternal rights of visitation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the circuit court and remanded the cause with directions that the trial court receive whatever additional evidence the parties desired to offer, fix visitation rights of the father based upon the best interests of the child in the manner provided in the Illinois Marriage and Dissolution of Marriage Act, and consider such orders of support as were appropriate.

 

1435 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Carey v. Starview Drive-In Theatre, Inc.


No. 80-1538


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


100 Ill. App. 3d 624; 427 N.E.2d 201; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 3378; 56 Ill. Dec. 121



September 8, 1981, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 24, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. HAROLD A. SIEGAN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant outdoor theater challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), in plaintiff county's action for declaratory judgment which ruled that the Cook County Outdoor Movie Theater Ordinance was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: The county filed an action in the circuit court seeking a declaratory judgment that the Cook County Outdoor Movie Theater Ordinance was constitutional and an injunction barring the outdoor theater from operating without a license. Subsequent to the filing of the complaint, the theater applied for and received a license to operate as an outdoor theater, thereby rendering moot the county's prayer for injunctive relief. The court found that the outdoor theater lacked standing to contest the validity of a provision of the ordinance that proscribed the admission of minors to certain movies because it claimed to cater exclusively to adult audiences. The court held that the ordinance was not unconstitutional solely because the regulations were based on the content of communication protected from total suppression by the First Amendment. The court held that part of the ordinance was overbroad but that the portion of the ordinance requiring screening to eliminate viewing from private residences was enforceable.


OUTCOME: The court held that clauses (A) and (C) of the Cook County Outdoor Movie Theater Ordinance were constitutional. The court held that clause (B) was constitutional insofar as it applies to the exhibition of films that are viewable from "any private residence" and that clause (B) was unconstitutional to the extent it restricted the exhibition of films that were viewable only from any public street or walkway.

 

1436 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Phelan


Nos. 80-2194, 80-2654


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


99 Ill. App. 3d 925; 426 N.E.2d 925; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 3246; 55 Ill. Dec. 600



September 1, 1981, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 22, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. JEROME T. BURKE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Two defendants were charged together with two counts of delivery of a controlled substance, cocaine. In addition, first defendant was charged with delivery and possession of cocaine and second defendant was charged with possession of cocaine. In a separate action, a third defendant was charged with possession of cocaine. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) dismissed the charges. Plaintiff, the People of the State of Illinois, appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court dismissed the charges on the ground that cocaine was not a controlled substance under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1401, 1402 (1979). The trial court also found that the charging instruments failed to give defendants proper notice of the charged crimes because the instruments did not apprise defendants of the form of cocaine they were alleged to have possessed and/or sold. On appeal, the court reversed. The court first determined that the instruments on their face met the pleading requirements of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 111-3 (1979) in that they stated the name of offense, cited the relevant statutory provisions, set forth the elements of the offense, and stated the time and place of the crime and the name of the accused. The court also found that instruments properly apprised defendants of form of cocaine they were alleged to have possessed or sold. The court acknowledged that the Illinois Controlled Substances Act covered only "1" cocaine, but found that the use of the term "cocaine" in the instruments was sufficient to inform defendants that they had been charged with possession or sale of the controlled form of cocaine.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgments of the trial court and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

 

1437 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Jones


Nos. 79-1784, 80-493 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


99 Ill. App. 3d 882; 425 N.E.2d 1279; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 3239; 55 Ill. Dec. 106



August 28, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. ROBERT J. MASSEY, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which, upon a bench trial judgment, entered an order convicting defendant of possession of codeine in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1402(b) (1975) (statute) and sentenced to three years imprisonment. The State challenged the trial court's decision granting defendant's a post-conviction petition, which alleged that the statute was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Several bottles of a red substance were found in defendant's possession. It was determined that the red substance was the same type of codeine that doctors prescribed to treat a cough. On appeal, defendant argued that he was not proven guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. In order to sustain its burden of proof, the State was required to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant knowingly possessed a controlled substance in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1402(b). The court held that the critical question was whether the State proved that the substance in question was a controlled substance as defined by the Illinois Controlled Substances Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, paras. 1100-1603 (1975). The State classified the codeine as a schedule II, III, and V controlled substance. After defendant was charged, the legislature amended the Act to include codeine as a schedule II drug; however prior to that time, codeine was not a schedule II drug. Therefore, the court held that State failed to prove that codeine was a controlled substance under schedule II. Likewise, the court held that codeine was not controlled substance under schedules III and V.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision.

 

1438 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Kline


No. 79-536


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


99 Ill. App. 3d 540; 425 N.E.2d 562; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 3197; 54 Ill. Dec. 697



August 25, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Will County; the Hon. ROBERT R. BUCHAR, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision by the Circuit Court, Will County (Illinois), which entered a judgment of conviction against defendant after a bench trial and sentenced him to a term of 50 to 100 years imprisonment for murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and two co-defendants were convicted for their participation in the bludgeoning death of a student who had photographed their drug transaction. The state's key witness was defendant's wife who testified that defendant had admitted his participation in the murder and further testified as to the events of the murder, which were supported by the circumstantial evidence. On appeal, defendant contended inter alia that the evidence was insufficient to establish guilt because it was based primarily upon the testimony of his biased wife from whom he was separated. The court affirmed the conviction but remanded for sentencing. The court held that the credibility of a witness was strictly within the competence of the fact finder and that there was sufficient evidence to support the version believed where the evidence corroborated the witness' testimony. The court held that defendant was not prejudiced where the lower court restricted cross-examination of his wife on certain issues because those issues were cumulative. The court also held that defendant's sentence of 50 to 100 years might have been excessive in light of his co-defendants' sentences of 15 to 25 years.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction against defendant, reversed the sentence, and remanded for a resentencing hearing.

People v. Johnson


No. 80-2142


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


99 Ill. App. 3d 863; 425 N.E.2d 1215; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 3235; 55 Ill. Dec. 42



August 24, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. GERALD L. SBARBORO, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state challenged the order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted defendant's motion to quash his arrest and suppress evidence associated with the charge of attempt armed robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant conceded the police had probable cause for his arrest. The state's attorney conceded that there were no exigent circumstances, which eliminated the need for a warrant. The state argued that an authorized person gave the police the consent to enter the premises. The court affirmed the order because the state failed to demonstrate voluntary consent for the warrantless search. There were no exigent circumstances, which would have excused the warrantless entry and arrest. The police officers had ample opportunity to obtain a warrant before the arrest. Furthermore, there was no evidence as to the good faith of the police officers. The record did not provide the court with sufficient facts to determine whether defendant's statement was free from the taint of the illegal arrest. Therefore, it was proper to suppress the statement.


OUTCOME: The order granting defendant's motion to quash his arrest and suppress evidence was affirmed.

 

1440 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Kerouac v. Kerouac


No. 81-50


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


99 Ill. App. 3d 254; 425 N.E.2d 543; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 3151; 54 Ill. Dec. 678



August 21, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Kankakee County; the Hon. JOHN F. MICHELA, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs injured minor appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Kankakee County (Illinois), which ruled in a declaratory action against defendant insurance company that a policy of insurance issued to the injured minor's father did not afford uninsured motorist coverage against a vehicle driver who was a family member.


OVERVIEW: After the injured minor was hurt while riding as a passenger in a vehicle driven by his brother and owned by his father, he sought recovery against the father's insurance company based upon statutorily mandated uninsured motorist coverage. In reversing the trial judge, the court held that a policy provision purporting to deny coverage to family members was void as against public policy, as it would have placed an injured family member in a different position than a third party. Even though the uninsured motorist policy provision provided a two year limitation on claims, that provision did not bar a claim by the injured minor, who had until two years after his 18th birthday to file a claim. Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 83, para. 22 (1983). Collateral estoppel did not apply to the claim, as a determination that the driver of another vehicle was not at fault did not compel the finding that the driver of the vehicle in which the minor was riding was at fault, so the case was remanded for a trial. As there was a legitimate claim that the policy provision was applicable, the insurance company had not unreasonably denied the minor's claim.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the ruling of the trial court, holding that a policy provision denying uninsured motorist coverage to the injured minor's family member was void as against public policy, and remanded the case, as the doctrine of collateral estoppel did not apply.

People v. Bayless


No. 81-86


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


99 Ill. App. 3d 532; 425 N.E.2d 1192; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 3196; 55 Ill. Dec. 19



August 21, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Will County; the Hon. ROBERT R. BUCHAR, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois), which, upon bench judgment, entered an order convicting defendant of armed robbery pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 18 -- 2 (1979) and sentenced him to a term of eight years imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant contended that he was not proven guilty beyond a reasonable doubt because the State's sole identification witness allegedly did not see the face of the perpetrator of the crime. The court held that a positive identification by a single witness who had an adequate opportunity to observe the offender was sufficient to support a conviction as long as the witness's testimony was credible. The court noted that the witness testified that he saw the armed robber face-to-face for a period of approximately 15 seconds in an alleyway illuminated by streetlights some 45 to 50 feet away. While the witness first identified defendant by the hat he was wearing, the witness was able to identify defendant by his facial features. Therefore, the court held that the witness's experience was adequate to permit a positive identification. Next, the court determined that the toy gun that defendant used to commit the robbery constituted a dangerous weapon because the shape, size, weight, and composition of the toy gun made it capable of inflicting serious bodily harm, particularly if used to batter the head and face of a victim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision.

Thornton v. Mono Mfg. Co.


No. 80-573


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


99 Ill. App. 3d 722; 425 N.E.2d 522; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 3216; 54 Ill. Dec. 657; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P9080



August 20, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County; the Hon. PHILIP G. REINHARD, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff minor appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of Winnebago County, Illinois, which granted summary judgment to defendants, manufacturer and retailer, in the minor's products liability action. The court dismissed the appeal with respect to the manufacturer, but not the retailer. The minor challenged the constitutionality of the Illinois products liability statute of limitation, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 83, para. 22.2 (1979).


OVERVIEW: A minor lost his arm in an accident involving a piece of farm machinery that his grandfather had purchased a little more than 10 years before the date of the injury. The products liability statute of limitation, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 83, para. 22.2(b) (1979), provided that no products liability action based upon a theory of strict liability in tort could be commenced after 10 years from the date of sale of an allegedly defective product to its initial user. The minor argued that the statute was unconstitutional on its face and as applied to him. The court held that the statute was not a true statute of limitation because it extinguished a cause of action before it arose, but it held the statute was reasonably related to the constitutionally permissible purpose of limiting the growth of the number of claims filed for strict liability in tort, and therefore did not violate Ill. Const. art. I, § 2. The court held that the minor's claim was not protected by Ill. Const. art. I, § 12 because he did not have a vested right. The court held that the savings clause in the statute did not apply to the minor because his claim did not arise within the period permitted by the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court granting summary judgment to the retailer.

OVERVIEW: The trial court denied defendant's motion to transfer matters to another county for consolidation with an indictment issued in that county, thereafter convicted him of aggravated battery, attempted murder, and armed violence and sentenced him to a term of 60 years' imprisonment. The court held that there was sufficient evidence of evidence guilt and that the trial court properly instructed the jury on attempted murder. The court also found that the trial court complied with Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-4-1 in sentencing defendant to the maximum term.

Rayfield v. Homart Development Co.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee filed a personal injury action under the Structural Work Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 48, para. 60 et seq. (1979), against defendant property owners. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granted the property owners summary judgment, and the employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employee was injured while operating a Traxcavator at a construction site owned by the property owners. The employee contended that that the property owners were are liable under the under the Structural Work Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 48, para. 60 et seq. (1979), because the Traxcavator had no seat belt and no other type of restraining device to hold the plaintiff in place on top of the machine, in the event the machine tipped or lurched. People v. Hall
