Pioneer Towing, Inc. v. Illinois Commerce Com.


No. 80-2131


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


99 Ill. App. 3d 403; 425 N.E.2d 1109; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 3173; 54 Ill. Dec. 892



August 14, 1981, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 4, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. ARTHUR L. DUNNE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff towing company filed a declaratory judgment action against defendant, the Illinois Commerce Commission, seeking a determination that § 18a-200(3) of the Illinois Commercial Relocation of Trespassing Vehicles Law, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 18a-200(3) (1979), was unconstitutional. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) found that the statute was a valid exercise of the legislature's authority. The company appealed.


OVERVIEW: Under § 18a-200(3), the Commission was authorized to set reasonable rates, not to exceed $ 35, for the commercial towing or removal of trespassing vehicles from private property. The company filed suit, alleging that the $ 35 cap was confiscatory, in violation of Ill. Const. art. I, § 15 (1970), that the cap deprived it of property without due process of the law, in violation of U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Ill. Const. art. I, § 2 (1970), and that the cap constituted special legislation, in violation of Ill. Const. art. IV, § 13 (1970). The trial court sustained the constitutionality of the statute. On appeal, the court affirmed, concluding that the company failed to sustain its burden of demonstrating that the $ 35 rate ceiling was unreasonable as applied to all commercial towers operating under the statute. The court acknowledged that the Commission found that the company could not operate successfully at a rate of $ 35 per tow. However, the court found that there was no evidence that others in the industry could not operate at that rate. Further, the court noted that the legislature had no duty to set rates at a level that would ensure success for all operators in the business.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Schrader v. Krok


No. 80-970


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


99 Ill. App. 3d 129; 424 N.E.2d 1357; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 3134; 54 Ill. Dec. 454



August 11, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. WILLIAM D. BLOCK, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant county sheriff's merit commission brought an interlocutory appeal challenging the decision of the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which granted, on remand, an injunction, in favor of plaintiff deputies, restraining the enforcement of a commission rule restricting political activities of the deputies. The trial court had previously granted a preliminary injunction that had been reversed.


OVERVIEW: On remand, the trial court found the rule was unconstitutionally overbroad and preliminarily enjoined its enforcement. The commission appealed, contending that the trial court failed to dismiss the action in accordance with the mandate issued in the prior opinion; that the action was barred by collateral estoppel; and that the rule was not facially overbroad. The deputies sought to dismiss the appeal on the grounds of mootness because the commission enacted a new rule prohibiting political activity. The court agreed that the issue of whether the old rule was constitutionally overbroad was moot. The court held that the only persons threatened by the previous rule were the deputies, who would have standing to challenge the rule if it was applied to them in a manner which violated their first amendment rights. The deputies, however, did not challenge the rule as applied. Further, the court held that the deputies did not have standing to challenge the prior rule as unconstitutional on its face on the basis of vagueness or overbreadth. The court reasoned that they were the only ones threatened under the rule and it was supplanted by a new rule which was not directly before the court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded with directions to dismiss the complaint.

People v. Levine


No. 80-100


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


99 Ill. App. 3d 141; 426 N.E.2d 215; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 3136; 55 Ill. Dec. 240

Minnesota Mut. Life Ins. Co. v. O'Connor


No. 16764


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


98 Ill. App. 3d 1040; 425 N.E.2d 38; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 3100; 54 Ill. Dec. 526



August 7, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County; the Hon. SIMON L. FRIEDMAN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state officials appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois) that granted plaintiff insurance company's motion for summary judgment in an action to recover taxes paid pursuant to a retaliatory tax provision.


OVERVIEW: The insurance company, a Minnesota corporation licensed to sell insurance in Illinois, was sued by the state officials for deficient and delinquent taxes pursuant to the retaliatory tax provision at Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 73, para. 1056 (1979). The insurance company brought an action to recover the sums paid. The trial court granted the insurance company's motion for summary judgment and ordered the state officials to refund the money. The state officials appealed, and the court affirmed. The insurance company was not subject to the retaliatory tax because Illinois companies doing business in Minnesota were not subjected to a more onerous tax rate. A comparison of the Minnesota and Illinois privilege taxes did not show which one was invariably or even generally more harsh.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment granting the insurance company's motion for summary judgment in an action for refund of taxes paid pursuant to a retaliatory tax provision.

Carpentersville v. Fiala


No. 80-853


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


98 Ill. App. 3d 1005; 425 N.E.2d 33; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 3094; 54 Ill. Dec. 521



August 5, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Kane County; the Hon. BARRY E. PUKLIN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff village appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), which dismissed the complaint against defendant pet owner and held that Carpentersville, Ill., Village Code § 15-23 was unconstitutional. The pet owner was charged with the violation of § 15-23 because he kept more than two adult dogs in or about his single-family residence.


OVERVIEW: The pet owner pleaded not guilty and admitted that there were more than two dogs on his premises. The trial court sua sponte dismissed the complaint against the pet owner and held that the ordinance was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment and remanded the case. Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24, para. 11-60-2 authorized the village to pass and enforce all necessary police ordinances to define, prevent, and abate nuisances. Under the rational basis test, the ordinance, which limited pet ownership based on whether a residence was a single-family residence or a multiple-housing building, Carpentersville, Ill., Village Code § 15-23 was valid. The differences in the classifications included considerations of space, density and proximity to others, noise levels, and structural differences. The limitation on the number of dogs was necessary for the protection of the health and safety of the community, and the classification scheme was reasonably related to that purpose.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that held that an ordinance, which limited the number of dogs a person could own based upon the type of residence, was unconstitutional and that dismissed the complaint against the pet owner.

 

1451 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. One 1979 Pontiac Grand Prix Auto.


No. 80-519


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


98 Ill. App. 3d 841; 424 N.E.2d 973; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 3072; 54 Ill. Dec. 223



July 31, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Kankakee County; the Hon. JOHN F. MICHELA, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant car owner challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Kankakee County (Illinois), which ruled in favor of appellee state and declared the owner's automobile to be contraband per se and the property of the city police department pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 4--211 (1979).


OVERVIEW: The owner purchased a used car from a dealership. Later, the city police department confiscated the car as contraband per se because the vehicle identification number (VIN) on the car was false and the confidential VIN was illegible. The state filed a complaint for an order permitting the city to sell the car. The owner filed an interpleader and a motion to strike. The trial court entered an order declaring that the car was the property of the police department pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 4--211 (1979). On appeal, the court reversed and held that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 4--107(i) (1979) was unconstitutional as applied against the owner because it violated his due process rights. The court found that stripping an innocent purchaser of his rights to a car without giving him notice or a hearing would not assist in uncovering car thieves. The court noted that the owner was completely innocent of any wrongdoing and had no way of discovering that the car he had purchased was unconstitutional. The court also determined that the statute's classification of any automobile without an identifiable VIN as contraband per se was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment entered in favor of the state declaring that the automobile purchased by the owner was contraband per se.

 

1452 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


County of La Salle ex rel. Peterlin v. Mauzy


Nos. 81-244, 81-191 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


98 Ill. App. 3d 615; 424 N.E.2d 857; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 3040; 54 Ill. Dec. 107



July 27, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of La Salle County; the Hon. LEONARD HOFFMAN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state environmental protection agency (EPA) appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of La Salle County (Illinois), which ruled in favor of plaintiff citizens. The trial court granted a preliminary injunction against further development of the hazardous waste site by defendant applicants of a hazardous waste site (applicants) and declared that the permit issued by the EPA was void.


OVERVIEW: The applicants sought a permit to construct a hazardous waste disposal site. The EPA reviewed the application and scheduled a public hearing. The citizens attended the public hearing and filed a brief objecting to the permit. The EPA issued a permit to the applicants, allowing the development of the site. The citizens filed the instant suit, seeking a declaratory judgment that the permit was void and asking for a preliminary injunction to prevent further development of the site. The trial court agreed with the citizens that the EPA's public hearing violated the Administrative Procedures Act (act), Ill. Comp. Stat. 127/1101-1021 (1979). On appeal, the EPA contended that the citizens failed to exhaust their administrative remedies and that the complaint should have been dismissed. The court agreed. Under section 40(b) of the act, a third party could petition the EPA within 35 days for a hearing. Although the citizens did initiate EPA proceedings, they also filed the instant complaint for injunctive relief without allowing the EPA to rule on their claims. The court did not find any applicable exception to the exhaustion of remedies doctrine.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and dissolved the preliminary injunction. The citizens failed to exhaust their administrative remedies within the EPA and could not bring the instant suit for declaratory or injunctive relief.

 

1453 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Devine


No. 79-546


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


98 Ill. App. 3d 914; 424 N.E.2d 823; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 3083; 54 Ill. Dec. 73



July 24, 1981, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied August 31, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Peoria County; the Hon. ROBERT E. MANNING, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction from the Circuit Court of Peoria County (Illinois) for felony murder and armed robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted on charges of murder, felony murder, and armed robbery after he went to a motor lodge, shot and stabbed the clerk to death, and took $ 90. Defendant was acquitted of murder. On appeal, the court affirmed in part, and reversed in part. The court reversed defendant's conviction for armed robbery because the court found that it was a lesser included offense of the felony murder charge. The court reasoned that armed robbery was a lesser included offense because the felony in the felony murder was established by proof of the same or less than all of the facts required to establish the offense of murder in the course of an armed robbery. The court also found that the trial judge did not err in determining that defendant's conduct was exceptionally brutal or heinous and thus indicative of wanton cruelty. The court reasoned that in evaluating the brutality and heinousness of an offense, the entire spectrum of facts surrounding the given incident must be analyzed and evaluated. Defendant's act of stabbing the victim seven times after shooting him twice adequately spoke for itself, irrespective of whether the victim was actually dead at the time of the stabbings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part defendant's conviction and sentence for felony murder, and reversed in part defendant's conviction for armed robbery and vacated the sentence for that offense.

 

1454 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Roman


No. 79-673


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


98 Ill. App. 3d 703; 424 N.E.2d 794; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 3055; 54 Ill. Dec. 44



July 23, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. HELEN C. KINNEY, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) convicting and sentencing him for armed violence based on a jury verdict finding him guilty of armed violence, aggravated battery, and reckless conduct.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended on appeal that the armed violence statute was unconstitutional, that the jury's verdicts were legally inconsistent, and that the prosecutor's closing argument denied him a fair trial. The court affirmed the judgment. The court concluded that defendant was not aggrieved by the application of the armed violence statute. The court found that based on the record, the jury could have rationally concluded that defendant had different states of mind when he fired the several shots he fired at the victim. The court observed that there was evidence that the first shots were fired during a struggle with the victim and that the last shot was fired while the victim was prone on the ground. The court noted that the jury could have found that defendant acted recklessly in firing the initial shots and knowingly with respect to the final shot. The court concluded that the complained of arguments did not rise to the level of plain error. The court noted that the prosecutor had a legitimate right to comment upon the credibility of the witnesses and stated that it did not find that the prosecutor flagrantly exceeded that right so as to constitute plain error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court convicting and sentencing defendant for armed violence.

People v. Link


No. 80-544


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


98 Ill. App. 3d 208; 424 N.E.2d 101; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 2974; 53 Ill. Dec. 688



July 16, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Knox County; the Hon. DANIEL J. ROBERTS, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Knox County (Illinois) that held that she had committed the offense of harassment by telephone, granted the petition of the state to revoke probation, and imposed two concurrent four-year terms of imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had originally been sentenced to two consecutive terms of probation after entering guilty pleas to two of three attempt arson charges. The factual basis then presented indicated defendant had set fires at a hospital and a building after feeling rejected by males who had been counseling her. A psychiatric evaluation concluded that defendant had a long-standing and deep-seated neurotic preoccupation with sex which was manifested by hysterical attention seeking, including the setting of fires. Defendant continued to seek counsel and began seeing a priest. The psychiatrist recommended that she be only counseled by females. After she was sentenced to probation, she began counseling with a female therapist. However she attempted to see the priest and began making phone calls to him. The petition alleged that defendant had violated the terms of her probation by committing three criminal offenses. The trial court found a probation violation in her perpetration of the offense of harassment by telephone. The court reversed and held that not only did the charging instrument fail to set forth a criminal violation, it described behavior which was found unconstitutional to proscribe.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the circuit court that held that defendant had committed the offense of harassment by telephone and that had granted the petition of the state to revoke probation.

 

1456 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Kavinsky


No. 80-5


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


98 Ill. App. 3d 579; 424 N.E.2d 340; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 3034; 53 Ill. Dec. 705



July 16, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. CHARLES R. NORGLE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of armed violence, in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 33A-2 (1977), forcible detention, in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 10-4 (1977), and attempt escape, in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 8-4 (1977), in the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois). The trial court sentenced him to concurrent terms of imprisonment of 15, 7, and 5 years for the respective offenses. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who was in the custody of a county youth home, assaulted an employee of the facility and took him hostage in an attempt to secure his release. He was convicted of multiple offense in connection with the incident. Defendant claimed on appeal, inter alia, that the indictment did not properly charge the offense of forcible detention. The court held that the indictment was fatally defective with respect to the forcible detention charge because it failed to allege that defendant's purpose in taking the employee hostage was to obtain performance by a third person of defendant's demands, which was an essential element of the offense under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 10-4(a). The court determined that the missing language could not be supplied by presumption or necessary implication. The court also found that the forcible detention and attempt escape convictions were lesser included offenses of the armed violence offense and, therefore, that the convictions could not stand. Further, the court determined that defendant waived his remaining claims of error by failing to include them in his post-trial motions and that none of the alleged errors amounted to plain error.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's forcible detention conviction, vacated his attempt escape conviction, and affirmed his armed violence conviction.

People v. Carmickle


No. 79-114


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


97 Ill. App. 3d 917; 424 N.E.2d 78; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 2901; 53 Ill. Dec. 665



July 14, 1981, Filed

DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Peoria County (Illinois), which denied defendant's motion for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of arson and murder and the court vacated the conviction of arson. Defendant then filed a pro se petition for post-conviction relief, and the state's motion to dismiss that petition was granted. The court affirmed defendant's conviction because defendant failed to raise many issues on direct appeal and the post-conviction procedure was not to be used to raise issues that were or could have been raised on direct appeal. Further, defendant's claim of ineffective assistance of counsel was nothing more than an allegation and was insufficient to require or constitute a basis for a hearing on the post-conviction petition.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's murder conviction.

 

1458 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Dugan Oil Co. v. Coalition of Area Labor


Nos. 17010, 17035, 17042, 17043 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


98 Ill. App. 3d 126; 423 N.E.2d 1373; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 2965; 53 Ill. Dec. 569; 113 L.R.R.M. 2436



July 14, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Courts of Morgan, Logan, and Sangamon Counties; the Hon. GORDON D. SEATOR, JOHN T. McCULLOUGH, and SIMON L. FRIEDMAN, Judges, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, picketers and labor coalition, in a consolidated appeal, challenged the orders of the Circuit Courts of Morgan, Logan, and Sangamon Counties (Illinois), which issued preliminary injunctions limiting the picketing in front of businesses owed by appellee service station operators. The coalition claimed that the picketers were engaged in activities protected by the federal and state constitutions.


OVERVIEW: Shell Oil Company hired a South Carolina company that employed nonunion labor from the south rather than union labor from the Springfield area to build a local mine. A community coalition gathered to convince local governmental officials and Shell that workers from outside the Springfield area labor market should not be used to construct the mine. The coalition started a secondary boycott by picketing Shell service stations and blocking entryways, causing irreparable injury and harm to the service station owners. The court affirmed the injunctions against the coalition, finding that secondary boycotts, even though free from violence, may be enjoined where the activity was directed at a neutral employer. The court found that the service station owners possessed a property right in their businesses that needed protection. As a result of the coalition's picketing, irreparable and substantial damage was being inflicted upon the owners by the loss of customers and of good will, which placed the businesses in a financially hazardous position. Because of the uncertainty as to damages and loss of good will, the extraordinary relief in the form of a preliminary injunction was warranted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments granting the preliminary injunctions.

 

1459 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Gardner v. Geraghty


No. 80-1699


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


98 Ill. App. 3d 10; 423 N.E.2d 1321; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 2945; 53 Ill. Dec. 517



July 7, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. JAMES L. GRIFFIN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff administratrix challenged the action of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which entered judgment, upon a jury verdict, for defendant alleged tortfeasor in the administratrix's wrongful death action for the death of her husband.


OVERVIEW: The administratrix brought a wrongful death action on behalf of the estate of her husband, who died as a result of injuries sustained when an automobile driven by the alleged tortfeasor struck him. The trial court dismissed the administratrix's comparative negligence count. A jury found for the alleged tortfeasor on the remaining negligence counts, and the jury returned a special interrogatory finding decedent guilty of contributory negligence. Judgment was entered for the alleged tortfeasor. The administratrix asked the court to consider: (1) whether the lower court erred in dismissing the comparative negligence claim and in submitting to the jury a contributory negligence interrogatory; (2) whether the lower court erred in striking the administratrix's claim for punitive damages; (3) whether the claim for prejudgment interest was properly dismissed; (4) whether testimony regarding decedent's careful habits were properly ruled inadmissible; and (5) whether the lower court properly refused to instruct the jury regarding a pedestrian's right-of-way when in a crosswalk. The court reversed on the fourth and fifth assignment of error, finding that the trial court had ruled incorrectly.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's judgment, which held in favor of the alleged tortfeasor, and remanded the case to it for a new trial. The lower court should have admitted the proffered habit testimony. Also, the administratrix was entitled to a jury instruction regarding decedent's entitlement to a right-of-way if found to be walking within an unmarked crosswalk.

Jenkins v. Bobrowicz


No. 80-723


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


97 Ill. App. 3d 526; 422 N.E.2d 1132; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 2839; 52 Ill. Dec. 923



June 19, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. CARL F. J. HENNINGER, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff motorcyclist appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which, in his suit to recover damages for injuries sustained in a collision with defendant driver's car, ordered a new trial after a verdict was rendered for the motorcyclist on a general verdict. By special interrogatory, the motorcyclist was found to be contributorily negligent. Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 65 (1979) was declared unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The collision occurred at an intersection. The evidence showed that the motorcyclist was on a preferred road, and thus had the right of way, but that he saw the driver's car 150 feet away from the point of impact and did not slow his motorcycle or do anything else to avoid the collision. On appeal, the court ruled that: (1) the trial judge erred in holding that the answer to the special interrogatory was against the manifest weight of the evidence because the jury could have found that the motorcyclist failed to take any reasonable alternative available to avoid the accident; (2) section 65, which provided that when a special finding of fact was inconsistent with the general verdict the former controlled the latter, did not unduly infringe upon the inherent powers of the judiciary, and § 65 was, therefore, constitutional; and (3) because the answer to the special interrogatory was not against the manifest weight of the evidence, and because § 65 was constitutional, the court ordered that a judgment be entered in accord with the special interrogatory, which barred a recovery by the motorcyclist.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the cause with directions that a judgment be entered on the special interrogatory.

 

1461 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Lyden


No. 80-941


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


97 Ill. App. 3d 540; 423 N.E.2d 262; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 2842; 53 Ill. Dec. 70



June 19, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Jo Daviess County; the Hon. ERIC S. DeMAR, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with the offense of driving under the influence of intoxicating liquor. Upon defendant's request, an implied consent hearing was held pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 11 -- 501.1. The Circuit Court of Jo Daviess County (Illinois) entered its judgment that defendant's driver's license would not be suspended, which plaintiff State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State argued that the trial court erred when it decided that defendant's driver's license not be suspended because all four findings made by it during the implied consent hearing were in favor of the State. The State asserted that the trial court was compelled to notify the secretary of state to suspend defendant's driving privileges and that such suspension was mandatory after compliance with the statutory requirements of § 11 -- 501.1. The court held that the dispositive portion of the trial court's notice to the secretary of state was the findings on the issues and not the trial court's "decision" that defendant's license be suspended or not, nor its "recommendation" of a restricted driving permit. The court held that neither the trial court's decision nor its recommendation affected the exclusive statutory authority of the secretary of state in regard to licenses. Anything beyond the trial court's findings on the four issues in the implied consent statute was superfluous and could not be said to have prejudiced the State. Although the court found that the trial court's decision not to suspend was inconsistent with its findings, the inconsistency did not require reversal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1462 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Van Jacobs v. Parikh


No. 80-1648


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


97 Ill. App. 3d 610; 422 N.E.2d 979; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 2852; 52 Ill. Dec. 770



June 10, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. ARTHUR A. SULLIVAN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Third-party plaintiff helmet manufacturer appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) dismissing its third-party complaint for contribution against another defendant, driver of an automobile which struck a motorcycle.


OVERVIEW: After a motorcycle accident, the administrator of the estate of the motorcycle rider brought an action against multiple defendants, including the driver of the vehicle that struck the motorcycle (driver), and the manufacturer. The manufacturer sought contribution from the driver, who had reached a settlement with the administrator. In affirming the dismissal of the manufacturer's complaint for contribution, the court held that the manufacturer failed to allege any pre-tort relationship between it and the driver which gave rise to a duty to indemnify. The allegation that the driver solely and proximately caused decedent's injuries did not support a claim for indemnity, for in the absence of some pre-tort relationship, proof of the allegation would exonerate the manufacturer completely from liability to the deceased's estate, and there would be no need for indemnity. Conclusory allegations that the driver somehow misused the deceased's helmet or that he assumed the risk of the helmet worn by the deceased did not state a cause of action, as the court could not see how one not a user of a product could be deemed to misuse or assume the risks of the product.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the helmet manufacturer's complaint for contribution against the driver of the automobile which struck the motorcycle, who had settled the case brought on behalf of a person injured in the motorcycle accident.

 

1463 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Allen


No. 16407


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


97 Ill. App. 3d 38; 422 N.E.2d 254; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 2756; 52 Ill. Dec. 573



June 9, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County; the Hon. HARVEY BEAM, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his sentencing by the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois) for burglary. Defendant claimed that the trial court applied an aggravating factor not present in the record, improperly considered the fact that he was a public aid recipient, and improperly allowed the payment of court costs and public defender fees to be assessed from defendant's bond deposit.


OVERVIEW: At 4 a.m., a police officer saw defendant's upper body sticking through a bathroom window of a commercial building. Defendant went back inside, and the officer found defendant in the bathroom. Defendant was convicted and sentenced for burglary. On appeal, the court reversed the sentence and remanded for resentencing. The trial court erred in applying the "risk of harm" aggravating factor because the risk of harm was not greater than that inherent in most burglaries. The trial court did not consider public aid as an aggravating factor, but instead referred to defendant's record and propensity to commit crime instead of working in order to obtain a livelihood and indicated that defendant had not made a reasonable effort to be gainfully employed. It was permissible for the trial court to take these factors into consideration. The court erred in imposing a fee for the public defender's services to be withheld from defendant's bond money, but the assessment of costs was proper.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the sentence imposed against defendant by the trial court, and the court remanded for resentencing.

 

1464 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Siefke


No. 80-27


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


97 Ill. App. 3d 14; 421 N.E.2d 1071; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 2752; 52 Ill. Dec. 208



June 5, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. CARL HENNINGER, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which convicted him of rape and sentenced him to 12 years in prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the rape shield statute was an unconstitutional infringement of his Sixth Amendment right to confrontation and that, therefore, the trial court erred in granting the State's in limine motion precluding the introduction of the prosecutrix's reputation for chastity. The court held that in order to have standing to challenge the constitutionality of the statute, defendant had to show either that he was directly affected by the statutory provision or that the unconstitutional feature was so pervasive as to render the entire act invalid. Because defendant made no attempt to introduce evidence of the prosecutrix's reputation for chastity, he could not contend that he was affected by the statutory provision. Further, the rape shield law did not violate his right to due process or deprive him of his right to confrontation. Defendant also argued that it was error to admit testimony at the sentencing hearing of a witness who testified that defendant had attacked her at a particular time and place because the charge had not resulted in a conviction. The court held that such evidence was admissible because defendant was given an opportunity to cross-examine.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and sentence of the trial court.

 

1465 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Szczurek v. Park Ridge


No. 80-1464


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


97 Ill. App. 3d 649; 422 N.E.2d 907; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 2859; 52 Ill. Dec. 698



June 5, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. REGINALD J. HOLZER, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff condominium owner appealed an order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted the motion of defendant city to dismiss the owner's complaint pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 48(1)(i) (1979). The owner sought injunctive relief and compensatory damages for the city's failure to provide garbage removal service to condominium owners when the city provided service to owners of single family homes.


OVERVIEW: The owner asserted that the city's failure to provide the services violated the Due Process Clause and the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment and Ill. Const. art. I, § 2. The trial court agreed with the city that the multiple-dwelling ownership from in the Park Ridge, Ill., Council Policy Statement No. 5, which clarified Park Ridge, Ill., Ordinance 14-4-6, was not a suspect classification, and that the city had a rational basis for distinguishing between the refuse needs of the two groups. The dwellers in multifamily units had greater bargaining power than persons who owned a single family home. On appeal, the city asserted that the owner's claims were moot because the city had amended the challenged code sections. The court held that the owner's complaint for injunctive relief was moot, but that her claims for damages were not. The rational basis for the classification of owners of multifamily units was sufficient for grounds for dismissal of the owner's complaint under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 48(1)(i). Park Ridge, Ill., Council Policy Statement No. 5 was entitled to a presumption of validity because it did not modify existing ordinances.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order that granted the city's motion to dismiss the owner's complaint for an injunction that required the city to provide garbage removal service to condominium owners and to recompense condominium owners for additional money spent on the services that were provided to owners of single family homes.

 

1466 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Stiles


No. 79-662


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


95 Ill. App. 3d 959; 420 N.E.2d 1204; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 2548; 51 Ill. Dec. 646



May 29, 1981, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 29, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. BRUCE R. FAWELL, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment vacated and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the orders of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which convicted her of armed robbery after a bench trial. The trial court refused to hold an evidentiary hearing on defendant's motion to quash arrest and to suppress evidence because defendant had previously litigated the same motion in a separate robbery trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged in two armed robberies in different counties and gave a statement that included both offenses. Defense counsel filed a motion to quash arrest and to suppress evidence in the first county, but did not have the arresting officers present and did not avail himself of a continuance offered by the trial court. Defendant later pleaded guilty. On this appeal of the second conviction, the court noted that the doctrine of collateral estoppel was of limited utility in criminal cases because defendants did not have an immediate right to appeal pretrial rulings and could be cut off from appellate review by an acquittal or a guilty plea. The court held that the lack of review brought the case under an exception to the doctrine that barred relitigation of the same motion. The court also found that testimony of the arresting officers was "available" at the first hearing, but that defendant's counsel was ineffective. The court held that the lack of a full and fair hearing on the motion and the lack of effective assistance of counsel violated defendant's fundamental rights and were "exceptional circumstances" that allowed her to relitigate the motion.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment of conviction and sentence and remanded with directions that the trial court conduct an evidentiary hearing of defendant's motion to quash arrest and suppress evidence. The court instructed that if that motion was denied, the trial court would reinstate the judgment and sentence, but if it was granted, the trial court would give defendant a new trial.

 

1467 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Clark


No. 80-543


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


96 Ill. App. 3d 491; 421 N.E.2d 590; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 2655; 51 Ill. Dec. 955



May 28, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Warren County; the Hon. U. S. COLLINS, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Warren County (Illinois), which convicted her of the unlawful delivery of a controlled substance, 3,4-methylenedioxyamphetamine (MDA).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of the unlawful delivery of a controlled substance MDA. The trial was conducted in the defendant's absence pursuant to § 115-4.1(a) of the Code of Criminal Procedure of 1963, Ill. Rev. Stat. 1979, ch. 38, para. 115- 4.1(a) (1979). Defendant asserted that the trial court erred in permitting an amendment to the information. The court concluded that the amendment to the information was permissible because it corrected a mere formal defect. The court also rejected defendant's challenged to the constitutionality of § 115-4.1(a), which permitted her trial in absentia because of her wilful avoidance of trial. The court held that there was no constitutional prohibition against trying a defendant in absentia after the defendant voluntarily absented herself form the trial. Further, defendant failed to show that any of her constitutional rights were violated in her absence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Brodner v. Elgin


No. 80-694


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


96 Ill. App. 3d 224; 420 N.E.2d 1176; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 2614; 51 Ill. Dec. 618



May 12, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Kane County; the Hon. JOHN A. KRAUSE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners appealed the judgment and order of the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois) which dismissed with prejudice for failure to state a cause of action and failure to exhaust their administrative remedies, the property owners' declaratory judgment action against defendant city and its rezoning of their property.


OVERVIEW: The city filed applications to rezone parcels of real estate. The city did not obtain written consent of the owners when it filed applications to rezone the property. The city's land use committee held public hearings to consider the applications. The land use committee recommended denial of the city's applications. However, the city council approved the applications. The owners of seven of the parcels sought declaratory relief, contending that the city had no authority to accept an application to rezone property without their written consent and that therefore they had been denied due process by the subsequent rezoning. The trial court dismissed the complaint. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the consent requirement constituted an unlawful delegation of the city's rezoning power. The court also held that judicial relief from an unlawful zoning ordinance was appropriate only after the property owners had exhausted the available local remedies, which they had failed to do. If the rezoning was erroneous the local authorities should have had an opportunity to correct their mistake and reconsider the ordinance as applied to each of the parcels at issue.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed judgment in favor of the city.

Thompson v. Cook County Zoning Bd. of Appeals


No. 80-190


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


96 Ill. App. 3d 561; 421 N.E.2d 285; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 2667; 51 Ill. Dec. 777



May 12, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. JAMES MURRAY, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff homeowners appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which found for defendants, county, county commissioners, and zoning appeals board (county). The homeowners sought an injunction restraining the county from amending the official county maps and records and from issuing any building permits for construction of a proposed planned unit development.


OVERVIEW: The homeowners challenged the validity of an amended zoning ordinance and special use granted by the county and sought an injunction against a proposed planned unit development. The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment for the county and held that that there were no deficiencies in the process of the zoning amendment. In their effort to overturn the amendment, the homeowners did not satisfy their burden of proving by clear and convincing evidence that the ordinance bore no substantial relation to the public welfare. The court held that the requirements of Cook County, Ill., Zoning Ordinance § 13.15 were not met because the homeowners failed to show that they owned the requisite percentage of frontage, and, therefore, a three-quarters vote of the county commissioners was not necessary. Because the zoning board did not make a recommendation either way, only a simple majority of the county commissioners was needed to pass the amendment. The notice of the hearing was timely. The court affirmed the decision after considering five factors in determining the validity of an amended ordinance. The homeowners had no absolute right in the continuation of the zoning classification.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court, which found for the county in the homeowners' action for an injunction restraining the county from amending the official county maps and records and from allowing a proposed planned unit development.

People v. Kloiber


No. 80-282


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


95 Ill. App. 3d 1061; 420 N.E.2d 870; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 2561; 51 Ill. Dec. 456



May 11, 1981, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Rock Island County; the Hon. DAVID DeDONCKER, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Rock Island County (Illinois), which convicted him of murder and armed robbery following a jury trial. Defendant was sentenced for a term of natural life on his murder conviction. No sentence was imposed following his armed robbery conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant raised several issues on appeal including that the trial court erred in refusing to give an accomplice instruction tendered by defense counsel, that he should be granted a new trial because his attorney formerly had represented a state's witness, that the prosecutor made improper remarks and that his sentence was unconstitutional. The court ruled that defendant properly was convicted of the crimes. The court found that the accomplice instruction was correctly refused by the trial court because the evidence established that the person at issue was an accessory after the fact who did not aid the defendant in the murder or robbery of the victim. The court also found that no new trial was required because the public defender had terminated his representation of the state's witness prior to trial and there was no conflict of interest. The court also ruled that the prosecutor's remarks were proper and that the sentence imposed was constitutional and did not constitute an abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence for murder and armed robbery were affirmed.

 

1471 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Bowman


No. 79-205


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


96 Ill. App. 3d 136; 420 N.E.2d 1132; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 2600; 51 Ill. Dec. 574



May 6, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County; the Hon. STEPHEN M. KERNAN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois) entered a judgment that convicted defendant of kidnaping and unlawful restraint. Defendant was sentenced to an extended term of imprisonment of 14 years on the kidnaping offense. No judgment was entered on the unlawful restraint conviction. Defendant sought review.


OVERVIEW: After she was abducted at knifepoint, the victim escaped and later identified defendant as her attacker from a photographic array. The victim also identified defendant at a lineup on the basis of his appearance and high-pitched voice. When his guilty plea was vacated, defendant petitioned for discharge based on an alleged violation of his statutory right to a speedy trial within 120 days. The petition was denied. The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence, holding that defendant's right to a speedy trial was not denied because his plea of guilty operated to toll the running of the 120-day rule during the period that elapsed between the entry of such plea and the order vacating it. Next, the court held that defendant was not denied effective assistance of counsel where defense counsel's law partner was a former assistant State's Attorney who participated in the preliminary stages of the prosecution. Defendant had knowingly and intelligently waived any conflict of interest. Furthermore, given the victim's unequivocal in-court identification and corroborating testimony, the admission of prior consistent statements to bolster the victim's identification was harmless error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that convicted defendant of kidnaping and unlawful restraint and sentenced him to an extended term of imprisonment of 14 years on the kidnaping offense.

La Salle Nat'l Bank v. Brookfield


No. 80-156


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


95 Ill. App. 3d 765; 420 N.E.2d 819; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 2521; 51 Ill. Dec. 405



May 1, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. GEORGE J. SCHALLER, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant village sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which found Village of Brookfield, Ill. Book of Ordinances of the Village of Brookfield ch.28, art. IV, § 28-41 (1979) as an enactment beyond the village's legislative grant of powers. Appellee property owner had challenged § 28-41 when it was required to post a deposit in exchange for a building permit.


OVERVIEW: The property owner successfully challenged the village's reversal of the village zoning board's approval of its petition to rezone its property to allow for development of mixed residential and commercial uses. The property owner then successfully challenged the validity of § 28-41, which required it to post a deposit for the costs of certain improvements before the issuance of a building permit to allow it to make connections to the sanitary sewer system. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. Section 28-41 was invalid because in its enactment, the village had exceeded its grant of power by the Legislature. Section 28-41 was not in compliance with Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24, para. 11-12-8 (1979), which required the approval of the plat of the property involved before requiring the posting of a performance bond or deposit to ensure the completion of improvements to the property. The disputed ordinance was silent as to approval of a plat upon payment of a bond or deposit. The village failed to show that it acted under implied authority because the disputed ordinance was not essential or reasonably necessary to its implementation of its statutory authority.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court in its determination that the village ordinance was unconstitutional.

 

1473 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Power v. One 1979 Chevrolet Camaro


No. 80-518


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


96 Ill. App. 3d 109; 420 N.E.2d 770; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 2596; 51 Ill. Dec. 356



April 30, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Kankakee County; the Hon. JOHN F. MICHELA, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee State's attorney brought a forfeiture action in the Circuit Court of Kankakee County (Illinois) against appellants, the vehicle owner and the vehicle, under the Illinois Forfeiture Act (Forfeiture Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 36-1 (1979). Appellants challenged the judgment that ordered the vehicle forfeited, claiming that § 409 of the Illinois Controlled Substances Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1409 (1979), was a bar.


OVERVIEW: Indicted by state and federal authorities on drug charges, the owner pleaded guilty to the federal charge. He claimed on appeal of the instant forfeiture action that it imposed another penalty, in addition to the federal one, so that it was barred by § 409 of the Controlled Substances Act. Section 409 prohibited a prosecution on a controlled substance charge in Illinois after a conviction or acquittal in a federal or other state court on a charge that was based on the same acts. The court, however, ruled that the forfeiture action was not barred by § 409. The prosecution contemplated by § 409 was strictly a criminal one, while the forfeiture action was a civil, in rem proceeding. The forfeiture proceeding did not determine the owner's guilt or innocence but only whether the vehicle had been used in the commission of the offense. Thus, although the same criminal acts to which the owner had pleaded guilty formed a connecting link between the vehicle and the forfeiture proceeding, the prohibition of § 409 did not affect the forfeiture proceeding under the Forfeiture Act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court that ordered the vehicle forfeited.

Mississippi Bluff Motel, Inc. v. County of Rock Island

Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 26.1 (1979).

People v. Powell


No. 16429


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


95 Ill. App. 3d 93; 419 N.E.2d 708; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 2414; 50 Ill. Dec. 600



April 9, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County; the Hon. JAMES T. LONDRIGAN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois), which entered judgment on a jury verdict that found defendant and his co-defendant guilty of burglary in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 19-1 (1979), and which sentenced him to imprisonment for a term of six years.


OVERVIEW: At the time he was arraigned on his burglary charges, he was admonished by the circuit court, pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 113-4(d), of the possibility of a trial in his absence. Defendant was not present at the time his trial commenced, and it proceeded in his absence pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 115-4.1 (1979). The circuit court entered judgment on the jury's guilty verdict, and sentenced him to six years imprisonment. In affirming the judgment the court held that § 115-4.1 was neither facially unconstitutional, nor unconstitutional as applied to him. The court held that the statute and decisional law provided that his voluntary absence constituted a waiver of his right to be present during the trial. Further, the statute was not unconstitutional as applied because the circuit court's admonition was sufficient; the record did not have to reflect a positive statement that he understood the admonition. Additionally the State proved that his absence was a result of his efforts to avoid trial. The court upheld the denial of defendant's motion for severance because it was untimely and he did not make a sufficient showing of antagonism of the defenses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

People v. March


No. 15490


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


95 Ill. App. 3d 46; 419 N.E.2d 1212; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 2408; 50 Ill. Dec. 763; 7 Media L. Rep. 1465



April 7, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Vermilion County; the Hon. RALPH S. PEARMAN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his murder conviction after a jury verdict in the Circuit Court of Vermilion County (Illinois).


OVERVIEW: A shoot-out between defendant and a bouncer at a nightclub resulted in the bouncer's death. The court reversed defendant's murder conviction, holding that: (1) the trial court's closing the courtroom to the press during two offers of proof heard outside the presence of the jury violated defendant's right to a public trial, and that the press, as a surrogate for the public, had a First Amendment right to be present absent an overriding interest articulated by the trial court; (2) while the state introduced sufficient evidence to support the jury's tacit finding that defendant was not acting in self-defense, and while the jury was properly instructed that the state had the burden of negating a self-defense claim beyond a reasonable doubt, the trial court erred in refusing defendant's tendered instruction on voluntary manslaughter because there was evidence of serious provocation, specifically that defendant and the bouncer engaged in a quarrel and that the bouncer drew his gun first; and (3) the trial court was not required to instruct the jury that the state had to negate the elements of voluntary manslaughter beyond a reasonable doubt before defendant could be convicted of murder.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's murder conviction and remanded the matter for a new trial.

McAleer Buick-Pontiac Co. v. General Motors Corp.


No. 16855


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


95 Ill. App. 3d 111; 419 N.E.2d 608; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 2418; 50 Ill. Dec. 500



April 2, 1981, Filed

DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant manufacturer challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Vermilion County (Illinois) that granted plaintiff dealer an injunction prohibiting the manufacturer from terminating the parties' contract.


OVERVIEW: A dealer and a manufacturer entered into a contract where the dealer sold the manufacturer's cars. While the contract was renewed on several occasions, the manufacturer gave notice to the dealer that it would not renew the contract when it expired. The dealer sought and received an injunction from the trial court, with the trial court finding that the manufacturer could not terminate the contract absent a showing of good cause. The manufacturer appealed. On review, the court found that the good cause requirement only existed in Ill. Rev. Further, there was no language in the act that indicated that it should be given retroactive application. Thus, the manufacturer did not have to have good cause to terminate the contract with the dealer.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court, finding that good cause was not required to terminate the contract.

 

1481 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Townes


No. 16409


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


94 Ill. App. 3d 850; 419 N.E.2d 604; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 2357; 50 Ill. Dec. 496



March 31, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Vermilion County; the Hon. PAUL M. WRIGHT, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Vermilion County (Illinois), which convicted him of rape, sexual assault, and home invasion pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, pars. 1-1, 11-3, 12-11 (1979). Defendant's main contention on appeal was that his early admissions to the police officers should have been suppressed on the ground that he was illegally detained by the police in violation of his Fourth Amendment rights.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was told to go to the police station to be interviewed regarding a rape but the police had no probable cause to arrest or detain him. His only connection with the crime was that he fit a general description given by the victim. The officers testified that they had no intention to arrest defendant, yet they detained him for over 12 hours and subjected him to 5 separate interrogations until sufficient incriminating statements were obtained to serve as a predicate for his arrest. During his police detention, defendant was never told that he was not under arrest or that he was free to go. On appeal, the court explained that while the latter facts were not controlling, they were significant factors in the totality of the circumstances that caused the court to conclude that defendant was illegally seized in violation of the Fourth Amendment. That fact that defendant received Miranda warnings was insufficient to attenuate the taint of his unlawful seizure and validate his subsequent admissions. Thus, the court held that the trial court erred in not suppressing defendant's admissions and that the error was sufficiently grave as to require a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the cause for a new trial.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant taxi company filed an interlocutory appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied the taxi company's motion to dismiss a wrongful death action filed by plaintiff, the administrator of the estate of the deceased.


OVERVIEW: The administrator brought a wrongful death action against the taxi company, under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 70, para. 1 et seq. (1979), sounding in negligence. The administrator alleged that the deceased had leased a taxicab from the taxi company and was killed during the operation of that cab when one or two passengers shot him. The administrator claimed that the taxi company was negligent to provide a taxicab that did not have a bulletproof shield between the passengers and the driver. 1483 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


In re Marriage of Galvin


No. 80-1105


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


94 Ill. App. 3d 1032; 419 N.E.2d 417; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 2383; 50 Ill. Dec. 309



March 25, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. RENE GOIER, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After respondent client discharged his attorneys from representing him in an action for the dissolution of his marriage, petitioner firm filed a request in the matrimonial action for an award of attorney fees. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) awarded fees to the firm. The client appealed.


OVERVIEW: The client contended that § 508(a) of the Illinois Marriage and Dissolution of Marriage Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 508(a) (1977), was constitutionally prohibited special legislation. Section 508(a) of the Act authorized a trial court to adjudicate, incident to a pending dissolution proceeding, the liability of either spouse for the costs and attorney fees necessarily incurred by the other spouse as well as for his or her own costs and attorney fees. The court held that § 508(a) was not prohibited special legislation and that the trial court properly entered judgment for the firm against its own client. The court held that § 508(a) affected all members of the same class alike. Further, a unique function of the trial court in dissolution proceedings was to make divisions and allocations of property, enter orders of support, and determine whether one spouse should pay the other spouse's attorney fees. It was reasonable for the legislature to have provided that the same court determine fee disputes between attorney and client. Finally, it was clear from the statutory language that § 508(a) permitted an adversarial fee action between attorney and client.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court.

Ray v. Department of Registration & Education


No. 80-1022


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


94 Ill. App. 3d 1123; 419 N.E.2d 413; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 2396; 50 Ill. Dec. 305



March 25, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. ARTHUR L. DUNNE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff veterinarian appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which suspended his veterinary license in a case involving the veterinarian's administrative appeal against defendant Department of Registration and Education (department). The trial court affirmed the order of the director of the executive committee (director) for the department suspending the veterinarian's license for six months.


OVERVIEW: The department charged the veterinarian with violating the Veterinary Medicine and Surgery Practice Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111, para. 6901 et seq. (1977), and alleged that he committed gross malpractice and failed to keep his home, where he took care of animals, in a sanitary condition. After a hearing, the executive committee for the department recommended that the veterinarian be suspended for six months and the director adopted the recommendation. The veterinarian appealed to the trial court, which affirmed the director's ruling. On appeal, the court affirmed the order of the trial court and held that the finding that the veterinarian had violated the Act was supported by the evidence. The court ruled that the testimony at the hearing showed that the veterinarian committed several acts of gross malpractice and also conducted his business out of his home, which was in very unsanitary. The court rejected the veterinarian's claim that the Act's standards of "gross malpractice" and "unsanitary conditions" were unconstitutionally vague and held that the terms were definite enough to provide him with a guide as to how to conduct himself.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court suspending the veterinarian's license for six months.

 

1485 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Illinois Bell Tel. Co. v. Allphin


No. 79-1869


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


95 Ill. App. 3d 115; 419 N.E.2d 1188; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 2419; 50 Ill. Dec. 739



March 25, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. EARL J. ARKISS, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff telephone company challenged that part of an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which directed it to pay $ 115 million in back taxes under the Messages Tax Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 467.1 et seq., (1979). Defendant Director of the Department of Revenue (Department) challenged that part of the order that enjoined it from taking action to collect an additional $ 13 million it claimed was due.


OVERVIEW: The telephone company sought a declaration that it did not owe back taxes, penalties, and interest assessed by the Department. Both parties sought review when the trial court held that the Act exempted revenues from the transmission of interstate messages, but had expanded, sub silentio, to impose the tax on revenues from interstate messages. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court held that the Act did not impose a tax on receipts from the transmission of interstate messages, and that it made no distinction between those taxpayers which operated entirely in Illinois and those which also had facilities or activities located outside Illinois. The court ruled that the Department's assessment of a tax on that portion of the telephone company's revenue derived from the relaying of interstate messages was an improper retroactive application of new regulations dealing with the Act. The court held that the trial court erred in directing the telephone company to pay the back taxes, penalties and interest, but that it properly enjoined the collection of the additional taxes claimed by the Department.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court directing the telephone company to pay $ 115 million to the Department in back taxes, penalties, and interest. The court affirmed the order permanently enjoining the Department from taking any action to collect additional assessed tax liabilities against the telephone company.

 

1486 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Brown


No. 79-1789


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


94 Ill. App. 3d 609; 418 N.E.2d 1093; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 2317; 50 Ill. Dec. 99



March 24, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. WILLIAM COUSINS, JR., Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed a murder indictment for a violation of defendant's right to a speedy trial.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court noted that defendant had been charged with two murders and a robbery and that defendant was in custody on three charges when his bond in the first murder case was revoked. Thus, a 160-day term for bringing him to trial under the speedy trial statute commenced with the judgment entered on his plea of guilty to the robbery charge the next day, even though the bond on that charge was not revoked prior to his guilty plea. Also, the 160-day term for bringing defendant to trial was renewed by his agreed continuance, in a case arising prior to March 1, 1977. In addition, a timely commencement of trial on one of the murder charges after entry of judgment in the robbery case did not excuse the State from bringing defendant to trial on the other murder charge within the same 160-day period. Further, the court held that a tolling of the statutory period for interlocutory appeal applied only when the appeal was taken in the cause which was otherwise subject to dismissal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1487 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Marynczak v. D & L Transport Co.


No. 79-2405


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


94 Ill. App. 3d 381; 418 N.E.2d 972; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 2288; 49 Ill. Dec. 952



March 19, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. JOSEPH GORDON, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured driver appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which was entered on a general verdict in favor of defendant stalled driver and defendant truck driver on the injured driver's claims for personal injury damages.


OVERVIEW: The injured driver suffered personal injuries when his car was struck from behind by the truck driver's truck. The injured driver, who claimed that he was struck after he stopped in the center land of a highway to assist the stalled driver, whose car had broken down in that lane, filed an action for damages against the truck driver, his employer, and the stalled driver. The truck driver, stalled driver, and another witness testified that the injured driver was struck after he swerved in front of the truck driver, who was in the process of stopping in order not to strike the stalled driver's car. The court affirmed the judgment in favor of all defendants. The trial judge had the inherent judicial power to give the jury a special interrogatory on contributory negligence, which the jury answered in the affirmative, and its use of the interrogatory was not unconstitutional. The general verdict and the answer to the special interrogatory were not contrary to the manifest weight of the evidence. The trial court did not err in refusing to give an instruction regarding negligence of the stalled driver because the instruction misstated the law or was not warranted by the evidence.


OUTCOME: The judgment for the stalled driver and the truck driver on the injured driver's claims for personal injury damages was affirmed.

 

1488 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Darnell


No. 80-170


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


94 Ill. App. 3d 830; 419 N.E.2d 384; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 2354; 50 Ill. Dec. 276



March 18, 1981, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 8, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Henry County; the Hon. ROBERT J. HORBERG, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Henry County, (Illinois), which convicted him following a bench trial of rape and murder. A sentence of life imprisonment was imposed for the murder and a concurrent sentence of 30 years' imprisonment was imposed for the rape conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was 16 years old at the time of the offenses. Promising his 10-year-old victim a horse, defendant lured her to the site of a previously prepared grave where he raped her. He then strangled her from behind with his bandana. He put her body in the grave and covered it with dirt. Defendant later confessed to the crime and claimed that he was insane. A pathologist testified that rape could not be ruled out on the basis of his findings. The court upheld the convictions and sentences. The court rejected defendant's argument that he was not proven guilty of rape beyond a reasonable doubt because the only evidence tending to show that a rape occurred was defendant's confession. The court held that direct and positive evidence was unnecessary to prove the corpus delicti and it was sufficient if other evidence so corroborated the confession or admission as to show the commission of the offense beyond a reasonable doubt. Here, photographic evidence tended to corroborate the confession. Further, the trial court did not err in imposing a life sentence on the ground that the murder was accompanied by exceptionally brutal or heinous behavior indicative of wanton cruelty.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions and sentences imposed by the circuit court.

People v. Childers


No. 79-161


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


94 Ill. App. 3d 104; 418 N.E.2d 959; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 2244; 49 Ill. Dec. 939



March 18, 1981, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 22, 1981.
Writ of certiorari denied Childers v. Illinois, 455 U.S. 947, 102 S. Ct. 1448, 71 L. Ed. 2d 661, 1982 U.S. LEXIS 924 (1982)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Childers v. Cowan, 343 Ill. App. 3d 1306, 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 7267 (Ill. App. Ct. 3d Dist., 2003)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Petition denied by People v. Childers, 207 Ill. 2d 609, 807 N.E.2d 977, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 341, 283 Ill. Dec. 136 (2004)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at People v. Childers, 2015 IL App (3d) 130647-U, 2015 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1666 (2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Tazewell County; the Hon. JAMES HEIPLE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Tazewell County (Illinois), which convicted him of murder and sentenced him to three concurrent terms of imprisonment for his natural life.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued, inter alia, that: (1) the trial court's order directing disclosure of the state psychiatrist's report was beyond the scope of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110A, para. 413(d) (1979); (2) his statements were involuntary; (3) insufficient time elapsed from his demand for an attorney to permit a waiver; and (4) the trial court erred in denying his application for the divestiture of a news reporter's privilege. The appellate court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The report, while adverse to defendant, did not deny him any privilege against self-incrimination. Defendant volunteered himself into the station house and deceitfully bent every effort to mislead the police. There was no indication in the record that the police were doing anything other than attempting to protect defendant until the officer shortly after noontime had the opportunity to review the statement of the neighbor. It was then that defendant's duplicity began to emerge and adequate probable cause to detain him arose. As for the reporter's privilege, other sources not only were available to defendant, but it was difficult to perceive what public interest might have been involved.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court convicting defendant of murder and sentencing him to life imprisonment was affirmed.
