Queenwood East Sheltered Care Home, Ltd. v. Morton


No. 80-92


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


94 Ill. App. 3d 51; 418 N.E.2d 472; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 2234; 49 Ill. Dec. 618



March 17, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Tazewell County; the Hon. JAMES D. HEIPLE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant village appealed from the Circuit Court of Tazewell County (Illinois), which held that an ordinance adopted by its board of trustees was void as beyond its regulatory power. Plaintiff sheltered care home sought a declaratory judgment that the ordinance was void because it was beyond the police power of the village or because certain provisions offended against the due process provisions of the Illinois and United States constitutions.


OVERVIEW: The village relied on Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24, para. 11--11--1 (1979) as the source of its power to enact the ordinance which sought to regulate and prohibit false fire alarms. The sheltered care home had installed a fire detection system that was connected to the fire station in the village. Prior to the date of the enactment of the ordinance, the system began to trigger numerous false alarms to which the fire department responded. The court noted that no express power to require fire detection devices was found. The court held that § 11--1--1 conferred no substantive powers, but was an implementing grant which permitted the enactment of ordinances to carry out powers elsewhere conferred. The court held that if the village had required the installation of fire detection devices, the regulatory ordinance would have flowed naturally from § 11--11--1. The court held that there was no ordinance requiring installation, only an ordinance purporting to regulate something not required. The court found that the power to regulate existed only when the object of regulation was mandated by a specific ordinance and that the circuit court was correct in finding that the ordinance was void.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part the judgment of the circuit court. The court held that the power to regulate existed only when the object of regulation was mandated by a specific ordinance and that the ordinance was beyond the power of the village and hence void. The court held that the judgment of the circuit court in favor of the village on the constitutional issues was reversed.

 

1491 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Dobbs v. Chase


No. 79-452


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


94 Ill. App. 3d 177; 418 N.E.2d 919; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 2258; 49 Ill. Dec. 899



March 16, 1981, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 20, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Jackson County; the Hon. ALBERT W. McCALLISTER, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff payors sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Jackson County (Illinois), which granted the motion of defendants', judge and circuit clerks, to dismiss the payors' complaint that sought to maintain a class action for declaration that a circuit rule was invalid in requiring payment of jury fees in civil actions other than small claims.


OVERVIEW: The payors alleged that they and members of the class that sought to be certified had been improperly required to pay jury fees, pursuant to an administrative circuit rule. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment. Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 25, para. 27.1(v) (1979) provided that a circuit court could set only fees not covered by the section. The court held that the payors' request for a declaratory judgment that the circuit rule was invalid and for an injunction against assessment of jury fees under the rule had been rendered moot by the enactment of the statutory provision for jury fees set forth in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 25, para. 27.1(d)(5) (1979). The court held that the payors did not provide the trial court with any basis for concluding that the class was so numerous that joinder was impracticable because the payors merely alleged this in a conclusory fashion and did not support this conclusion. Thus, the trial court properly held that the action could not be maintained as a class action. The payors' failure to allege the county or counties where they allegedly were required to pay jury fees resulted in a failure to state a cause of action against the circuit clerks.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which granted defendants' motion to dismiss the payors' complaint that sought to maintain a class action for a declaration that a circuit rule was invalid in requiring payment of jury fees in civil actions other than small claims.

 

1492 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Baldasar


No. 76-535


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


93 Ill. App. 3d 168; 418 N.E.2d 443; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 2085; 49 Ill. Dec. 589



March 12, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. ALFRED E. WOODWARD, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The United States Supreme Court reversed defendant's conviction and sentence and remanded to the court. Although unable to agree on a majority opinion, five members of the Supreme Court held that a prior uncounseled misdemeanor conviction could not be used collaterally to impose an increased term of imprisonment, or an enhanced penalty, upon conviction for a subsequent offense.


OVERVIEW: The Supreme Court had called into question the constitutionality of an enhancement provision of the theft statute, under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 16-1(e)(1) (1975), which provided that a second or subsequent conviction for theft of property not exceeding $ 150 in value was punishable as a Class 4 felony. The court found that the provision was unconstitutional as applied to defendant but was not unconstitutional on its face. Although the court found that the prior uncounseled misdemeanor conviction with no imprisonment was not violative of the Constitution, it was the subsequent use of the evidence of the conviction to enhance a misdemeanor to a felony that was unconstitutional. However, it was not sufficient to reduce the felony conviction to a misdemeanor in order to cure the constitutional infirmity because there remained no valid evidentiary purpose to balance against the obvious prejudice to defendant when the jury heard it. The admission of the prior conviction for the sole purpose to invoke an enhanced penalty was constitutionally impermissible and was reversible error.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for a new trial.

 

1493 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Williams


No. 79-723


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


94 Ill. App. 3d 241; 418 N.E.2d 840; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 2267; 49 Ill. Dec. 820



March 12, 1981, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 9, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. FRANCIS J. MAHON, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of a decision by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which rendered judgment on a jury verdict finding defendants guilty on the initial charges of rape, and the new charges of kidnapping and battery. Defendants were subsequently sentenced to concurrent terms of imprisonment for the rape charges and the kidnapping charges.


OVERVIEW: On the 120th day after defendants' arrest, the state filed nine additional charges against defendants which arose from the same incident as the initial charges. Defendants' public defenders subsequently requested a continuance to prepare their defense and trial was set for a month later. Defendants were found guilty on the initial charges and some of the new charges. Defendants appealed their convictions contending inter alia that they were denied their right to a speedy trial and that they were denied effective assistance of counsel. The court reversed the conviction on the new charges and affirmed the remaining convictions. The court held that: (1) defendants were tried on the new charges after the permissible 120 day term had expired and the state was responsible for the delay because their late filing caused defendants to request a continuance; and (2) defendants waived the issue whether they were denied effective assistance of counsel on grounds that their defenses were antagonistic because defendants did not raise the issue during trial or in their post-trial motions, and furthermore there was no actual conflict where neither defendant attempted to implicate the other.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the convictions arising from the new charges of kidnapping and battery, remanded to the trial court with directions to vacate those judgments, and affirmed the remaining convictions against defendants for rape.

People v. Smith


No. 80-194


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


93 Ill. App. 3d 1133; 418 N.E.2d 172; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 2227; 49 Ill. Dec. 528



March 10, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. FRANK W. BARBARO, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of murder, armed robbery, and armed violence. Defendant contended, in part, that: 1) his motion to suppress was erroneously denied; 2) his right against self-incrimination was violated; and 3) § 5-5-3.2(b)(2) of the Unified Code of Corrections, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-5-3.2(b)(2) (1978 Supp.), was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Police arrested defendant and two companions for the murder of a man. Defendant had been in police custody for 9 1/2 hours at the time he made a statement regarding his involvement with the murder. Defendant alleged that he had been mistreated while in custody, but police testimony controverted his claim. Defendant suggested that such testimony was not credible due to conflicts within police testimony as to other issues. At trial, an officer testified that defendant had made an oral statement, but that he had refused to reduce it to writing. The court affirmed the judgment of conviction. The court held, in part, that: 1) defendant's statement was not the result of physical or psychological coercion and was not against the manifest weight of the evidence and therefore his motion to suppress was not erroneously denied; 2) defendant's right against self-incrimination was not violated when the officer referenced his refusal to sign a statement and any error was cured when the trial court instructed the jury to disregard the officer's statement; and 3) defendant waived his right to challenge the constitutionality of § 5-5-3.2(b)(2) when he failed to raise the issue at trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which convicted defendant of murder, armed robbery, and armed violence.

Miller v. Illinois Dep't of Public Aid


No. 80-2243


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


94 Ill. App. 3d 11; 418 N.E.2d 178; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 2231; 49 Ill. Dec. 534



March 10, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. JOSEPH M. WOSIK, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a class action brought in the name of plaintiff recipient of general assistance (GA) (recipient) under article VI of the Illinois Public Aid Code (code), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 23, para. 1-1 et seq. (1979), defendant Illinois Department of Public Aid (IDPA) appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which, inter alia, enjoined the IDPA from further denial of payment for dental and optical care.


OVERVIEW: For budgetary reasons, the IDPA discontinued payment for dental and optical services to GA recipients. The trial court held that the IDPA had violated its duties under the code, but on appeal, the court reversed. The court reviewed the history of the code, and held that the code set forth a flexible public assistance scheme and granted the IDPA broad discretion to allocate scarce resources. The court noted, for example, that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 23, para. 108 (1965) and Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 23, para. 6-2 (1979) utilized the word "may" in delineating the parameters of the GA program. The recipient argued that the use of the mandatory "shall" in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 23, para. 6-1 (1965) required that all medical needs of recipients be provided through the program, but the court held that, construing the section consistently with the rest of the statute, para. 6-1 mandated only that those persons meeting the tests for GA eligibility set forth elsewhere receive such aid as the statute otherwise provided. Finally, the court held that the IDPA's construction of the statute did not violate equal protection by providing some types of medical services and not others.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court, which enjoined the IDPA from denying payment for dental and optical care, dissolved the injunction, and entered summary judgment for the IDPA.

People v. Stocks


No. 80-204


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


93 Ill. App. 3d 439; 417 N.E.2d 1080; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 2124; 49 Ill. Dec. 253



February 26, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Williamson County; the Hon. WILLIAM A. LEWIS, Judge, presiding.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of Williamson County (Illinois), which sentenced him to 20 years in the department of corrections after a jury convicted him of the murder of his father. The juvenile court had granted the motion of the state's attorney and transferred the minor defendant for trial in the circuit court pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, para. 702-7 (1977).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was taken into custody after he killed his father with a shotgun. The minor defendant told the police that he had accidentally shot his father. The juvenile court held a transfer hearing and determined that defendant was to be prosecuted as a defendant in the circuit court. After an indictment and jury trial, defendant was convicted of murder. On appeal, the court affirmed the transfer and the conviction. There was evidence on the record in front of the juvenile court that the alleged offense was premeditated, defendant had previous violent behavior, he was almost 17, and security of the public required continued custody and supervision. The juvenile court held a hearing that provided due process of law. No abuse of discretion was shown. The court also affirmed the conviction for murder. The pictures allowed into the record were not objectionable and were admitted within the circuit court's discretion. The jury was able to infer that defendant knew his action was likely to cause serious injury or death.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the juvenile court's transfer of defendant for trial under the criminal laws and his conviction in the circuit court for the murder of his father.

Springfield v. Hall


No. 16468


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


93 Ill. App. 3d 860; 417 N.E.2d 1059; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 2187; 49 Ill. Dec. 232



February 24, 1981, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 31, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County; the Hon. JOHN B. CRAIN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois), which entered a judgment of conviction for operating a movie theater without a license, a violation of the Springfield City Code, § 42A.2, and fined $ 25. The trial judge did not expressly declare unconstitutional any portion of the theater license ordinance but ruled that severability saved the licensing requirement.


OVERVIEW: Although defendant did not apply for a theater license, he had standing to challenge his conviction because the ordinance was unconstitutional on its face. On appeal, defendant argued that the city's theater license ordinance, Springfield City Code ch. 42A, was unconstitutional. The city conceded the unconstitutionality of certain sections in the ordinance but believed that they were severable and that the licensing section was valid by itself. The theater license ordinance did not contain its own severability clause, but the City Code had a general one applicable by its own terms to all sections of the code. The court reversed the conviction. All the restrictions on the issuance of licenses in the city's theater license ordinance were clearly and admittedly invalid, and without those the ordinance was only an empty shell. References to safety codes were insufficient to sustain the licensing requirement of an ordinance overloaded with invalid criteria. The invalid portions of the theater license ordinance were not severable, and the whole ordinance was invalid as an ensemble.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction.

Melvin v. West Frankfort


No. 80-239


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


93 Ill. App. 3d 425; 417 N.E.2d 260; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 2122; 48 Ill. Dec. 858; 25 Empl. Prac. Dec. (CCH) P31,744

DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff applicant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Franklin County (Illinois), which granted judgment on the pleadings in favor of defendants, city and city officials, in the applicant's action seeking a declaration that a statute was unconstitutional. The applicant also sought the permission of the court to amend his complaint to include a 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claim.


OVERVIEW: The applicant, who had an amputation of one of his legs below the knee, applied to the city to become a firefighter and passed the qualifying physical and written examinations. Subsequently, the city informed the applicant that they could not hire him because, pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24, par. 10-2.1-6 (1977), they were prohibited from hiring him as a regular duty firefighter because he was an amputee. The applicant filed an action seeking a declaration that the statute was unconstitutional. The trial court granted judgment on the pleadings in favor of defendants. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded. The court held that the statute violated the provisions on Ill. Const. art. I, § 19 (1970), which prohibited discrimination in hiring. However, the court held that the applicant could not collect damages for defendant's action because defendants were immune from damages under the Local Governmental and Governmental Employees Tort Immunity Act (Act), Ill. The court also denied the applicant's motion to amend his complaint to include a 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claim because he failed to file the appropriate application.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the trial court's decision that granted judgment in favor of defendants in the applicant's action which sought to declare a statute unconstitutional. The court denied the applicant permission to amend his complaint.

Artim Transp., Inc. v. Illinois Commerce Com.


No. 16507


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


93 Ill. App. 3d 344; 417 N.E.2d 225; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 2109; 48 Ill. Dec. 823



February 18, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County; the Hon. RICHARD L. CADAGIN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff applicant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois), which affirmed the decision of defendant Illinois Commerce Commission that denied approval of the applicant's acquisition and control of a motor carrier. Intervenor transportation company sought to have the Commission's decision sustained. The company's appeal was consolidated with the applicant's action in the circuit court.


OVERVIEW: The applicant sought approval from the Commission's motor carrier division for his acquisition of a carrier by the purchase of all of the outstanding shares of its common stock. The applicant was the manager of the company. The carrier's majority stockholder testified that space and equipment were leased from a business that was partially owned by the applicant's father. The Commission speculated that the applicant entered into an oral agreement with the stockholder to purchase the carrier when he was hired and failed to get prior approval from the Commission. The court reversed the circuit court's judgment. Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 18-309 provided for Commission approval of an acquisition if the purchaser was fit, willing, and able; the seller had not abandoned, suspended, or discontinued operations; and the transaction was consistent with the public interest. There was no evidence of an oral contract. Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 18-301(d) was interpreted as a legislative mandate that the development of business was to be encouraged. The carrier had not abandoned its operation because it leased space and equipment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's judgment that affirmed the Commission's decision.

 

1500 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Korte-Reinheimer v. City Council of Palos Hills


No. 80-3031


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


94 Ill. App. 3d 219; 418 N.E.2d 783; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 2263; 49 Ill. Dec. 763



February 17, 1981, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 9, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. MARJAN P. STANIEC, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city council members sought review of the order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which awarded a writ of mandamus to appellee citizens that required the presentation of a public policy proposition to a municipality's electorate.


OVERVIEW: After the citizens filed a complaint for mandamus that sought a writ directing that a special election be held on a designated date, the city council members filed a motion to dismiss. The trial court denied the motion to dismiss and granted the writ of mandamus, and the city council members sought review. On appeal, the city council members contended that the trial court erred in ordering a special election pursuant to a petition and on a date not contemplated within the provisions of the Election Consolidation Act of Illinois, and that the Act would have been unconstitutionally retroactive. The city council also contended that the citizens were guilty of laches, and that the citizens did not have a clear legal right to mandamus. The court held that certain provisions of the Act that became effective prior to the time the proposition was to have been voted upon were mandatory and that other, while directory in nature, were worded in such affirmative language as to have required a result other than that which obtained. Therefore, the court held that the citizens were not possessed of a clear legal right to the mandamus that they sought.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and vacated the order of the trial court that awarded the citizens a writ of mandamus requiring the presentation of a public policy proposition to a municipal electorate.

 

1501 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Mid-America Television Co. v. Peoria Housing Authority


No. 80-222


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


93 Ill. App. 3d 314; 417 N.E.2d 210; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 2102; 48 Ill. Dec. 808; 7 Media L. Rep. 1034



February 11, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Peoria County; the Hon. ROBERT E. HUNT, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant media organization sought review of the order of the Circuit Court of Peoria County (Illinois), which denied its motion for summary judgment against appellee housing authority in the media organization's action for a writ of mandamus ordering the release of information from the housing authority.


OVERVIEW: The housing authority refused the media organization access to records containing information about which landlords were receiving federal rent subsidies. The media organization filed an action for a writ of mandamus ordering the housing authority to produce the requested information and filed a motion for summary judgment. The trial court denied the media organization's motion and held that the housing authority prevailed on its affirmative defenses. The court reversed and held that the records requested were "reports and records" as meant by Ill. Const. art. VIII, § 1, and Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 116, para. 43.103(a) (1979), which guaranteed the public access to information on the operations of state and local government. The court further held that landlords and tenants who received public funds had no protectable right of privacy because public aid was not a private fact. The court noted state provisions that already mandated disclosure of the names of recipients of public aid. The court remanded the cause to the trial court with instructions to enter an order issuing a writ of mandamus granting the media organization access to the records.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order, which denied the media organization's motion for summary judgment and ruled that the housing authority prevailed on its affirmative defenses. The court remanded the cause with instructions to the trial court to enter an order issuing a writ of mandamus granting the media organization access to the requested records.

 

1502 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Miller


No. 79-1007


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


92 Ill. App. 3d 1148; 416 N.E.2d 765; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 2059; 48 Ill. Dec. 492



February 4, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of McDonough County; the Hon. MAX B. STEWART, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of McDonough County (Illinois) denying his petition for post-conviction relief. The court had previously affirmed on direct appeal his conviction for rape. Following the court's affirmance of his conviction, he filed the underlying petition in the circuit court seeking post-conviction relief, which was denied.


OVERVIEW: The court first noted that most of defendant's claims, including the effectiveness of trial counsel, were waived for failure to timely raise them. Therefore, the court would not address them. One issue that was not waived, however, was whether defendant's due process rights were violated when, at the pretrial hearing to determine his competency to stand trial, he was unconstitutionally given the burden of proving himself unfit to stand trial. The court found that the fitness hearing conducted in the instant case pursuant to the § 5-2-1(i) of the Unif. Code Corr., Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-2-1(i) (1975), constituted a violation of defendant's due process rights and necessitated reversal. The only question that remained was whether the court was to remand for a retrospective fitness hearing or for a new trial. The court reluctantly held that, in view of the difficulties inherent in conducting a nunc pro tunc redetermination of defendant's fitness at trial, the only way to adequately protect his due process rights was to afford him a new trial, provided that he was fit for retrial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court and remanded the case for a new trial.

 

1503 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Davis


No. 80-32


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


93 Ill. App. 3d 187; 416 N.E.2d 1179; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 2089; 48 Ill. Dec. 657



February 3, 1981, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 9, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. WILLIAM COUSINS, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of unlawful use of a weapon.


OVERVIEW: When defendant was stopped for questioning because he matched the description of an attempted automobile theft suspect, defendant drew a pistol. The court affirmed defendant's conviction. It was within the trial court's discretion to admit into evidence the reason defendant was stopped. Although it was unnecessary to comment upon the screwdriver protruding from the auto's ignition, admission of this unnecessary detail was harmless error. Admission into evidence of the handcuffs found on defendant was not error because it was intertwined with the circumstances of the arrest. The prosecutor's argument regarding defendant's credibility was within permissible bounds. Further, defendant's closing argument, that the police officers were biased and had lied, invited the state's response thereto in rebuttal. The state's closing argument that possession of handcuffs strengthened the supposition that defendant was in possession of a weapon was improper, but it did not result in substantial prejudice to defendant. There was no indication that the difference in the sentence after trial from the sentence upon the withdrawn guilty was a penalty for the election to stand trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for unlawful use of a weapon.

 

1504 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Turner


No. 79-1695


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


93 Ill. App. 3d 61; 416 N.E.2d 1149; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 2069; 48 Ill. Dec. 627



February 2, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. THOMAS FITZGERALD, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of rape and deviate sexual assault. He also challenged the sentence imposed under the extended-term statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-8-2 (1979).


OVERVIEW: On appeal from his rape and deviate sexual assault conviction, defendant argued that the prosecutor's closing argument regarding defendant's failure to call corroborating witnesses denied him a fair trial because he had no duty to produce a witness who was equally accessible to the State. The court affirmed, and held that defendant had failed to raise the objection at trial or in his motion for a new trial and, therefore, it was waived. Further, any error caused by the closing remarks was harmless. The court held that defendant had been notified before sentencing of the aggravating allegation and that it was not necessary to include it in the information. An extended-term sentence was properly imposed upon a finding of only one of the aggravating factors, heinous conduct, under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-5-3.2(b) (1977). The extended-term statute was not unconstitutionally vague. Defendant's behavior went beyond what was necessary to show exceptionally brutal and heinous behavior indicative of wanton cruelty. Finally, the trial court correctly did not consider evidence of a separate incident regarding pending charges against defendant in imposing the sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction and sentence for rape and deviate sexual assault.

 

1505 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Stevens


No. 80-1039


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


92 Ill. App. 3d 794; 416 N.E.2d 314; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 1997; 48 Ill. Dec. 283



January 19, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. ARTHUR V. ZELEZINSKI, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of the dismissal by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) of charges against defendants for possession of talwin, a controlled substance, in violation of § 402 of the Illinois Controlled Substances Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1402(b).


OVERVIEW: Defendants had argued in their motion to dismiss that existing case law had struck down § 402 as unconstitutional. The State contended that the constitutional infirmity was not present in the instant action because possession of talwin did not incur a more severe penalty than delivery of the same substance. Based on an order in an unrelated chancery action that declared talwin to be temporarily regulated by Schedule IV of the Act rather than Schedule II, defendants argued that possession at the time of the arrest would incur a more severe penalty and, thus, equal protection was violated. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded. The court held that the existing case law was limited to applications of the Act that subjected a defendant to a harsher penalty for possession than for delivery or manufacture of the controlled substance in question. As a Schedule II controlled substance, the court found that charges of possession of talwin were, therefore, not constitutionally infirm. The court also pointed out that the chancery court order that declared talwin to be a Schedule IV controlled substance did not have the potency of stare decisis as it had not been appealed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of the charges against defendants and remanded for further proceedings.

 

1506 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Bachman


No. 80-179


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


92 Ill. App. 3d 419; 414 N.E.2d 1369; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 1971; 47 Ill. Dec. 253



January 7, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of La Salle County; the Hon. FRANK X. YACKLEY, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of La Salle County (Illinois), in which he was convicted of rape and unlawful restraint and was sentenced to prison for 20 years and two years, respectively, with the sentences to run concurrently.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the verdict and the constitutionality of the "Rape Shield" statute and claimed that the trial court erred in entering convictions for both rape and unlawful restraint, making certain evidentiary rulings, instructing the jury, and imposing a 20-year sentence. The court reversed in part and affirmed in part, holding that: (1) there were not two acts committed which were sufficient to support convictions for both rape and unlawful restraint; (2) the victim's testimony as to her doctor's medical advice was cumulative and not prejudicial to defendant; (3) the jury instruction on the issue of resistance was proper as there was evidence that the victim was threatened and intimidated by defendant, and the Prim instruction was proper as the case was not a complex one, the law was not misstated, and the jury was not confused; and (4) the trial court properly considered both a letter from the victim regarding the effect of the rape upon her and defendant's prior criminal record in determining defendant's sentence. The court concluded that defendant was proven guilty beyond a reasonable doubt and that the "Rape Shield" statute had repeatedly been deemed constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that portion of the trial court's judgment convicting and sentencing defendant for the offense of rape and reversed that portion of the trial court's judgment convicting and sentencing defendant for the offense of unlawful restraint.

Kurtzworth v. Illinois Racing Bd.


Nos. 78-164, 78-281, 78-292, 78-293, 78-386, 78-164, 78-517 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


92 Ill. App. 3d 564; 415 N.E.2d 1290; 1981 Ill. App. LEXIS 1976; 48 Ill. Dec. 6



January 7, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County; the Hon. J. F. CUNNINGHAM, the Hon. KENNETH J. JUEN, the Hon. RICHARD GOLDENHERSH, and the Hon. THOMAS M. DALEY, Judges, presiding.

APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Madison County; the Hon. A. ANDREAS MATOESIAN and the Hon. JOHN W. DAY, Judges, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Courts of St. Clair and Madison County (Illinois) issued preliminary injunctions staying the suspensions of plaintiff licensees until the defendant Illinois Racing Board (board) issued its final rulings. The licensees did not seek relief upon any substantive issue. The board objected to the circuit courts' jurisdiction, and took an interlocutory appeal.


OVERVIEW: Although the cases appeared moot the court found that the public interest required a determination of the consolidated appeals. In each case, the plaintiff as holder of an occupational license alleged that he was being summarily penalized, being deprived of his livelihood and suffering irreparable damage prior to the time that his case was to be heard. It was further variously asserted that by the time a hearing could be held the loss or detriment suffered would be irretrievable. The court held the preliminary injunctions to stay the suspensions were properly issued pending hearings on the merits by the board, despite the fact that the preliminary injunction was the only relief being sought from the circuit court. The court concluded that none of the licensees were deprived of due process of law by the interim suspensions made by the stewards. The public interest in preserving the integrity and honesty of the horse racing industry outweighed any inconvenience to the holders of race-track-related occupational licenses caused by the summary interim suspension of licenses pending a hearing before the board.


OUTCOME: The temporary restraining orders and preliminary injunctions staying the suspensions of race track related licenses pending a full hearing before the Illinois Racing Board was affirmed.

People v. Robinson


Nos. 79-771, 79-501 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


91 Ill. App. 3d 1128; 414 N.E.2d 1335; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 4146; 47 Ill. Dec. 219



December 31, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Will County; the Hon. ANGELO F. PISTILLI, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants challenged a decision from the Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois), which convicted them of robbery and aggravated battery, sentenced one to an extended term of 12 years for robbery and a five year term for aggravated battery, the sentences to run concurrently, and the other to concurrent terms of imprisonment of three years for robbery and two years for aggravated battery, and ordered reimbursement to the public defender.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were convicted of robbery and aggravated assault. One was sentenced to an extended term of 12 years for robbery and a five year term for aggravated battery, the sentences to run concurrently and the other to concurrent terms of imprisonment of three years for robbery and two years for aggravated battery. Both defendants were ordered to reimburse the public defender. Both defendants asserted that the obligation to reimburse their public defender was unconstitutional and one defendant challenged the imposition of an extended sentence based on prior convictions within a 10-year period. The court vacated the reimbursement order because the obligation had been previously determined to be unconstitutional. Drury v. County of McLean


No. 16438


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


92 Ill. App. 3d 83; 414 N.E.2d 1330; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 4160; 47 Ill. Dec. 214



December 30, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of McLean County; the Hon. WAYNE C. TOWNLEY, JR., Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff payors challenged a summary judgment from the Circuit Court of McLean County (Illinois), which awarded the payors only the sums representing payment of court costs to defendant county. The payors had filed suit seeking reimbursement for fines and costs they paid to the clerk of the circuit court after the payors were convicted under a controlled substances act later held to be unconstitutional. Both sides moved for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: Of the fine and costs money received from the payors, a portion was remitted to the county treasurer and another portion was remitted to the county's State's attorney. These sums represented payment of court costs. Fine money was disbursed to the State and a city equally. None of the balance had gone into the county treasury. On appeal, the payors argued that the trial court was a county officer and because the money had gone into the hands of the clerk, the county was liable for reimbursement. The trial court concluded that the clerk of the circuit court was not a county officer and that the county was liable only for sums actually received by it. The court held that: (1) the payors' action more nearly resembled the common law action for money had and received than a tort action; (2) under the Illinois Constitution, the clerk was also a judicial officer; (3) since the money was paid out not in the ordinary course of duty but under a mistake as to what that duty was, equity required restitution; and (4) this was particularly true because the county would be able to recoup disbursements from the State and the city or at least make setoff on future payments due to those entities.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the portion of the summary judgment fixing damages and remanded the cause to the trial court with directions that the amounts of the judgments entered be increased as to each payor to reflect the fines paid by them to the clerk.

People v. Nelson


No. 79-254


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


92 Ill. App. 3d 35; 415 N.E.2d 688; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 4154; 47 Ill. Dec. 683

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County; the Hon. JOHN S. GHENT, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the decision of the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois), which convicted him of the murders of his six children. He was sentenced to 100 to 200 years' imprisonment on each of the six counts, the sentences to run concurrently.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of killing his six children. The jury was unable to reach a decision on whether to impose the death penalty. He was sentenced to 100 to 200 years' imprisonment on each of the 6 counts, the sentences to run concurrently. Defendant contended that it was error not to instruct the jury on the consequences of a verdict of not guilty by reason of insanity. By its own terms, defendant's proposed instruction inferred by its language that defendant would have been committed as a result of a commitment hearing. Inasmuch as this misstated the law, and as it would have mislead the jury, the instruction was properly refused. The defendant also argued that his sentence was excessive. The court disagreed with this argument because the record fully supported the sentence within the court's proper exercise of discretion. The court affirmed the conviction and sentences of defendant.

People v. Smith


No. 79-245


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


91 Ill. App. 3d 438; 414 N.E.2d 1281; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 4051; 47 Ill. Dec. 165



December 24, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Ogle County; the Hon. L. E. ELLISON, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Ogle County (Illinois), which convicted him of murder and armed robbery and sentenced him to life imprisonment for the murder conviction and 50 years' imprisonment for the armed robbery conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder and armed robbery. Defendant appealed, claiming that the trial court erred in not suppressing incriminating statements that he alleged were elicited in violation of his right to counsel as provided in the Sixth and Fourteenth Amendments to the United States Constitution and Ill. Const. art. 1, § 8. On appeal, the court affirmed and ruled that the record showed that a jailer wrongfully interfered with the attorney-client relationship where there was no valid reason to justify the jailer's denial of a personal consultation between the attorney and defendant while defendant was being held. However, there were significant intervening circumstances between the time that the attorney was denied permission to consult with defendant and defendant's making of the statement, including the passage of almost 24 hours, and the fact that defendant was given his Miranda warnings, which he claimed he understood before he voluntarily made the statement, to support the court's finding that the causal connection between the police misconduct and the incriminating statement was sufficiently attenuated to permit the use of the incriminating statement at trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Bishop v. Crowther


No. 79-1852


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


92 Ill. App. 3d 1; 415 N.E.2d 599; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 4149; 47 Ill. Dec. 594



December 22, 1980, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 26, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. EDWARD C. HOFERT, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff roofer brought an action pursuant to the Structural Work Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 48, para. 60 et seq. (1977), for injuries suffered while working on the home of defendant, who was experienced in construction work and was operating as the general contractor (homeowner). The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) entered judgment on the jury verdict against the homeowner. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: The homeowner decided to put an addition on his house. He was a principal or shareholder and vice-president of a company that was to install gutters and shingle the roof. He had the authority to stop the roofer's work if it was being done in an unsafe manner, and he scheduled the work. The accident occurred when the roofer placed a ladder in a muddy, uneven area close to a recent excavation for the project, and began carrying a 85-pound bale of shingles up. The ladder slipped. Affirming the decision, the court noted that the homeowner performed the duties of general contractor and coordinator personally and not as an employee of his company, and as general contractor, he was responsible for job safety. The court found ample evidence supporting the jury's finding that defendant reasonably could have known about violations of the Act. The court added that the covenant providing that the roofer would not seek to execute any judgment against any personal assets of the homeowner, but reserved the right to execute against assets relating to his insurance, was irrelevant to the finding of damages. The court also rejected the homeowner's argument that the Act was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment for the roofer in the suit he brought against the homeowner under the Structural Work Act for injuries sustained when he fell off a ladder while working on the homeowner's project.

People v. Rodriguez


No. 79-914


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


91 Ill. App. 3d 626; 414 N.E.2d 1202; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 4077; 47 Ill. Dec. 86



December 9, 1980, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 13, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. ANGELO D. MISTRETTA, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction and sentence for direct contempt entered by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois). Defendant argued that his act of slapping a police officer was not an intentional act but an irrational outburst that was not intended to disrupt the courtroom proceedings, that he was denied due process, and that his sentence was excessive.


OVERVIEW: When a police officer who had issued two traffic tickets to defendant was coming before the trial court to testify, defendant slapped the officer in the face. The trial court determined that defendant was in direct contempt and sentenced him to five months' imprisonment. On appeal, the court concluded that a contemptuous intent was inferable from the action of the contemnor. Defendant was guilty of direct contempt because his action did create a disturbance and interfered with the orderly administration of justice. The court determined that, because of the unique circumstances present in direct criminal contempt cases, an order finding a person in contempt was able to be entered without prior notice, written charge, plea, issue, or trial. Defendant's due process rights were not violated. The court found that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in sentencing defendant to five months' imprisonment and, absent proof of abuse of discretion, the court had no power to modify defendant's sentence under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 615(b)(4), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110A, para. 615(b)(4) (1979).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1514 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Padilla


No. 80-172


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


91 Ill. App. 3d 799; 415 N.E.2d 12; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 4098; 47 Ill. Dec. 287



December 9, 1980, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 9, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. VINCENT BENTIVENGA, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a bench trial in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), defendant was found guilty of voluntary manslaughter. He was sentenced to five years. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that his accomplice's uncorroborated testimony was insufficient to convict him because the accomplice was offered dismissal of the charges pending against him in exchange for the testimony. The court stated that although accomplice testimony should be scrutinized carefully, the uncorroborated testimony of an accomplice could be sufficient evidence to support a conviction. Here, the court stated, it was satisfied that defendant was proven guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. Next, the court noted that the Illinois Supreme Court had held that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-5-4.1 (1979), which authorized reviewing courts to reduce a sentence to probation, was an unconstitutional exercise of legislative authority over the judicial standard of sentence review. Thus, the court had no authority to reduce a sentence of imprisonment to one of probation. Finally, the court held that because the trial court had not specified its reasons for arriving at its sentencing determination, as required by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-4-1(c), it could not review defendant's complaint that his sentence was excessive. Therefore, the court vacated defendant's sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and vacated his sentence. It remanded the case for a new sentencing determination.

People v. Ogunsola


No. 16070


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


91 Ill. App. 3d 26; 414 N.E.2d 219; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3982; 46 Ill. Dec. 497



December 3, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of McLean County; the Hon. WAYNE C. TOWNLEY, JR., Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of McLean County (Illinois), which found him guilty of deceptive practices in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 17-1(B)(d) (1979). Defendant was sentenced to serve 60 days in the county jail, and the trial court entered an order declaring a forfeiture of a bond deposit to reimburse the county for the services provided by a public defender.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the State failed to establish intent to defraud, that the information omitted an essential element of the offense, that he was denied a fair trial because the jury was not instructed on an element of the offense, that he was denied effective assistance of counsel, and that the trial court relied upon an unconstitutional statute in ordering a forfeiture of his cash bond. The court affirmed the trial court with respect to the first four points, but it reversed and ruled for defendant on the fifth point. The court found that there was intent to commit fraud when defendant failed to pay a bill to pick up his car from a repair shop. Defendant admitted he issued a bad check with the intent of obtaining the car after there was a dispute over the repairs and corresponding charges. Defendant was in a position where he had to pay the charges or leave his car. The court concluded that defendant issued a bad check intending to overcome a valid lien in favor of the repair shop, but such a self-help measure was not a lawful defense. However, based on a holding in case law, the court found that the trial court erred in requiring forfeiture of defendant's bond.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction, but it reversed the trial court's order forfeiting defendant's bond.

Altman v. Health & Hospitals Governing Com.


No. 79-2121


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


91 Ill. App. 3d 498; 414 N.E.2d 1091; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 4057; 46 Ill. Dec. 938



December 2, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. NATHAN M. COHEN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the county health and hospital governing commission, appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which awarded reinstatement and backpay to plaintiff employees in their action that alleged bad faith in their lay-offs from their jobs as tradesmen at the county hospitals.


OVERVIEW: The employees filed a complaint against the commission, alleging that because there were sufficient funds to cover their employment, the discharges were in bad faith and that they had a constitutionally-protected right in their employment sufficient to require a plenary hearing. The trial court ordered reinstatement and awarded backpay. The court reversed, holding that the trial court's finding of bad faith by the commission was against the manifest weight of the evidence. The fact that a supervisor purportedly laid off painters and bricklayers as retribution against the foremen of those shops was not believable in light of the numbers of employees who were discharged. The court found that the lay-offs did result in substantial savings and that there was insufficient evidence of bad faith to rebut the presumption of the commission's good faith. The court found that the employees were not discharged within the meaning of § 16 of the County Hospitals Governing Commission Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 34, para. 5026 (1977) and that any property interest in their jobs was adequately protected by the hearing provided them.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court, which awarded back pay and reinstatement to the employees. The court held that the finding of the commission's bad faith was against the manifest weight of the evidence.

 

1517 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Merchel


No. 79-426


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


91 Ill. App. 3d 285; 414 N.E.2d 804; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 4026; 46 Ill. Dec. 751



November 28, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Jefferson County; the Hon. HARRY L. ZIEGLER, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Circuit Court of Jefferson County (Illinois) for murder and his sentence to a term of natural life imprisonment pursuant to the Unified Code of Corrections, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-8-1(a)(1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant beat the victim to death. The trial court found that there were no mitigating factors and that the murder was accompanied by exceptionally brutal or heinous behavior indicative of wanton cruelty. The court affirmed the conviction, finding that defendant waived the right to argue that the waiver of his Miranda rights was involuntary because he failed to raise this issue at trial or in a post-trial motion. The failure of the police to inform defendant of the nature and purpose of their questions did not render the statements involuntary. The court found that the natural life statutory provision, para. 1005-8-1(a), was not unconstitutionally vague. The court could only impose the natural life sentence if the murder was accompanied by behavior which was brutal or heinous, and which indicated wanton cruelty on the part of the perpetrator. The court found that this provision gave reasonable guidance and was designed to avoid arbitrary and discriminatory enforcement. When the natural life provision was read in conjunction with other statutory provisions and the sentencing scheme established by the legislature, it did not violate Ill. Const. art. I, § 11.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's murder conviction and sentence to a term of natural life imprisonment for a beating death.

 

1518 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Roque v. Quern


No. 79-1340


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


90 Ill. App. 3d 1015; 414 N.E.2d 161; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3957; 46 Ill. Dec. 439



November 26, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. RICHARD L. CURRY, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff doctor appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which affirmed the finding of defendant Director of the Illinois Department of Public Aid (director) that the doctor violated the licensing provision of Section 14(a) of the Illinois Dangerous Drug Abuse Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 91 1/2, para. 120.14 (1977). The doctor appealed on the ground that the Act was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The director adopted a hearing officer's recommendation to terminate the doctor's participation as a vendor in a medical assistance program based on the finding that he provided services without a license to a clientele of whom 95 percent were drug users seeking treatment of an abstinence syndrome. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's order. The court held that the director's decision was not against the manifest weight of the evidence. The court held that the doctor's actions contravened the purpose of the Act to establish a comprehensive program to prevent addiction and abuse and to provide treatment, care, and rehabilitation of persons addicted to drugs. The court further held that the Act did not constitute an unconstitutional delegation of legislative authority. The court stated that the Act sufficiently identified the persons and activities subject to regulation, the harm of drug addiction, and the means available to prevent the harm through licensing of physicians and a comprehensive treatment program. The court also held that the legislation sufficiently defined the terms such as "treatment" and "care" and was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order that the doctor violated the licensing provision of the Act.

People v. Woolridge


No. 79-438


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


91 Ill. App. 3d 298; 414 N.E.2d 814; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 4027; 46 Ill. Dec. 761



November 26, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Clay County; the Hon. W. R. TODD, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of her conviction and sentencing by the Circuit Court of Clay County (Illinois) for unlawful delivery of a controlled substance. Defendant asserted that the court improperly excluded evidence that would have revealed witness bias. Defendant requested a reduction of sentence, and the prosecution requested a sentence increase under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-5-4.1 (1979).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted and sentenced for the unlawful delivery of a controlled substance. The court affirmed the trial court's conviction and sentence of defendant. Although defendant asserted that the trial court had improperly excluded evidence that would have revealed witness bias, the court noted that defendant failed to lay a foundation for the introduction of that evidence. Before a party may introduce evidence concerning bias, she must first lay a foundation by questioning the witness concerning the alleged bias and giving the witness an opportunity to respond. Although the prosecution requested that defendant's sentence be increased under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-5-5-4.1 (1979), the court noted that this statute had been declared unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed both the conviction and sentence entered by the trial court.

People v. Lenhart


No. 80-153


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


90 Ill. App. 3d 502; 413 N.E.2d 220; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 4255; 45 Ill. Dec. 887



November 26, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Will County; the Hon. CHARLES P. CONNOR, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment by the Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois), which convicted him for the offense of armed violence in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 33A-2 (1979) while committing the felony of criminal damage to property in excess of $ 150 in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 21-1 (1979).


OVERVIEW: Defendant shot at a police officer who was driving an unmarked police car. At the time of the shooting, defendant was under the mistaken belief as to the identity of the officer. A verdict was directed in favor of defendant on a charge of armed violence based on intimidation. The jury acquitted defendant of the charge of attempted murder. On appeal of the armed violence based on property damage conviction, defendant contended that the armed violence statute was unconstitutional because the mandatory minimum penalty of six years for his conduct did not reasonably relate to the seriousness of the offense of criminal damage to property. The court held that because of the seriousness of defendant's conduct and defendant's long criminal record the trial judge properly exercised his discretion to impose a greater sentence than the minimum demanded by the statute. The court found that the armed violence statute was not unconstitutional on its face or as applied to defendant because the legislature's rational and legitimate intent to severely punish an armed individual who showed disrespect for the law was met under the facts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Aliperto v. Department of Registration & Education


No. 79-1647


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


90 Ill. App. 3d 985; 414 N.E.2d 117; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3952; 46 Ill. Dec. 395



November 25, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. REGINALD J. HOLZER, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, department of registration and education and its director, sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which permanently enjoined the department from taking further action to suspend or revoke appellee barber's certificate of registration to practice barbering.


OVERVIEW: The director adopted the barbering examining committee's findings, but ordered it to reconsider its recommendation to spend the barber's license. The committee then recommended revocation of the license. The court concluded that equitable relief was appropriate even though the administrative proceedings were continuing because the barber had shown the inadequacy of available remedies, the futility of pursuing exhaustion of administrative remedies, and the likelihood of irreparable injury if the courts did not intervene. The court found that it was unnecessary to determine whether § 52 of the Ill. Barbers Law, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111, para. 1659 (1979) required the director to order a rehearing within 20 days because the director did not act within a reasonable amount of time in ordering the rehearing by waiting 132 days. The court reversed, holding that the trial court should not have substituted its judgment for that of the director, and erred when it enjoined the director from entering a final order based on the committee's findings. The court remanded for the trial court to enter an order directing the director and department to proceed to a final decision.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision in favor of the barber in his action to enjoin the department and its director from suspending or revoking his certificate of registration to practice barbering.

McKenna v. Board of Trustees


No. 79-1850


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


90 Ill. App. 3d 992; 414 N.E.2d 123; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3953; 46 Ill. Dec. 401



November 25, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. ARTHUR L. DUNNE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employees challenged an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted the motion to dismiss of appellees, merit board and university trustees, and dismissed the employees' complaint seeking declaratory and injunctive relief from appellees' redesignation of their wage rate classification.


OVERVIEW: The employees were employed by the university and had been compensated at the prevailing rate tied to the wage scale in a collective bargaining agreement governing a local union. The employees' collective bargaining agreement effected a retroactive discontinuance of compensation that paralleled the local union's agreement and the merit board approved a negotiated rate of pay. The negotiated rate was less than that paid under the prevailing rate of wage. The employees brought suit seeking relief from the redesignation of their wage rate classification. The trial court granted the university's motion to dismiss and the court affirmed. It found that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 127, para. 391 (1975) (Pay Act), did not apply to the employees as the university was not an agency of the state within the Pay Act. Further, redesignation of the employee's wage status did not violate the University Civil Service System Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24 1/2, para. 38b1 et seq. (1975), as the merit board was only required to initially compensate the employees at the prevailing rate; subsequent negotiations were permitted and could result in a change in the rate of compensation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the employee's complaint challenging appellees' redesignation of the employees' wage rate classification for failure to state a cause of action.

People v. Wagner


No. 79-298


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


91 Ill. App. 3d 254; 414 N.E.2d 773; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 4023; 46 Ill. Dec. 720



November 25, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County; the Hon. KENNETH J. JUEN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of selling a brown powder that he represented to be heroin to an undercover agent in violation of § 404 of the Controlled Substances Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1404 (1977).


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted defendant of selling a brown powder that he represented to be heroin to an undercover agent in violation of § 404 of the Controlled Substances Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1404 (1977). The brown powder was neither heroin nor any other controlled substance. Defendant contended on appeal that § 404 was unconstitutional on the ground that it punished individuals more severely for the delivery of innocuous substances than for the delivery of controlled substances. The court affirmed the judgment against defendant. The court concluded that the Equal Protection Clause did not require proportionality of penalties because the conduct of those who delivered purported controlled substances was dissimilar from the conduct of those who actually delivered controlled substances. The court also concluded that defendant's rights to due process of law were not violated because the penalty provision of § 404 did not have to bear a reasonable relation to any of the penalty provisions of the Act relating to sale or possession of controlled substances.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted defendant of a violation of the Controlled Substances Act.

Springfield Metropolitan Exposition & Auditorium Authority v. Castle


No. 16205


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


90 Ill. App. 3d 710; 413 N.E.2d 443; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 4285; 46 Ill. Dec. 3



November 20, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County; the Hon. SIMON L. FRIEDMAN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff Springfield Metropolitan Exposition and Auditorium Authority (authority) appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois), that was entered in favor of defendant director of the Illinois Department of Business and Economic Development (department). The authority filed this action for a declaratory judgment to have a paragraph in its contract with the department declared void.


OVERVIEW: The authority was created by the Springfield Metropolitan Exposition and Auditorium Authority Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 85, para. 1251 et seq. (1979), to promote and operate expositions in the city, with the power to purchase or construct convention centers. The authority was funded in part through the Metropolitan Civic Center Support Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 85, para. 1391 et seq.(1979), which was administered by the department. In order to fund the purchase and construction of a convention center, the authority entered into an agreement with the department for state support of its bonds. The department required the contract to contain a provision that it would receive the bond proceeds each year as a set off against the state support payments on the bonds. The authority filed for a declaratory judgment and the trial court found in favor of the department. On appeal, the court reversed. The court determined that under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 85, para. 1394(3) the department did not have the authority to require the provision in the contract. The provision meant that the state was paying less than the statutory requirement and was therefore void.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which entered judgment in favor of the department, and remanded.

Thomas v. Police Bd. of Chicago

Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


90 Ill. App. 3d 1101; 414 N.E.2d 11; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3971; 46 Ill. Dec. 289



November 17, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. ARTHUR L. DUNNE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant police officer sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which affirmed a decision of appellee police board, which discharged the officer for violating a police department rule forbidding bringing discredit upon the department for outstanding parking tickets.


OVERVIEW: A police officer obtained 99 parking tickets in 1975, 75 tickets in 1976, and 27 tickets in 1977. The police department's internal affairs division investigated the matter and it was discovered that the police officer paid $ 865 out of $ 2,135 in fines. The police board found that the police officer was twice arrested for failure to pay parking tickets, received notice, and failed to appear in court for such tickets. The board ruled that the police officer's conduct was cause for discharge. The lower court affirmed the ruling. The court partly reversed the factual findings as unsupported by the evidence, and remanded the matter for the imposition of a lesser sanction holding that the police officer's conduct of not fully paying off the parking tickets was insufficient cause for discharge. The court found that a police board finding of cause for discharge was subject to judicial review and that the finding could be reversed.


OUTCOME: The court partly reversed the factual findings of the police board, as unsupported by the evidence and remanded the case for the imposition of a lesser sanction against the police officer.

People v. Wood


No. 79-263


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


91 Ill. App. 3d 414; 414 N.E.2d 759; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 4048; 46 Ill. Dec. 706



November 17, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Clay County; the Hon. DANIEL H. DAILEY, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Clay County (Illinois), which convicted him of arson following a jury trial and sentenced him to five years' imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court sought to determine whether defendant was improperly denied appointed counsel at trial. Defendant urged that the trial court erroneously determined that he was not indigent on the basis of his substantial bail deposits. The State urged that the law presumed bail deposits were in fact the property of the accused. The court concluded that the trial court's November 30, 1978, granting of the public defender's motion to withdraw on the sole ground that defendant had substantial bail on deposit in various Illinois counties was erroneous. The court further concluded that defendant's testimony and admissions showed that he made gratuitous conveyances to his ex-wife, during the pendency of the case, of property and money, which defendant could have used to hire appointed counsel. The court determined that the trial court should have concluded on the basis of defendant's transactions during the pendency of the case that defendant had or controlled assets sufficient to enable him to employ counsel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

People v. Bitner


No. 80-64


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


89 Ill. App. 3d 1106; 412 N.E.2d 721; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3874; 45 Ill. Dec. 370



November 13, 1980, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 26, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Fulton County; the Hon. CHARLES H. WILHELM, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Fulton County (Illinois) that convicted him of home invasion and one count of battery for an incident in which he and others entered into a home occupied by college students. Defendant and the others woke the students and demanded that they party with them; after drinking the students' alcohol, defendant struck two of the students before they could escape the house.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended error, in part, on grounds related to the conduct of his trial, that he received ineffective assistance of counsel, that his sentence was unconstitutionally disproportionate, and that the battery conviction was a lesser included offense of home invasion. On appeal, the court noted that the statute defining home invasion had been held constitutional. There was sufficient evidence to show that defendant's entry was unauthorized, even though he disputed that fact. Further, the unauthorized entry was the mental state proscribed at time of entry, therefore, no evidence of any other intent was required. He failed to preserve his evidentiary challenges when he failed to include the contentions in his post-trial motion and based his appeal on a ground different than that asserted at trial. The court refused to review for plain error because he received a fair and impartial trial. He did not establish his claim of ineffective assistance of counsel pursuant to the standard applicable to representation by private counsel. The sentence was not disproportionate. The conviction for battery was reversed because it was a lesser included offense of the crime of home invasion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment that convicted defendant of home invasion, but it reversed his conviction for battery.

Beane v. Millers Mut. Ins. Asso.


No. 80-69


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


90 Ill. App. 3d 258; 412 N.E.2d 1124; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3919; 45 Ill. Dec. 542; 36 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 78; 25 Empl. Prac. Dec. (CCH) P31,498



November 12, 1980, Filed

DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court, Madison County (Illinois), which denied the employee's motion to file a third amended complaint against appellee employer. Claiming to have been fired for opposing sexual discrimination against women, the employee brought claims based on the constitutional prohibition against sex discrimination, the Illinois Fair Employment Practices Act, and the Civil Rights Act of 1964.


OVERVIEW: The employee filed an action against the employer, claiming the employee's termination was in retaliation for opposing the employer's policies of sex discrimination against women. After several amendments, the employee moved to file a third amended complaint, alleging unconstitutional sex discrimination and violations of the Employment Practices Act and the Civil Rights Act. When the employee's motion was denied, review was sought. Upon review, the court held that the motion's denial was proper because the amended complaint did nothing but re-allege previously rejected matters.
