For instance, the court held that with respect to the constitutional prohibition against sex discrimination, the employee lacked standing to challenge the employer's policies toward women. The court also rejected the Employment Practices Act claim because the employee had failed to pursue and exhaust the administrative remedies. Likewise, the court rejected the Civil Rights Act claim because the employee's charge of discrimination had not been timely filed with the Equal Employment Opportunity Commission.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

People v. Herron

Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


89 Ill. App. 3d 1048; 412 N.E.2d 1365; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3868; 45 Ill. Dec. 641



November 6, 1980, Filed

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Peoria County (Illinois) entered on a jury verdict finding him guilty of armed robbery. Defendant challenged the judgment of conviction on grounds including that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress certain evidence that was obtained after police officers improperly stopped him during an investigation of the offense.


OVERVIEW: The police officers stopped defendant after midnight when they observed him walking in a residential neighborhood that was located a block and a half from a convenience store that had been robbed a few minutes earlier. Defendant stated that he had seen someone running in a northerly direction, and he agreed to a police officer's request to travel with them to the convenience store as a witness. The police officers later recovered a revolver, currency, and other evidence, and the store clerk identified defendant as the robber. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction. The court held that the trial court properly denied defendant's motion to suppress the evidence that implicated defendant in the crime. The court held that the police had the right to make the investigatory stop because they had sufficient articulable facts to infer that criminal activity was afoot. The court held that the trial court properly found that defendant voluntarily consented to accompany the police officers to the store. The court noted that the store clerk was able to describe defendant to the police before the police showed him to the clerk.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's conviction of defendant for armed robbery.

People v. Kleffman


No. 79-399


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


90 Ill. App. 3d 1; 412 N.E.2d 1057; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3883; 45 Ill. Dec. 475



November 6, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Tazewell County; the Hon. JAMES D. HEIPLE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Tazewell County (Illinois), which dismissed an indictment charging defendant, a mayor, with official misconduct under § 33-3(c) of the Illinois Criminal Code of 1961, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 33-3(c) (1979), ruling that § 33-3(c) was unconstitutionally overbroad and vague, and that the indictment failed to allege the elements of the offense with sufficient specificity.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a mayor, was charged with official misconduct in buying a confiscated weapon from the police department. The trial court dismissed the indictment. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded, finding that § 33-3(c) was not overbroad because it did not regulate speech, press, or any other constitutionally protected right, and its requirement that the act be in excess of defendant's lawful authority left it inapplicable to constitutionally protected conduct. The court ruled that § 33-3(c) was not unconstitutionally vague because "in his official capacity" meant accomplished by exploitation of his public position and that defendant's lawful authority as a public official was sufficiently defined that he was able to determine the propriety of his actions. The court found that "personal advantage," in light of the purpose of § 33-3(c), meant an advantage to a particular person as opposed to the public the officer served. The court concluded that the indictment was sufficient in that it reflected the language of the statute and specified defendant's conduct, noting that sale of confiscated weapons was not authorized by the statute governing the disposition of such weapons.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's dismissal of the defendant's indictment and remanded for further proceedings.

People v. Abraham


No. 80-200


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


89 Ill. App. 3d 786; 412 N.E.2d 45; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3825; 45 Ill. Dec. 9



October 31, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Tazewell County; the Hon. JAMES D. HEIPLE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the decision of the Circuit Court of Tazewell County (Illinois), which ordered him to make restitution to the victim of his aggravated battery within one year of his release from the penitentiary.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated battery, sentenced to imprisonment, and ordered to make restitution to his victim within one year of his release from prison, and the court affirmed his sentence. The court found that the lower court did not abuse its discretion in deciding not to hold a hearing to determine defendant's financial capacity to make the restitution. The court determined that the lower court had sufficient information as to defendant's financial status from a hearing held earlier to determine whether he was indigent with respect to the appointment of appellate counsel. The court stated that the information from this hearing, coupled with the earning capacity of defendant in the presentence report, was sufficient for the lower court to make its decision on the issue of restitution. The court found that the amount to be paid was the actual loss suffered by the victim, regardless of any insurance payments made to him, and was not ambiguous. The designation of one-year following defendant's release was a sufficiently specific condition of payment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

City of Champaign v. Dep't of Revenue


No. 16270


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


89 Ill. App. 3d 1066; 412 N.E.2d 211; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3869; 45 Ill. Dec. 78



October 31, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Champaign County; the Hon. HAROLD L. JENSEN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), which dismissed the counts of its complaint concerning the power of appellee department of revenue to correct and relocate taxes it collected on behalf of the city and the county under the Illinois Retailers' Occupation Tax Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 440 et seq. (1979).


OVERVIEW: The department collected and remitted taxes for both the city and the county. An audit revealed that two commercial enterprises were located in the county and not the city. The taxes from those two enterprises that had been remitted to the city totaled $ 479,718.41, and the department proposed to adjust the amount over a period of 36 months by deducting current payments to the city and paying them to the county. On appeal four principal issues were raised: (1) the power of the department to adjust future tax payments in order to correct past errors, (2) the time within which such adjustments of past errors could have been made, (3) the necessity of the adoption of rules by the department before any adjustments were made, and (4) the lack of administrative review or certiorari in the proceedings. Upon review, the court found that the city's issues were meritless. The department had the statutory power to make a correction in the distribution, no public policy was offended thereby, and any reliance on the receipt of the funds by the city was unwarranted. No period of time for correction existed and the department was free to go back as far as its records supported its actions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court dismissing the counts of the city's complaint concerning the power of the department to correct and relocate taxes it collected on behalf of the city and the county.

Gillilan v. Illinois Racing Bd.


No. 80-388


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


89 Ill. App. 3d 726; 411 N.E.2d 1374; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3813; 44 Ill. Dec. 908



October 22, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Kane County; the Hon. JOHN A. KRAUSE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff track owner sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), which affirmed the decision of defendant Illinois Racing Board to deny the owner's three applications for racing dates.


OVERVIEW: The owner bought a track and applied to the Board for racing dates. A hearing was held on the first application and before a decision was rendered, the owner applied a second time. The second application was denied without a hearing and the first application was denied because of financial considerations, the physical problems with the track, and because there was another track within 45 miles (which was a violation of the Illinois Horse Racing Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. Ch. 8, par. 37-1, § 19(a)(1) (1979)). The Board also denied the third application filed a couple of months later without holding a hearing. The lower court and the court affirmed the Board's denial of all three applications. The court found that the Board's decision was not against the manifest weight of the evidence and that the deficiencies in the track were not trivial and at the time of the first application, the track was not suitable for racing. Although some improvements had been made to the rack before the second application was filed, there were still financial problems. The third application was made by the corporation, but was properly denied as it was controlled completely by the owner and his family.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

1534 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Arquilla-De Haan Realtors v. Park Forest


No. 80-330


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


89 Ill. App. 3d 682; 411 N.E.2d 1219; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3806; 44 Ill. Dec. 853



October 16, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. ARTHUR L. DUNNE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a municipality and the members of its Fair Housing Review Board, appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted summary judgment in favor of plaintiffs, a realty agency and a realtor. Plaintiffs filed an action seeking injunctive and declaratory relief alleging that defendants' fair housing ordinances were void as against real estate brokers and salespersons.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs argued that the ordinances were void in their entirety because the state preempted all power to enact fair housing laws as to brokers and salespeople. On appeal, the court held that § 24 of the Real Estate Brokers and Salesmen License Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111, para. 5742 (1979), declared that the powers and functions of that Act were exclusive powers of the state. However, the second paragraph of § 24 provided that nothing in the Act should impair the validity of a Illinois Municipal Code insofar as any municipality enacting ordinances prescribing fair housing practices, defining unfair housing practices, prohibiting discrimination in real estate practices, and establishing fair housing or human relation commissions. The court held that defendants' fair housing ordinances that did not concern licensing, record-keeping, or permits were not subject to attack on the grounds of state preemption or a prior supreme court decision that held that the licensing of real estate brokers and salesmen was the exclusive power of the state. The court reversed the order of the circuit court granting plaintiffs' motion for summary judgment and remanded the cause.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court granting plaintiffs' motion for summary judgment seeking injunctive and declaratory relief to declare the municipality's fair housing ordinances void and remanded the cause for further proceedings.

People v. Robinson


No. 80-56


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


89 Ill. App. 3d 211; 411 N.E.2d 589; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3736; 44 Ill. Dec. 467



October 15, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Will County; the Hon. ANGELO F. PISTILLI, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois), which convicted him of robbery and home invasion and sentenced him to seven years imprisonment on the robbery conviction and eight years on the home invasion conviction.


OVERVIEW: An elderly man identified defendant as one of two men who forced their way into his home and severely beat and robbed him. Defendant was convicted of robbery and home invasion and sentenced to seven years imprisonment on the robbery conviction and eight years on the home invasion conviction. On appeal, he claimed that the home invasion statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12 -11 (1979), was unconstitutional because it did not include an element of felonious intent at the time of entry. The court held that because the issue was raised for the first time on appeal, it was not preserved for appellate review. The court further held that in light of the fact that there was no constitutional provision requiring the legislature to include criminal intent at the time of entry in the offense of home invasion, the issue was not reviewable for plain error. The court also held that the trial court properly considered the extent of the victim's injuries in imposing sentence on defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences.

 

1536 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Albaugh v. Cooley


No. 78-422


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


88 Ill. App. 3d 320; 410 N.E.2d 873; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 4316; 43 Ill. Dec. 740



October 8, 1980, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 88 Ill. App. 3d 320 at 336.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Opinion of May 28, 1980, Reported at 88 Ill. App. 3d 320.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a petition for rehearing, contending that the constitutionality of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 65 (1979) was not necessary to the decision on appeal and requesting remand to the trial court.


OVERVIEW: The court found that the answer to a special interrogatory was inconsistent with the general verdict, set the answer aside, and entered judgment on the verdict. In doing so, the court acted contrary to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 65 (1979), which provided that a special finding of fact controlled over an inconsistent general verdict. Defendant sought a rehearing, contending that the constitutionality of para. 65 had not been raised by the appeal, and requesting remand so that the trial court might exercise its discretion to decide what effect should be given to the general verdict. By separate order the petition was denied and one of the justices issued a supplemental opinion adhering to the reasoning set out in the original decision. In deciding to enter judgment on the general verdict, the court was required to give effect to a statute that encroached on its power or to exercise its inherent duty to protect the judicial power from encroachment. Therefore, a determination of the validity and constitutionality of para. 65 was essential to a proper determination of the issues before the court.


OUTCOME: One of the justices of the court issued a supplemental opinion in support of the denial of the petition for rehearing.

 

1537 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Shufelt v. Rockford


Nos. 79-818, 79-819 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


89 Ill. App. 3d 717; 412 N.E.2d 4; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3811; 44 Ill. Dec. 928



October 6, 1980, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 25, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County; the Hon. PHILIP G. REINHARD, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois), which dismissed plaintiff's action that was brought against defendant property owners after plaintiff fell on an allegedly defective public sidewalk. Plaintiff sought to recover under a theory of common law negligence and under an ordinance that stated "no person shall hereafter suffer or permit such nuisance to exist in the front of" one's premises.


OVERVIEW: While using a public sidewalk as a means of ingress and egress into the owners' funeral home, plaintiff fell and suffered an injury. Thereafter, plaintiff brought an action against the owners, seeking to recover under a theory of common law negligence and under an ordinance that stated "no person shall hereafter suffer or permit such nuisance to exist in the front of" one's premises. After the trial court granted the owners' motion to dismiss, plaintiff sought review. After finding that the words "suffer or permit" required proof of knowledge of the prohibited act or conduct, the court held that plaintiff had failed to state a valid cause of action based on the ordinance because plaintiff's complaint did not contain an allegation that the owners knew or should have known of the sidewalk's defect. Likewise, the court held that plaintiff had failed to state a cause of action based on the theory of common law negligence because plaintiff had failed to plead that the owners had actual notice of the defective walk or constructive notice of such facts and circumstances as would lead a reasonably prudent person to such knowledge.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1538 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Streif v. Bovinette


No. 79-179


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


88 Ill. App. 3d 1079; 411 N.E.2d 341; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3694; 44 Ill. Dec. 372



October 2, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County; the Hon. WILLIAM B. STARNES, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant neighbor appealed an order from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois), which entered a preliminary injunction preventing him from harassing plaintiff bus company president in any manner as described in the complaint and from interfering in any way with plaintiff's use and enjoyment of his property rights and his business operations. Defendant was specifically enjoined from making spurious complaints to governmental agencies.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff bus company president alleged that defendant neighbor engaged in various actions that interfered with his business. Defendant sent allegedly unwarranted letters of complaint to state agencies, accusing plaintiff of violations of various regulations. On numerous occasions, the parties contacted the police. Finding that most of defendant's complaints were without merit and that his actions constituted a nuisance, the circuit court entered a preliminary injunction. Defendant sought review. The order was reversed and the injunction was dissolved. The court held that the case was complicated because the alleged disparagement was communicated to government rather than the public, and defendant was not a commercial competitor. The portion of the order that enjoined defendant from annoying or harassing plaintiff as described in the complaint was improperly broad and imprecise under case law and the Injunction Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 69, para. 3 (1977). The remaining portions of the injunction, which stated that defendant could not interfere in any way with plaintiffs' use and enjoyment of their property rights and business operations, also lacked specificity.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's order and dissolved a preliminary injunction. The injunction, which prevented defendant neighbor from making spurious complaints to governmental agencies concerning plaintiff's bus company, lacked specificity. While the court agreed that defendant's actions were harassment, it could not let stand an order enjoining future acts based upon what was by definition merely a preliminary determination of fact.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizens challenged an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted a motion by appellees, county and officials, to dismiss appellants' motion for a determination of the propriety of the class action, in an action by appellants challenging the constitutionality of the Real Estate Transfer Tax, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, par. 1003 (1978).


OVERVIEW: Appellant citizens, as individuals and as representatives of a class, brought an action against appellees, county and officials, challenging the constitutionality of the Real Estate Transfer Tax, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, par. 1003 (1978) and also filed a motion for a determination of the propriety of a class action. The trial court denied the motion for a determination of the propriety of the class action, reversed and remanded its prior order granting an injunction, and granted appellees' motion to dismiss appellants' complaint. People v. Mau


No. 80-107


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


88 Ill. App. 3d 924; 411 N.E.2d 323; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3671; 44 Ill. Dec. 354



September 29, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Will County; the Hon. CHARLES P. CONNOR, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of conviction from the Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois), which convicted him of armed robbery and sentenced him to six years in prison.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted defendant of armed robbery and sentenced him to six years in prison. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment of conviction. The court held that defendant's case did not warrant the reduction of the degree of the offense. The court held that there was no evidentiary weakness upon which it could rely in reducing the degree of the offense. Further, the court held that the armed robbery statute's six-year mandatory minimum term of imprisonment was not unconstitutional as applied to defendant. It held that considering the seriousness of the crime of armed robbery and the dangers inherent in the commission of that offense, the moral sense of the community was not offended by a six-year minimum term for armed robbery, even though defendant had no prior felony convictions and had some psychological and drug abuse problems.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment of conviction against defendant for armed robbery, and it sentenced him to six years in prison.

People v. Pleasant


No. 79-936


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


88 Ill. App. 3d 984; 411 N.E.2d 132; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3681; 44 Ill. Dec. 226



September 29, 1980, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 27, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Peoria County; the Hon. ROBERT E. MANNING, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment from the Circuit Court of Peoria County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of rape pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11-1(a) (1977), and of deviate sexual assault pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11-3(a) (1977).


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction on the grounds that his written confession should have been suppressed because his right to remain silent had not been scrupulously honored and that he was denied a fair trial as the result of prosecutorial misconduct. On appeal, the court affirmed the convictions, holding that the trial court properly denied the motion to suppress. The court found that defendant's right to remain silent had been scrupulously honored because there had been a complete cessation of questioning for about one and one-half hours and because defendant was asked whether he recalled the Miranda warnings recited earlier prior to reinterrogation. The court found that the officer's asking whether defendant he recalled the previous warnings was a sufficient opportunity for defendant to exercise his right if he so chose. Concerning defendant's contention that he was denied a fair trial, the court found that the prosecution did not misstate the testimony of defendant's expert witness and that the prosecution's comments during closing argument were reasonable inferences drawn from the testimony. The court also found that other allegedly prejudicial comments had been cured.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for rape and deviate sexual assault.

People v. Rembert


No. 79-821


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


89 Ill. App. 3d 371; 411 N.E.2d 996; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3762; 44 Ill. Dec. 630



September 29, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. HOWARD M. MILLER, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a decision from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted defendant's motion to quash his arrest and suppress physical evidence, oral statements and a lineup identification pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110A, para. 604 (a)(1)(1979), in the State's charge against him for armed robbery, burglary, and armed violence in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 18-2, para. 19-1, and para. 33A-2 (1977).


OVERVIEW: Following a robbery at a local hotel, a police informant directed police officers to defendant's residence, where the officers attempted for 45 minutes to gain access to the resident and then finally broke down the door and entered with force. Defendant was arrested and charged with armed robbery, burglary, and armed violence. Defendant filed a motion to quash his arrest and suppress physical evidence, oral statements, and his lineup identification. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which quashed defendant's arrest and suppressed the physical evidence, the lineup identification, and the oral statements of defendant as products of the illegal arrest.

People v. Lenninger


No. 79-202


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


88 Ill. App. 3d 801; 410 N.E.2d 1157; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3659; 44 Ill. Dec. 65



September 24, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Ogle County; the Hon. JOHN L. MOORE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Ogle County (Illinois), which convicted him of cruelty to children and sentenced him to an extended term of six years of imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: The trial court denied defendant's post-trial motion in which he requested the trial court to modify or reconsider the sentence imposed by it, asserting that imposition of an extended term of six years of imprisonment was an abuse of discretion. On appeal, defendant raised other issues. The court determined that where a claim of error had not been preserved by means other than the post-trial motion, the court could only review it under the plain error doctrine. The court explained that the information was sufficient because it apprised defendant of the offense with which he was charged with sufficient specificity to enable him to prepare his defense and to allow pleading a resultant conviction as a bar to a subsequent prosecution arising from the same conduct. The court concluded that the sentence had to be vacated on the ground that the trial court did not find that the offense was accompanied by exceptionally brutal or heinous behavior indicative of wanton cruelty as was provided in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-5-3.2(b)(2) (Supp. 1978) and/or that defendant had been convicted of a prior felony as was provided in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-5-3.2(b)(1).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction, vacated the sentence, and remanded the cause for a new sentencing hearing.

Polyvend, Inc. v. Puckorius


No. 79-797


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


88 Ill. App. 3d 778; 411 N.E.2d 316; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3655; 44 Ill. Dec. 347



September 19, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. RICHARD L. CURRY, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the Director of the Department of Administrative Services and others, appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted plaintiff manufacturer's motion for judgment on the pleadings and which denied defendants' motion for summary judgment in the manufacturer's declaratory judgment action. The manufacturer sought the right to bid for and be awarded the job of making the Illinois license plates.


OVERVIEW: The manufacturer's prior owner was convicted of bribing a state official, and all charges against the manufacturer, as a company, were dropped. The manufacturer changed its name and merged with a subsidiary. After the prior owner died, the manufacturer was invited to bid for a contract to produce license plates. The manufacturer submitted the lowest bid, but defendants rejected the bid on the sole ground that § 10.1 of the Illinois Purchasing Act forbade the awarding of contracts to the manufacturer because of its prior owner's conviction of bribery. The manufacturer filed a declaratory judgment action against defendants, and the trial court entered a judgment for the manufacturer. The court reversed the trial court's judgment. The court found that § 10.1 permanently barred the state from awarding the manufacturer contracts because the statute spoke in clear and unambiguous terms that no "person or business entity shall be awarded a contract." The court noted that there were no limitations to § 10.1. The court held that once the prior owner's act was chargeable to the manufacturer, the prior owner's death became meaningless for the purposes of the application of § 10.1.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment that was in favor of the manufacturer.

People v. Pierce


No. 79-395


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


88 Ill. App. 3d 1095; 411 N.E.2d 295; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3696; 44 Ill. Dec. 326



September 19, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County; the Hon. JOHN J. HOBAN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois), which granted defendant's motion to suppress his confession. The state claimed that the exclusionary rule was improperly applied to exclude a confession that was not the result of police misconduct and to hold a prior search improper.


OVERVIEW: The trial court granted defendant's motion to suppress his confession because it found that defendant's statement would not have been made but for the police officers' display of stolen items found in defendant's car as a result of an unlawful search with an invalid search warrant. The state sought review. The court reversed the trial court's order and remanded the case for further proceedings because it found that: 1) there was no conscious or flagrant police misconduct; 2) the police had sufficient evidence that was legally obtained to provide an independent basis for the discovery of the challenged evidence; 3) a valid arrest occurred immediately after the search; 4) the stolen items were excluded from evidence; 5) Miranda warnings were given; 6) the threshold requirement of the voluntariness of defendant's statements and their truth were admitted by defendant; and 7) the statements were acts of free will and were unaffected by the prior search.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order granting the defendant's motion to suppress his confession and remanded the case for further proceedings.

Champaign v. Kroger Co.


No. 15946


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


88 Ill. App. 3d 498; 410 N.E.2d 661; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3619; 43 Ill. Dec. 661



September 18, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Champaign County; the Hon. CREED D. TUCKER, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee City filed an action against appellant company seeking injunctive relief and damages based on the company's failure to comply with an ordinance governing the erection and size of signs. The Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois) enjoined the company from using the signs in question. The company challenged the circuit court's order claiming multiple assignments of error.


OVERVIEW: On appeal the company argued that the city's ordinance regulating the size of signs was an unreasonable restriction on the company's use of its property. The court rejected the company's argument holding that the ordinance was reasonably related to a legitimate purpose. The court found that the ordinance was reasonably related to the trinity of public health, safety, and welfare. The company argued that the ordinance was related to achieving aesthetic purposes only and was therefore invalid. The court rejected this argument holding that aesthetics was an element of the public health, safety, and welfare. The court reasoned that the welfare of a community included its appearance and, therefore, municipalities could enact zoning laws regulating the dimensions of commercial signs. Finally, the court found that the company's other arguments were without merit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that enjoined the company from using the signs in question.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of attempted murder under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 8--4.


OVERVIEW: Defendant shot an undercover officer in the head during a traffic dispute. Defendant was convicted of attempted murder under para. 8--4, and the court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court held that the trial court properly denied defendant's motion for change of venue and reassignment because the establishment of special courts for recidivist cases was constitutional. The court found that disclosure of the actual sentences to be imposed under a statute that was effective at the time of the crime and one that was effective at the time of trial was not required for an intelligent election between the two sentencing codes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment against defendant.

Sanner v. Champaign County


No. 16206


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


88 Ill. App. 3d 491; 410 N.E.2d 656; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3618; 43 Ill. Dec. 656



September 17, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Champaign County; the Hon. ROBERT J. STEIGMANN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff probationers appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), which allowed defendant county's motion to dismiss the probationers' challenge to the probation procedures of § 10 of the Cannabis Control Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2 para. 710 (1977), and of § 410 of the Controlled Substances Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1410 (1977).


OVERVIEW: Under § 10 of the Cannabis Control Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2 para. 710 (1977), and of § 410 of the Controlled Substances Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1410 (1977), persons found guilty of a first offense might be placed on a special type of probation. A judgment of guilty was not entered unless the person subsequently violated the terms of the probation. The probationers sought reimbursement for fines and costs that they were required to pay as a condition of their probations. The General Assembly amended § 10 and § 410 expressly to authorize the requirement that a defendant pay fines and costs as a condition of probation. The circuit court found that the amendments were retrospective. The court considered various factors in affirming that the amendments should have a retrospective application. Additionally, the court held that the probationers' complaint sought equitable relief. The complaint gave no indication that such a remedy at law was sought or that it would be inadequate. Probationers should have objected to the fine and costs requirement and appealed that order.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that the probationers' complaint against the county failed to state a cause of action.

 

1550 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Jones


No. 79-889


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


88 Ill. App. 3d 737; 410 N.E.2d 1106; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3648; 44 Ill. Dec. 14



September 17, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Kankakee County; the Hon. PATRICK BURNS, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Kankakee County (Illinois), which convicted him of aggravated battery. Defendant claimed that his guilty plea must be vacated because the prosecutor reneged on his promise to recommend a term of probation. Defendant also claimed unconstitutional the statute allowing for the application of his bail bond deposit to reimburse the county for the expenses of the public defender.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated battery and appealed his conviction. On appeal, the court rejected defendant's argument that his guilty plea must be vacated because the prosecutor reneged on his promise to recommend a term of probation. The court found that defendant did not raise this issue at trial and further found that it could not decide the issue under the plain error doctrine because there was no error. The prosecutor kept his promise to recommend the sentence that was agreed upon by the parties, but the lower court chose to impose a higher sentence based on a prior conviction. This did not render defendant's guilty plea involuntary because the trial court was not bound to accept the recommendation of the prosecutor. As for defendant's argument regarding the application of his bail bond deposit to reimburse the county for expenses incurred by the public defender, the court found that the governing statute was recently declared unconstitutional. The court reversed the order of recoupment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the lower court denying the vacation of defendant's guilty plea. The court reversed the lower court's order of recoupment requiring application of defendant's bail bond deposit to reimburse the county for expenses incurred by the public defender in representing defendant.

People v. Meyer

88 Ill. App. 3d 965; 411 N.E.2d 75; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3677; 44 Ill. Dec. 169



September 17, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Madison County; the Hon. P. J. O'NEILL, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Madison County (Illinois) convicted defendant of unlawfully operating a snowmobile on a state highway in violation of the Snowmobile Registration and Safety Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 605/2 (1979). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant drove his snowmobile on a state highway. Defendant alleged that the Snowmobile Registration and Safety Act violated the United States Commerce Clause, U.S. Const., art. I, § 8 and imposed an unfair burden on intrastate commerce in violation of the Fourteenth Amendment's due process clause. The court held that The Snowmobile Registration and Safety Act was a proper exercise of the legislative power of the Illinois Legislature and was constitutional. Although the Act generally prohibited a snowmobile's use on the busiest roadways, the Act allowed certain exceptions where a snowmobile was likely to encounter fewer traffic hazards. There was a reasonable relationship between the Act's limitation on snowmobile access to state highways and the safety of persons and property connected with the use of snowmobiles.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court.

People v. Lewis


No. 79-1138


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


89 Ill. App. 3d 15; 410 N.E.2d 1047; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3701; 43 Ill. Dec. 914



September 16, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. FRANCIS J. MAHON, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of voluntary manslaughter. Defendant asserted that his sentence was excessive and claimed that under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-5-4.1 (1979), the sentence could be reduced if he made an affirmative showing that it had been erroneous.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of voluntary manslaughter. Defendant claimed that he received an excessive sentence and asserted that pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-5-4.1 (1979), he was entitled to have his sentence reduced if he made an affirmative showing that his sentence was erroneous. The court affirmed defendant's sentence. Although there was some controversy over the appropriate standard of review concerning the trial court's sentence, the court found that the trial court's decision would be upheld no matter which standard of review was employed. The court noted that this matter implicated some constitutional concerns, but because those matters were not critical for the resolution of the proceeding, it chose to pass judgment thereon.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's sentence.

Leu v. Illinois Dep't of Registration & Education


No. 79-1046


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


88 Ill. App. 3d 255; 410 N.E.2d 467; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3581; 43 Ill. Dec. 467



September 8, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. RICHARD L. CURRY, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant doctor sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which affirmed an order of appellee Department of Registration and Education, which revoked doctor's license to practice medicine based upon the fact that doctor was convicted of a felony, pursuant to the Medical Practice Act.


OVERVIEW: Doctor was convicted of improperly dispensing controlled substances. Pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111, para. 4433(2) (1977), Department of Regulation and Education revoked his license to practice medicine. The trial court affirmed an order of Department of Regulation and Education, and doctor sought review. Pursuant to the Medical Practice Act, at any time after such revocation, Department of Regulation and Education was entitled to reinstate or take other action. The court held that the findings of an administrative agency were prima facie correct if there was substantive evidence to support the decision. The court held that the Department of Regulation and Education was not required to automatically restore doctor's license and was only required to restore it if after investigation and hearing said restoration was not contrary to public interest. The court held that the evidence supported the Department of Regulation and Education's decision not to restore doctor's license. The court affirmed an order of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed an order of the trial court, which affirmed an order of Department of Regulation and Education revoking doctor's license after he was convicted of improperly dispensing controlled substances. The court held that, under the Medical Practice Act, Department of Regulation and Education was not required to automatically restore said license if after investigation it was deemed that restoration was contrary to public interest.

People v. G.B. (In re G.B.)


No. 16053


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


88 Ill. App. 3d 64; 410 N.E.2d 410; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3552; 43 Ill. Dec. 410



September 2, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Champaign County; the Hon. ROBERT J. STEIGMANN and the Hon. JOHN R. DeLAMAR, Judges, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision by the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), which placed appellant on probation subject to 60 days' incarceration and the payment of costs for violating a criminal contempt probation order based on appellant's continued truancy.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was ordered to attend school under supervision after a finding of habitual truancy. When appellant violated the supervision order, the trial court found him in criminal contempt and placed him on probation with conditions including incarceration. The trial court later found a probation violation and placed appellant on continued probation subject to 60 days' incarceration. The trial court denied appellant's petition to dismiss the contempt petition on the ground that the trial court lacked jurisdiction to impose the original probation and therefore could not punish appellant for violating the probation order. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's second probation order and remanded, holding that it was an abuse of discretion to place appellant on probation. The court noted that the trial court had jurisdiction to place a criminal contemnor on probation, but concluded that the trial court's second probation order was inappropriate and that the incarceration in a detention facility was sufficiently severe to approach the outer limits of that which could be upheld upon review.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order placing appellant on probation for the second time and remanded the cause for further proceedings.

People v. Marion


No. 79-952


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


87 Ill. App. 3d 1038; 409 N.E.2d 533; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3523; 42 Ill. Dec. 918



August 29, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Will County; the Hon. CHARLES P. CONNOR, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction by the Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois), for the unlawful possession of less than 30 grams of a substance containing LSD.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of the unlawful possession of less than 30 grams of a substance containing LSD Upon appeal, the court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court held that there was direct evidence of defendant's guilt. He was seen holding a packet and was subsequently observed to make a motion as though he was throwing something away. Immediately thereafter a packet containing LSD was found at the very point toward which defendant had made the motion, and that packet was introduced into evidence. This was direct evidence requiring the giving of only the first paragraph of Ill. Pattern Jury Instructions [Crim.] No. 3.02. The court reversed that portion of the judgment, which directed that defendant pay the costs of his court-appointed counsel from his cash bail deposit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part defendant's conviction for the unlawful possession of less than 30 grams of a substance containing LSD.

 

1556 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Chicago v. Festival Theatre Corp.


No. 79-445


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


88 Ill. App. 3d 216; 410 N.E.2d 341; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3577; 43 Ill. Dec. 341



August 29, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. ARCHIBALD J. CAREY, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city brought an action in equity against defendants, theater and operator (theater), to enjoin the theater from performing a show in which actual or simulated acts of sexual intercourse, fellatio, cunnilingus, and masturbation were performed on stage before and adult audience. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) found the shows to be a public nuisance and enjoined the performances. The theater appealed the order.


OVERVIEW: The theater claimed that the injunction violated the First Amendment. The court reversed the order. To determine whether a state's obscenity laws were constitutional, a trier of fact had to determine whether the average person, applying contemporary community standards, found the work, taken as a whole, appealed to prurient interests; whether the work depicted or described in a patently offensive way sexual conduct specifically defined in the state's law; and whether the work, taken as a whole, had any literary, artistic, political, or scientific value. Obscenity was not enjoinable as a public nuisance under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 100 1/2, para. 1 (1977). Obscenity was not enjoinable as conduct which offended public morals and decency under common law public nuisance. Thus, the injunction against the theater offended the First Amendment. The injunction prohibited the performance of certain physical acts inside the theater. Because the trial court did not see future shows containing those acts, it did not know the content of those shows. It was possible that such future shows would neither appeal to prurient interests nor lack serious literary, political, artistic, or scientific value.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that enjoined the theater from performing specific live actual or simulated sexual acts.

 

1557 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Kotche v. County Bd. of Winnebago County


No. 79-464


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


87 Ill. App. 3d 1127; 409 N.E.2d 501; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3538; 42 Ill. Dec. 886



August 28, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County; the Hon. ROBERT GILL, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The circuit court clerk (clerk) sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois), which granted defendant Board of Winnebago County (county) summary judgment and held that the clerk's office was subject to the county's control including turning over fees, hiring, job classifications, and other internal operations.


OVERVIEW: The clerk contended that deposit of fee statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 85, para. 722(2) conflicted with the Illinois constitution and was therefore unconstitutional. The trial court found that the statute was not unconstitutional and granted the county summary judgment. On appeal, the court found that the deposit of fees statute was constitutional. The court reasoned that the constitution empowered the Illinois General Assembly to provide by law for the appointment and election of clerks and other non-judicial officers of the court. The court found that this constitutional provision permitted requiring nonjudicial officers to pay all of their fee income into the county treasury, and court affirmed the trial court's granting of summary judgment to the county on the issue of the deposit of funds. The court reversed the trial court's judgment concerning internal operations, including hiring, firing, classification and remuneration. The court found that the actions by the board regarding the remuneration and reclassification of employees were not within the board's budgetary and statutory authority pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 25, para.27.3 (1977).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's granting of summary judgment to the county on the issue of the deposit of funds, and reversed the trial court's judgment concerning internal operations, including hiring, firing, classification, and remuneration.

 

1558 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Gray


No. 79-465


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


87 Ill. App. 3d 142; 408 N.E.2d 1150; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3392; 42 Ill. Dec. 441



August 8, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. DWIGHT McKAY, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed her convictions, entered by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), for murder, rape, and perjury, and her extended sentences.


OVERVIEW: Defendant testified before a grand jury that she had been instructed by a co-defendant to hold a lighter in a dark room so that her co-defendants could see what they were doing while they raped one victim multiple times before murdering her. Defendant then witnessed the murder of a second victim. At a preliminary hearing and at trial, defendant recanted her grand jury testimony. Defendant was convicted of murder, rape, and perjury and was sentenced to extended terms. Defendant appealed, but the court affirmed. The court held that the evidence was sufficient to establish defendant's specific intent to promote or facilitate the crimes. The court further held that the evidence revealed no attempt by defendant to leave; thus, she did not present a viable defense of compulsion. Because she did not raise the issue of her attorney's alleged conflict of interest and defendant had no proof that an actual conflict existed, the court rejected defendant's claim that her right to counsel was violated. Finally, the court ruled that the offense, not defendant's participation in it, was the determining factor which made her extended term sentence proper.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentences were affirmed.

People v. Tellery


No. 79-667


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


87 Ill. App. 3d 298; 409 N.E.2d 32; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3412; 42 Ill. Dec. 537



July 29, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. THOMAS CAWLEY, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review from an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which found him guilty of attempted murder, armed robbery, and aggravated battery and sentenced him to two concurrent terms of 10 to 12 years on the attempted murder and armed robbery convictions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and four other armed men entered the victim's scrap metal warehouse and took money from his wallet. While the robbers searched the warehouse, the victim made his way out of the front door and to an intersection in the street, where he was subsequently shot. Defendant was found guilty of attempted murder, armed robbery, robbery, and aggravated battery and sentenced to two concurrent sentences of 10 to 12 years. On appeal, the court held that defendant lacked standing to challenge the constitutional validity of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-4(a) (1975), the aggravated battery statute, as there was no contention that the alleged infirmity rendered the entire act invalid. The court found that although the jury was instructed and returned a verdict on the charge of aggravated battery, neither judgment nor sentence was entered on the jury's verdict, and therefore defendant was not convicted under the challenged provision, nor had he suffered any prejudice. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion when it refused to tender an instruction on inconsistent witness statements, and affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order from the trial court.

Scandroli v. Rockford

Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District

People v. Wilson


No. 79-69


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


86 Ill. App. 3d 637; 408 N.E.2d 988; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3289; 42 Ill. Dec. 279



July 24, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. LLOYD A. VAN DEUSEN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of possession of 1.65 grams of a controlled substance, in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56-1/2, para. 1402(b) (1977), following a bench trial in the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois). Defendant sought review of his conviction.


OVERVIEW: The police received a call from a hotel manager that a lamp had been stolen from a room and that other suspicious activities had taken place in the room. Two officers responded to the call and a hotel security guard escorted them to the room. The guard used his pass key to partially open the door. One of the officers then stepped into the doorway. He observed defendant move off of a bed and towards the bathroom. The officer pushed the door open and pursued defendant into the bathroom, where the officer retrieved a plastic bag containing five foil packets. Defendant was arrested and later convicted of possession of a controlled substance. The court reversed defendant's conviction, holding that while the officer had probable cause to arrest defendant for the theft of the lamp, the warrantless entry violated U.S. Const. amend. IV because there were no exigent circumstances justifying the entry. The court noted that the officers had ample time to secure an arrest warrant and that there was no evidence that the delay occasioned by the securing of a warrant would have impeded the apprehension of the suspects. The court thus found that the contraband should have been suppressed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for possession of a controlled substance.

 

1562 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Wills v. O'Grady


No. 79-1429


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


86 Ill. App. 3d 775; 409 N.E.2d 17; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3310; 42 Ill. Dec. 522



July 24, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. RICHARD L. CURRY, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff nudist appealed a decision from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed the nudist's first amended complaint in which he sought a declaratory judgment that certain state statutes and Chicago municipal ordinances would be unconstitutional if applied to his intended conduct of sunbathing nude at public beaches in Chicago and elsewhere in Illinois.


OVERVIEW: The nudist filed a declaratory judgment action, which sought to declare that certain state statutes and municipal ordinances were unconstitutional if applied to his intended conduct of sunbathing nude at public beaches. The trial court dismissed the nudist's amended complaint, and the nudist appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision of the trial court. The court held that the nudist failed to allege facts to show an actual, concrete controversy. The court found that the two instances, for which the nudist was actually arrested and prosecuted, concerned activities in or about his home and not for nude sunbathing at a public beach. Moreover, those activities occurred several years prior to the filing of the action. The court found that the nudist pointed to one isolated incident where he was threatened with arrest for disorderly conduct, but there was no allegation that if he repeated the behavior he would actually face the threat of prosecution and arrest. The court held that the nudist failed to establish a clear controversy with an immediate threat of injury. His case depended on speculative events in the future. Thus, the dismissal was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which dismissed the nudist's amended complaint for a declaratory judgment that sought to declare that certain statutes and ordinances were unconstitutional if applied to his sunbathing nude at public beaches.

People v. Swihart


No. 16015


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


86 Ill. App. 3d 151; 407 N.E.2d 1129; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3221; 41 Ill. Dec. 631



July 15, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Champaign County; the Hon. HARRY E. CLEM, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), which convicted him of resisting or obstructing a police officer. Defendant was sentenced to 90 days' imprisonment and assessed costs of $ 250 for services provided by the public defender.


OVERVIEW: Defendant served 55 of the 90 days imprisonment before the court granted defendant an appeal bond. The court found that defendant was properly advised of the potential sentence at the arraignment hearing. Further, once defendant waived his right to counsel, there was no reason to assume it had been revoked. Moreover, because a public defender who had represented defendant at an earlier stage had fully informed defendant of potential penalties, any error was harmless. Additionally in view of the substantial resistance which police officers encountered, and the fact that the sentence is far below the 364-day maximum sentence, the court was unable to say that defendant's sentence was an abuse of discretion. Finally, however, the order remitting the $ 250 to the county to defray the expenses of the public defendant was reversed because Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 110-7(g) violated equal protection and due process guarantees of both the State and federal constitutions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence. But, the order for defendant to remit $ 250 to defray the cost of the public defender's services was reversed.

People v. Willey


No. 79-938


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


85 Ill. App. 3d 749; 407 N.E.2d 1115; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3129; 41 Ill. Dec. 617



July 14, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of McDonough County; the Hon. CHARLES H. WILHELM, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of McDonough County (Illinois), which, following a jury trial, convicted him of burglary, the unlawful use of weapons, criminal damage to property, aggravated assault, and battery. Defendant was sentenced to a three-year term of imprisonment for burglary and concurrent terms of 364 days for the other offenses.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his brother were tried and convicted of various offenses. When they were first charged by information, a public defender was appointed to represent them, but subsequently they retained private counsel, with one attorney to represent both defendant and his brother. The public defender withdrew and was granted an order directing the circuit clerk to make payable to the public defender's reimbursement fund a check to be noted against the bonds of defendant and his brother. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded, holding that: (1) although the statute allowing reimbursement to the public defender, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 110-7(g) (1978), was unconstitutional, reimbursement based upon quasi-contract or a contract implied in law was required in the instant case; (2) defendant was denied the effective assistance of counsel because one attorney's representation of both him and his brother was a conflict of interest; and (3) there was no merit to defendant's contention that he was not proven guilty beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and the cause remanded for a new trial.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Henry County (Illinois), which convicted him of armed violence, attempt murder, aggravated battery, and battery. He was sentenced on the armed violence conviction to a determinate term of imprisonment of six years.


OVERVIEW: Following a shooting incident at a tavern, defendant was charged by information with armed violence, attempt murder, and aggravated battery. After a jury trial, he was convicted of those offenses and was sentenced on the armed violence conviction to a determinate term of imprisonment of six years. OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence entered by the trial court were affirmed.

People v. Bullis


No. 79-911


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


85 Ill. App. 3d 693; 407 N.E.2d 1100; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3119; 41 Ill. Dec. 602



July 10, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kankakee County; the Hon. JOHN F. MICHELA, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Kankakee County (Illinois), which granted defendant's motion to withdraw her guilty plea and to dismiss the information. Defendant had entered a negotiated plea of guilty to unlawful possession of a controlled substance in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1210(b)(7) (1977).


OVERVIEW: In exchange for her plea of guilty the State dismissed two other counts of possession of controlled substances and also recommended probation. Subsequent to her plea and sentence the State courts determined that the statutory section under which defendant had been convicted, Section 402(b) of the Controlled Substances Act, Ill. Rev. The court noted that waiver was particularly appropriate because the question of the validity and viability of the charge against defendant was a question that the defense quite understandably would have been able to contest below. The court noted that the State would have been free to reinstate the dismissed counts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment.

July 7, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. ALFRED E. WOODWARD, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which, on remand, had resentenced defendant for his conviction of forgery and two counts of attempt theft. Defendant claimed that on remand, he was entitled to be sentenced under the provisions of the Unified Code of Corrections, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-8-1 et seq., rather than the law that was in effect at the date of his initial sentencing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of forgery and two counts of attempt theft in connection with defendant's opening up of a checking account and writing checks he new would not be honored and for forging a check. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-8-4(a).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Helvey v. Rednour


No. 79-145


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


86 Ill. App. 3d 154; 408 N.E.2d 17; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3222; 41 Ill. Dec. 671



July 7, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jackson County; the Hon. RICHARD E. RICHMAN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Jackson County (Illinois) certified a question of law for interlocutory appeal arising out of an action brought by petitioners, perspective adoptive parents, to adopt the minor child of respondent parents pursuant to the Adoption Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 1501 et seq. (1977). The court had appointed a guardian ad litem for respondent mother, who was mentally retarded, with the authority to consent to the adoption.


OVERVIEW: Perspective adoptive parents brought an action to adopt the parents' minor child pursuant to the Adoption Act (act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 1501 et seq. (1977). The child's mother was adjudged mentally retarded, and the trial court appointed a guardian ad litem for her with the authority to consent to the adoption under § 8, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 1510 (1977), of the act. The trial court stayed the proceedings and certified a question for the court regarding the constitutionality of the act. The court reversed the appointment of a guardian ad litem for the mother and remanded the case, holding that § 8 of the act, so far as it pertained to the appointment of a guardian ad litem with power to consent to adoption for a mentally retarded parent, without a hearing to determine whether the parent was unfit, violated the Equal Protection and Due Process clauses of the Fourteenth Amendment of the United States Constitution as well as Ill. Const. art. 1, § 2. The court noted that although an adjudication that a parent was mentally retarded may not have in and of itself rendered that parent unfit, evidence of such adjudication could have been considered in determining fitness.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appointment of a guardian ad litem for the mother and remanded the cause for a fitness hearing.

 

1569 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Peoria v. O'Connor


No. 79-465


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


85 Ill. App. 3d 427; 408 N.E.2d 11; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3077; 41 Ill. Dec. 665



June 27, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Peoria County; the Hon. STEPHEN COVEY, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, county and county collector, appealed from the decision of the Circuit Court of Peoria County (Illinois), which permanently enjoined them from modifying taxpaying methods. Plaintiffs, town and township collector appealed from that part of the trial court's order directing them to distribute interest earned on investment of tax proceeds to the county in the plaintiffs' injunctive action against the defendants.


OVERVIEW: The county modified the method in which taxpayers could have paid their bills. The town and the township collector filed suit against the county, county treasurer and ex-officio county collector seeking a declaratory judgment and a permanent injunction enjoining the county collector from collecting real property taxes prior to September 1 of any collection year. The trial court issued a preliminary injunction and the defendants counterclaimed, alleging that neither the town nor its collector had statutory authority to invest the proceeds of the real estate taxes collected. The trial court permanently enjoined defendants from collecting real property taxes under the new method and directed the distribution of interest earned by the town collector on invested tax proceeds to the county and credited to the county treasury. The parties cross-appealed. The court held that the town and the collector were entitled to retain the interest earned on the investment of tax proceeds and had the authority to invest tax proceeds. The court found that the powers of tax collectors to have invested were conferred upon them by the Revenue Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 36, para. 22.2 (1977).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that part of the trial court's decision that permanently enjoined the county and county collector from proceeding to collect real property taxes under their new resolution. The court affirmed the holding of the trial court that the town collector had the authority to invest tax proceeds. The court held that the town and town collector were entitled to retain the interest earned on the investment of tax proceeds.

 

1570 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Rasky v. Department of Registration & Education


No. 79-334


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


87 Ill. App. 3d 580; 410 N.E.2d 69; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3454; 43 Ill. Dec. 69



June 27, 1980, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 12, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. ARTHUR L. DUNNE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff real estate broker sought review of the judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which affirmed defendant department's revocation of the real estate broker's license pursuant to § 15(e)(11), (12) of the Real Estate Brokers and Salesmen License Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 114 1/2, para. 115(e)(11), (21) (1975).


OVERVIEW: The department issued a complaint against the real estate broker setting forth a number of conditions existing in apartment buildings owned and operated by him that were in violation of the city health code and endangered the inhabitants. Consequently, the department revoked the real estate broker's license, and the circuit court affirmed the revocation. On appeal, the court also affirmed the revocation. The court concluded that the § 15 of the Act did not unconstitutionally delegate judicial power to the department because the decision to revoke a license concerned the competency of an individual to practice the profession rather than a judgment that his conduct was illegal. The complaint against the real estate broker gave him reasonable notice of the charges against him. There was sufficient evidence to support the fact that the poor conditions existed in the apartments, and the evidence did not clearly direct another conclusion. Additionally, the revocation of the real estate broker's license was not a criminal sanction and the Eighth Amendment did not apply.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court, upholding the revocation of the real estate broker's license.

In re Application of Rosewell


No. 78-1818


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


86 Ill. App. 3d 117; 407 N.E.2d 924; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3216; 41 Ill. Dec. 426



June 26, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. ROBERT J. DEMPSEY, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant company disputed judgments by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which overruled its objections to a quadrennial tax assessment and several yearly assessments on a steelmaking plant. The court considered, inter alia, its standard of review, whether the assessment procedure complied with the Illinois Revenue Act of 1939 (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 482 et seq. (1971), and whether the company's appraisals were valid.


OVERVIEW: In contesting the assessments, the company offered appraisal reports prepared by an independent organization, which reports were based on the reproduction cost of a model replacement plant. In its rulings, the trial court had "corrected" the appraisals. On appeal, the court noted that it had no power to review the tax valuations, which had been fixed by the appropriate officers, in the absence of a showing of actual or constructive fraud. The court held that the assessment procedure complied with the Act. The Act did not require the assessor to determine full value before determining assessed value, and the assessor did determine the full value. Reviewing them one by one, the court held that none of the trial court's corrections of the company's appraisal reports was erroneous. Given that holding, the court did not have to address the company's argument that the assessments violated Ill. Const. of 1970, art. IX, § 4(b). In light of the trial court's sound reasons for applying a "rule of reason" to the assessments rather than a per se rule, the court could not say that the company had proved by clear and convincing evidence that the trial court erred. The court affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments by the trial court overruling the company's objections to the tax assessments.

 

1572 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Rent-A-Sign v. Rockford


No. 79-153


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


85 Ill. App. 3d 453; 406 N.E.2d 943; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3081; 40 Ill. Dec. 740



June 25, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County; the Hon. PHILLIP G. REINHARD, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois), which found that Rockford, Ill., Sign Ordinance §§ 3-76(a) and (d) unfairly discriminated against mobile signs and entered an order permanently enjoining enforcement of those subsections, but upheld the general validity of the ordinance. Plaintiff mobile-sign rental companies cross-appealed, contending that the ordinance was void for vagueness.


OVERVIEW: The city ordinance represented a comprehensive regulatory scheme covering signs used in outdoor advertising. The trial court upheld the general validity of the ordinance but found that Rockford, Ill., Sign Ordinance §§ 3-76(a) and (d) were arbitrarily underinclusive because they did not apply to other signs that posed substantially the same safety and aesthetic problems as mobile signs. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment enjoining enforcement of those sections and affirmed the finding that the general ordinance was constitutional. The distinction between mobile signs and other types could conceivably be justified on several grounds, and arguably rested upon a legislative determination that mobile signs posed greater safety and aesthetic problems. Mobile signs were more readily moved into unauthorized locations which could have posed traffic hazards than were other types of signs, and the differential ease of enforcement was found to be a rational basis upon which to make regulatory classifications. The terms were definite enough measured by common understanding and practice, and a reasonable basis existed for treating mobile signs differently from other signs.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court enjoining enforcement of two sections of the city's sign ordinance was reversed. The judgment upholding the general validity of the ordinance was affirmed.
