In re B.


No. 79-763


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


85 Ill. App. 3d 1064; 407 N.E.2d 884; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3185; 41 Ill. Dec. 386



June 25, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. JOSEPH SCHNEIDER, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant adoptee sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed his amended petition to open sealed birth and adoption records as unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The adoptee filed a petition to review his sealed birth and adoption records. The trial court ruled that good cause was required to unseal the record. The adoptee amended his petition alleging that adulthood was in of itself good cause. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the adoptee's argument that the statute violated his right to receive information under the First Amendment was without merit because the First Amendment did not guarantee the adoptee special access to information not available to the public generally. The court ruled that, although the adoptee's interest in his records was important both socially and psychologically, the statute did not violate the adoptee's right to privacy because he failed to prove that his right to the information was explicitly or implicitly guaranteed by the constitution. The court held that the statute's requirement of a court order to view birth records did not subject the adoptee to any invidious discrimination and that the statute was fairly and substantial related to a legitimate state interest and only placed a reasonable limitation on access to the sealed records; thus, there was no violation of the Equal Protection clause.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the circuit court, which dismissed the adoptee's petition to open his sealed birth and adoption records.

People v. Thompson


No. 78-2075


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


85 Ill. App. 3d 964; 407 N.E.2d 761; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3164; 41 Ill. Dec. 263



June 18, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. JOHN J. McDONNELL, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed her conviction in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), for prostitution, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11-14(a)(1) (1977) and the sentence of a term of 30 days, asserting that (1) she was not proved guilty beyond a reasonable doubt, (2) the prostitution statute is unconstitutional, (3) she was prejudiced by the admission of testimony concerning prior offenses and (4) her sentence was excessive.


OVERVIEW: An undercover police officer placed defendant under arrest after she propositioned him. On appeal from her conviction for prostitution, the court affirmed, holding that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11-14(a) (1977) did not violate: (1) her due process rights by defining an inherently inchoate offense as a specific substantive offense; (2) her right to equal protection of the law; (3) her right to freedom of speech, or (4) Ill. Const. art. 4, § 8(d), providing that bills shall be confined to one subject. The trial court did not commit prejudicial error by admitting evidence of offenses other than the offense for which she was being tried. While questions concerning whether she and her companions were prostitutes did not contain evidence of other specific crimes and was erroneous, it did not prejudice her case. Because the evidence of her character was introduced by defendant, the trial court's refusal to sustain defendant's objections was harmless error. In view of defendant's record of five prior convictions for prostitution and one conviction for aggravated battery, and the latitude given to the trial court in sentencing, it did not abuse its discretion.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for prostitution and the sentence of a term of 30 days was affirmed.

Redemske v. Romeoville


No. 79-449


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


85 Ill. App. 3d 286; 406 N.E.2d 602; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3055; 40 Ill. Dec. 596

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant village appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois), which ordered the village to reinstate plaintiff employee to her position with the village and awarded the employee damages in the employee's action for wrongful discharge after she was terminated for participating in a political parade.


OVERVIEW: The employee was discharged after she drove an automobile in a parade through the village. The parade was in support of a candidate for village trustee in an upcoming election. The employee's discharge was based expressly upon a village ordinance authorizing the dismissal of any village employee that had taken an active part in a campaign for elective office for the village. The employee initiated a suit for wrongful discharge, and the trial court ordered the village to reinstate the employee and pay back wages. The village appealed, claiming that the ordinance serving as the basis for the discharge was constitutional and was not beyond the authority delegated to the village by the general assembly. The court affirmed, holding that the village ordinance was void for vagueness and therefore unenforceable because the language adopted therein was too broad and vague for ordinary people of common sense to understand which activities were prohibited. The court found that the village had failed to adopt an ordinance which clearly and specifically apprised its employees of which political activities on their part would be grounds for dismissal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order requiring the village to reinstate the employee and awarding the employee damages in the employee's action for wrongful discharge after she was terminated for participating in a political parade.

People v. Lucas


No. 15889


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


85 Ill. App. 3d 133; 406 N.E.2d 214; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3034; 40 Ill. Dec. 513



June 6, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Macoupin County; the Hon. JOSEPH P. KOVAL, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction in the Circuit Court of Macoupin County (Illinois) for aggravated battery. He contended that the statute under which he was given an extended term of imprisonment was unconstitutional, that the prosecutor improperly commented on his in-custody silence, and that the trial court erred in admitting a hearsay statement of the victim.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was involved in a bar fight. He sucker punched the victim. Everyone heard glass breaking before the punch but no one saw glass in defendant's hand. The victim's face was cut. When police arrived at the bar, the victim told one of them that he had been cut by glass. The victim did not say this at trial, but the police officer testified to the victim's statement. When defendant was taken into custody he was asked how he came to have blood on his hand. He said he cut his hand on a motorcycle while going over railroad tracks. He did not mention the fight or his theory at trial, self-defense. The prosecutor commented in closing argument on defendant's failure to mention self-defense during the in-custody statement. The court held that this was reversible error. Defendant was not asked about the bar fight, but about his hand. No assumption arose that defendant would explain the fight when asked only about his hand. The court did not have enough information to determine whether the victim's statement to the police officer was admissible under the spontaneous declaration exception to the hearsay rule. The court avoided the constitutional question.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded for a new trial. It gave the trial court instructions on what additional information was needed to determine whether the victim's statement to the police officer would be admissible.

Winokur v. Bakalis


No. 79-522


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


84 Ill. App. 3d 922; 405 N.E.2d 1329; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 2989; 40 Ill. Dec. 237



May 30, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. DONALD J. O'BRIEN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed his suit against appellees, state comptroller and treasurer, challenging the constitutionality of two statutes that increased the salaries of the members of the 81st General Assembly and seeking an injunction enjoining the disbursement of public funds for payment of the salaries.


OVERVIEW: The 80th General Assembly had passed two amendments to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 63, para. 14, which increased the salaries of the 81st General Assembly. The Ill. Const. of 1970, art. IV, § 11, prohibited a change in legislative salaries from taking effect during a legislative term for which the members had been elected, but had not taken office, as of the date of passage of the law. The taxpayer contended that a general election had to intervene between the adoption of the law increasing salaries and the date upon which it took effect. The court found that the action was not moot because funds were available for the granting of effectual relief to the parties. It reviewed the language in art. IV, § 11, "the term for which he has been elected," and found that it referred to the current term for which the members of the General Assembly were serving and not to their continuance in office. Thus, the change in salaries could only become effective during the next successive term of the legislature. The court concluded that the amended statutes were valid and constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Albaugh v. Cooley


No. 78-422


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


88 Ill. App. 3d 320; 410 N.E.2d 873; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3591; 43 Ill. Dec. 740



May 28, 1980, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Supplemental Opinion Filed on Denial of Rehearing October 8, 1980, Reported at 88 Ill. App. 3d 320 at 336.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. CHARLES DURHAM, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to section 65 of the Civil Practice Act, 110 Ill. Comp. Stat. 65(1977), the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) rendered judgment in favor of defendant tortfeasor on the jury's answer to the special interrogatory in plaintiff claimant's personal injury action. The claimant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The claimant was struck by the tortfeasor's automobile as the claimant was crossing a suburban street in an unmarked crosswalk. The jury returned a verdict in favor of the claimant for $ 20,000, but answered a special interrogatory finding the claimant guilty of contributory negligence. The claimant alleged that the evidence was insufficient to find contributory negligence. The tortfeasor alleged that the case was governed by 110 Ill. Comp. Stat. 65(1977) and that judgment could not be entered on the general verdict if the general verdict was inconsistent with the answer to the special interrogatory. The court reversed the trial court and held that there was insufficient evidence to substantiate a finding of contributory negligence and that 110 Comp. Stat. 65(1977) was an improper legislative infringement upon the judiciary power. The automobile was more than a half block away when the claimant started to cross the street. The legislature lacked the authority to direct the court on the rendition of judgments.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order granting judgment to the tortfeasor on the jury's answer to the special interrogatory. The court entered judgment on the general verdict in favor of the claimant.

Austin View Civic Ass'n v. City of Palos Heights


No. 79-532


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


85 Ill. App. 3d 89; 405 N.E.2d 1256; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3029; 40 Ill. Dec. 164



May 22, 1980, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 19, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. ARTHUR L. DUNNE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff nonresidents filed a class action against defendant city seeking a declaratory judgment, an injunction, and an accounting, alleging that the city discriminated against the nonresidents by charging them higher water rates and that the discrimination violated equal protection. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granted the city's motions to dismiss. The nonresidents filed an appeal.


OVERVIEW: The city enacted a water ordinance that provided that the nonresidents pay 25 percent more for water. The city filed a motion under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 45, 48(1)(i) (1977) to strike paragraphs of the complaint and to dismiss based on affirmative matter defeating the claim. On appeal, the court found that the city could have asserted that it had a rational basis for the classification scheme under § 48(1)(i) to defeat the nonresidents' claim of denial of equal protection because the nonresidents were not members of a suspect class and were not asserting the denial of a fundamental right. However, this allegation was not an affirmative matter under § 48(1)(i) because the rational basis test was not applicable to the common law right preventing unreasonable discrimination in water rates. The question of common law discrimination for a utility was always a question of fact based solely on the evidence presented. The court held that the contract alone did not establish a rational basis for the classification. It was improper for the trial court to strike certain paragraphs of the complaint because each paragraph did not have to state a complete claim.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the grant of dismissal for the city.

People v. O'Dell


No. 79-214


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


84 Ill. App. 3d 359; 405 N.E.2d 809; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 2900; 39 Ill. Dec. 830



May 16, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County; the Hon. JOHN J. HOBAN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois) judgment on jury verdict for arson, attempted arson, and theft by deception. He challenged the trial court's denial of his motion to suppress the tape recording of his conversation with an informant two years after the arson and the sufficiency of the arson indictment, and alleged certain errors at trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his wife were indicted for arson, attempted arson, solicitation and conspiracy to commit arson, and theft by deception, for burning down their apartment buildings. Their trials were severed. At defendant's trial, one arsonist testified he had been solicited by a third man to participate in the arson, which the two of them had done. He also testified on cross that he had never spoken with defendant until two years after the fire when he tape recorded a conversation for the State. The defense motion to suppress the recording on that basis was denied. Defendant challenged the eavesdrop petition and order, which resulted in the tape. He noted that the state's claim he met with the arsonist 10 times had been rebutted by the arsonist at trial. He also claimed the prosecution improperly cross-examined his wife and the defense was improperly limited in its cross of the arsonist on bias. The appellate court affirmed. There was ample cause to believe defendant's participation might have been the subject of conversation with a co-participant even two years later. The eavesdrop issue had been waived by failure to raise it before trial. There was no error.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. Unnecessary delay had waived the suppression issue. Allegations of negligence or innocent mistake were insufficient to attack the affidavit; the arson count of the indictment was not deficient. There was no reversible error in the prosecutor's cross-examination of defendant's wife or limiting cross-examination of the arsonist as to his bias.

People v. Thornton


No. 79-238


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


85 Ill. App. 3d 325; 406 N.E.2d 822; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3060; 40 Ill. Dec. 619



May 16, 1980, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 26, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County; the Hon. ROBERT L. GAGEN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois), which held on remand that defendant had waived the right to a jury trial. Defendant had been convicted of armed robbery and sentenced to 8 to 24 years in prison. The People contended that there was no appealable order.


OVERVIEW: The court remanded the case to the trial court to determine whether defendant waived the right to a jury trial. At a hearing on the waiver issue, the trial judge and the prosecutor testified that defendant waived a jury trial. The appeal notice stated that the appellate issue was the conviction, and that the date that the sentence was imposed was the date of the order that found a jury waiver. The court affirmed the judgment. Because the conviction was to be affirmed if the remand proceedings were proper, res judicata did not apply. The appeal notice was not defective enough to remove the court's jurisdiction because the People did not claim to have been prejudiced from the defects. Under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 329, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110A, para. 329 (1977), the burden of proof on remand was on the People as the seekers of the amendment and the trial court erred here. However, defendant now had to show more than this error because he was not prejudiced, and the finding that the prosecutor and the trial judge were more credible remained. The People did not have to demonstrate that a document supported the amendment because the amendment sought did not contradict the record.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that found that defendant had waived his right to trial by jury.

Kostelnak v. Retirement Bd. of Policemen's Annuity & Ben. Fund


No. 79-65


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


84 Ill. App. 3d 616; 405 N.E.2d 1170; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 2943; 40 Ill. Dec. 78



May 13, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. ARTHUR L. DUNNE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff retiree appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which affirmed a decision of defendant board denying him a supplemental annuity as provided in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 108 1/2, para. 5 -- 167.2 (1975). He contended that the statute, as signed by the governor, contained a printing error and that he was entitled to a supplemental annuity under the statute.


OVERVIEW: The retiree retired in 1967 from the police department at age 43 after serving 20 years. His length of service qualified him for a pension. The statute provided a supplement to the pension for policemen who retired before September 1, 1976, at age 50 or over with 20 years of service. The numbers 6 and 7 were transposed in the version of the bill signed by the governor. The bill the legislature passed said September 1, 1967. That was the clear legislative intent, as it did not change the date from prior versions of the statute. The court held that the statute should have read September 1, 1967. The retiree met two of the three statutory requirements. He retired before September 1, 1967 with 20 years of service, but he was not age 50 or over at retirement. Therefore he did not qualify for the supplemental annuity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

In re Extended March 1975 Grand Jury No. 655


No. 79-433


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


84 Ill. App. 3d 847; 405 N.E.2d 1176; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 2978; 40 Ill. Dec. 84



May 13, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. RICHARD J. FITZGERALD, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, parties to a civil suit (parties), sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied the parties their petition under Ill. Code of Crim. P. 6b, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 112 6(b), which sought the release of all evidence received by a particular grand jury.


OVERVIEW: The grand jury was impaneled to investigate improper intelligence activities of a police department. The grand jury found that the police had assaulted the fundamental freedoms of speech, association, press and religion as well as the constitutional right to privacy of hundreds of individuals, but did not return indictments and instead forwarded the names of the individuals for administrative action. The parties argued that a class action was an appropriate remedy, the grand jury's report was essential to its case, and the misconduct of the police presented a situation, which dictated that a disclosure of grand jury transcripts be made in the furtherance of justice. The parties also argued that the need to maintain public confidence in the police and public officials constituted a particularized need. The court held that denial of the report was proper because the parties failed to meet their burden of explaining why the discovery process was not sufficient to allow them to gather the evidence or at least make a more structured request rather than requesting the full report. The public policy against disclosure of grand jury proceedings was stronger than that for discovery.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which denied the parties their petition to obtain the evidence from a grand jury investigation.

 

1585 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Catholic Bishop of Chicago v. Justice


No. 79-115


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


84 Ill. App. 3d 827; 405 N.E.2d 1150; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 2976; 40 Ill. Dec. 58



May 9, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. NATHAN M. COHEN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, cemeteries and funeral directors, appealed from an order and judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied their motion to supplement and reopen the record in their action for a declaratory judgment and an injunction enjoining defendant village from enforcing Justice, Ill., Ordinance No. 76-3 (1976) and which held the ordinance severable and certain provisions valid.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs contended that the ordinance, which provided for burial permits and fees, was void in its entirety because it was not severable and it bore no reasonable relationship to the promotion of public welfare. They also contended that the trial court had erred in denying their motion to reopen the record. The court found that the provisions of the ordinance, which the trial court had voided, were not independent of the ones, which it had held valid. The court concluded that the village officials would not have adopted the ordinance without the invalid provisions. It held that the invalid provisions were not severable from the remainder of the ordinance and, thus, the entire ordinance was invalid. The court rejected plaintiffs' contention that additional evidence should have been allowed to show that the village had harassed and discriminated against the cemeteries. The court found that the parties had entered a stipulation that depositions would be treated as evidence because no other facts would be submitted. As the stipulation was not contrary to public policy or the product of fraud, the court held that the trial court had correctly denied plaintiffs' motion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court but affirmed its denial of the motion to reopen the record.

People v. Caliendo


No. 78-1148


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


84 Ill. App. 3d 987; 405 N.E.2d 1133; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 2998; 40 Ill. Dec. 41



May 9, 1980, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 13, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. FRANCIS J. MAHON, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of aggravated battery under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-3 and para 12-4 (1975).


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed a constitutional right to be warned of the exact degree of punishment that followed the prohibited conduct. The court affirmed the judgment and found that neither the United States nor the Illinois constitutions provided such a right. Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-3 and para 12-4 (1975) afforded defendant fair warning that his conduct was prohibited. The court found that defendant was aware of the charge against him and of the elements of that offense. Neither during the trial nor in the post-trial motion did defendant claim that the state failed to prove either of the alternative methods of committing a battery, which was the defect in the indictment. The indictment apprised defendant of the precise charge with sufficient specificity to enable him to prepare his defense. The court held that defendant's conviction for aggravated battery could be successfully pled as a bar to future prosecutions that arose out of the same conduct. The state's violation of Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 412(a)(ii) constituted harmless error. The court concluded that the evidence was not so improbable or unreasonable as to raise a reasonable doubt of defendant's guilt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted defendant of aggravated battery. The court held that the state's discovery violation was harmless error.

People v. Teague


No. 79-79


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


83 Ill. App. 3d 990; 404 N.E.2d 1054; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 2815; 39 Ill. Dec. 463



May 7, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Kankakee County; the Hon. JOHN F. MICHELA, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Circuit Court of Kankakee County (Illinois), which dismissed the petition for post conviction relief that he filed as to his convictions for aggravated kidnapping and for rape.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted defendant of aggravated kidnapping and rape. The trial court denied defendant's request for post-conviction relief, which was based on the denial of a pre-trial hearing pursuant to § 5-2-1 of the Unified Code of Corrections, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-2-1 (1973). The court reversed those convictions on appeal and remanded the action for a new trial. The court concluded that the associate judge wrongfully interpreted Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 295, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110A, para. 295 (1971), as requiring him to vacate his pre-trial grant of a fitness hearing. The court also held that there was a bona fide doubt as to defendant's fitness to stand trial and that failing to observe the procedure that was designed to protect his right to not be tried while unfit deprived him of his due process right to a fair trial. The court further opined that dismissing defendant's appeal of his conviction was equivalent to filing of no appeal at all because there the court did not consider any of his claims and that precedent showed that, due to his failure to appeal, res judicata did not bar defendant from seeking post-conviction relief for the alleged constitutional errors.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the denial of defendant's convictions of rape and aggravated kidnapping and remanded the action for a new trial.

People v. Lewis


No. 79-710


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


84 Ill. App. 3d 556; 406 N.E.2d 11; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 2932; 40 Ill. Dec. 310



May 6, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. ROBERT L. SKLODOWSKI, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which found him guilty of solicitation and sentenced him to a term of three years in the penitentiary.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contacted two brothers to arrange for them to burn down a warehouse containing defendant's belongings so that defendant could collect the insurance money. Defendant was caught because the brothers wore a wire during meetings in which defendant planned the crime. Defendant appealed his conviction for solicitation. The court affirmed. Defendant argued that the state failed to follow proper procedure in procuring the wiretap warrant. The court found that the procedures the state followed were more than adequate to satisfy the safeguards contemplated by statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 108-A-1 (1977), which required authorization of the state's attorney for an eavesdropping application. Defendant argued that the rules of evidence were violated when a transcript of the tape was admitted into evidence. The court found that any error in the admission of the transcript was harmless where the jury had an opportunity to listen to the tape and where defendant used the transcript to present his theory of the case and to impeach prosecution witnesses. The court also concluded that there was sufficient foundation for admission of the tape recording into evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for solicitation.

 

1589 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Ashcraft v. Board of Education


No. 15552


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


83 Ill. App. 3d 938; 404 N.E.2d 983; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 2807; 39 Ill. Dec. 392; 108 L.R.R.M. 2415



May 5, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Vermilion County; the Hon. CARL A. LUND, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff unpaid teachers, who did not receive wages covering a strike period, sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Vermilion County (Illinois), which declared the payment of wages by defendant school board to those teachers who signed an affidavit, which stated that they had intended to work during the strike, as valid and not in violation of the due process or equal protection clauses of the United States and state constitutions.


OVERVIEW: Unpaid teachers filed an action that contended that the board violated the due process or equal protection clauses of the United States and state constitutions when it paid wages to those teachers who signed affidavits, which stated they would have worked during the strike had the school not been closed. The trial court declared the action valid. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment. The court held that the unpaid teachers had failed to show that the action was either an arbitrary or unreasonable governmental action that deprived them of a guaranteed property interest. To the contrary, the court found that the board's action was neither arbitrary nor unreasonable because: (1) it was reasonable that the board did not want to penalize those teachers who did not participate in the strike but were precluded from teaching; (2) the affidavit was agreed to by the teachers' associations that had called for the strike; (3) the board was not legally obligated to pay any teacher for the days not worked; and (4) the salary distinction was related to the legitimate public policy purpose of not rewarding the unpaid teachers who had engaged in the illegal strike activity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that declared the school board's decision of compensating those teachers who swore that they had intended to work during the strike as valid.

 

1590 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. White


No. 79-623


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


84 Ill. App. 3d 1044; 406 N.E.2d 7; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3006; 40 Ill. Dec. 306



May 5, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. CLAUDE E. WHITAKER, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), convicting him of attempt sale of federal food stamps in violation of § 11--24 of the Illinois Public Aid Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 23, para. 11-24 (1977). He urged that the State failed to prove attempt beyond a reasonable doubt and that the statute was unconstitutional because it was overly broad.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of attempt sale of federal food stamps under para. 11-24 and he appealed. He urged that the State had not proven beyond a reasonable doubt either his specific intent to commit the crime or a substantial step toward the commission of the crime. He also claimed that the overly broad statute was unconstitutional. The court disagreed and affirmed. It explained that para. 11--24 made it a criminal offense to sell or exchange food stamps with some other person for another article. The court noted that the storeowner had testified that defendant asked him if he wanted to buy food stamps. After the storeowner declined the offer, defendant persisted, saying that he needed the money. The court held that this testimony established defendant's intent to sell food stamps. It further ruled that defendant's asking the storeowner if he wanted to buy food stamps constituted a substantial step toward the commission of the crime of selling food stamps. Thus, it held that the State had met its burden of proving attempt. The court declared that the statute was not unconstitutionally broad, as it rationally outlawed only unauthorized food stamp transactions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Brown v. Sexner


No. 79-1153


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


85 Ill. App. 3d 139; 405 N.E.2d 1082; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 3035; 39 Ill. Dec. 947



May 5, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. NATHAN B. ENGELSTEIN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff correctional officer appealed from the order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) upholding the decision of the police and corrections merit board (board) discharging the correctional officer from his position as captain of the department of corrections (department).


OVERVIEW: The sheriff filed a complaint against the correctional officer alleging that he violated the board's rules when he punched and kicked a junior correctional officer. The board found that the correctional officer violated the rules and discharged him. The correctional officer brought an administrative review, and the circuit court reversed one of the board's findings but upheld the correctional officer's discharge. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the board had jurisdiction to reconsider its earlier order dismissing the complaint against the correctional officer because the board had not issued a final and appealable order. The court determined that the board's findings were supported by the manifest weight of the evidence and that the correctional officer's conduct was sufficient cause for discharge even though the conduct occurred while he was off duty. Finally, the court held that the board's rules differentiating between suspension not to exceed 30 days and suspension pending discharge were neither unreasonable, violative of its rule-making authority, nor inconsistent with Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 125, paras. 112, 113 (1977).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order upholding the board's decision to discharge the correctional officer.

Dietz v. Midlothian


No. 79-983


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


83 Ill. App. 3d 638; 404 N.E.2d 955; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 2766; 39 Ill. Dec. 364



May 1, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. ARTHUR DUNNE, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an declaratory judgment action, defendants, property owners, a village, and a bank, sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which found that the village's zoning of the owners' property was arbitrary and unreasonable. Plaintiffs, neighboring homeowners and a homeowners' association, cross-appealed that portion of the judgment that declared that the village's annexation of the property was valid.


OVERVIEW: The trial court, in a declaratory judgment action, found that the village's annexation of the owners' property was valid, but that the village's zoning classification of the property as commercial and multiple family was arbitrary and capricious. On appeal, defendants argued that plaintiffs failed to prove that the classification was unreasonable. Plaintiffs argued that the annexation was void and unconstitutional. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment in part. The court found that plaintiffs had failed to sustain their burden of proving that the classification was arbitrary and capricious, noting that the evidence merely demonstrated that the property could have been zoned either single-family or commercial. Noting that plaintiffs had done no more than demonstrate a difference of opinion concerning the reasonableness of the classification, the court found that the legislative judgment was conclusive. The court rejected plaintiffs' contention that the annexation was void because the owners were not the owners of record when they signed the annexation petition, noting that the annexation statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24, para. 7 -- 1 -- 8 (1975), imposed no such requirement.


OUTCOME: The court modified the judgment by reversing the portion that declared the village's zoning classification arbitrary and capricious and affirmed the judgment as so modified.

Bramson v. Bramson


No. 79-771


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


83 Ill. App. 3d 657; 404 N.E.2d 469; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 2770; 39 Ill. Dec. 85



April 21, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. WILLIAM E. PETERSON, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former wife contested an order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), terminating maintenance payments by appellee former husband. She asserted that the parties' marital settlement agreement precluded the application of § 510(b) of the Illinois Marriage and Dissolution of Marriage Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 510(b) (1977) and that there was insufficient evidence of her continual cohabitation.


OVERVIEW: The former husband petitioned to terminate future maintenance payments to the former wife because she had been cohabiting with another man. The trial court granted the petition, ruling that the wife's conduct had amounted to cohabitation on a resident, continual conjugal basis under § 510(b). The wife appealed, alleging that § 510(b) did not apply because the parties' marital separation agreement had delineated the circumstances in which maintenance could be terminated. The court reversed, explaining that the parties' settlement agreement was irrelevant because the terminating events in § 510(b) were mandatory. Thus, § 510(b) applied to the petition. However, the court reversed because the trial court had misconstrued § 510(b). While not approving of the wife's living arrangements, the court concluded that her conduct did not fall within the provisions of § 510(b) and that not every conjugal cohabitation justified termination of maintenance. The wife had resided with her male friend for only four and one-half months and intended to move to the marital home with her children. Thus, the court could not say that her cohabitation had been continuous within the meaning of § 510(b).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order terminating the award of maintenance.

Director of Illinois Dep't of Agriculture v. Carroll Feed Service, Inc.


No. 79-347


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


83 Ill. App. 3d 164; 403 N.E.2d 762; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 2683; 38 Ill. Dec. 531



April 15, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Carroll County; the Hon. RICHARD DeMOSS, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant grain dealer appealed from a judgment on the pleadings entered by the Circuit Court of Carroll County (Illinois) in an action filed by plaintiff Director of the Department of Agriculture to permanently enjoin the dealer from operating a grain dealership without a license.


OVERVIEW: The dealer's license was suspended for failure to post a surety bond or its equivalent based on a percentage of its gross sales. The Director filed an action to enjoin the dealer from operating a grain dealership without a license. The trial court granted the Director judgment on the pleadings. The dealer's principal contention was that the bonding provisions of An Act to License and Regulate Grain Dealers, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111, para. 303 (1977) were unconstitutional on equal protection grounds. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court held that the classification based on gross sales bore a rational relationship to a legitimate legislative purpose. The legitimate state purpose of the Act was to safeguard producers from the bankruptcy of grain dealers. The legislature may have decided that it was rational to first protect against bankruptcies by small dealers and that a dealer who did a large volume business indicated some degree of sound management and customer confidence. Referencing the amount of the bond to sales volume appeared to be a rational approach.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court granting injunctive relief to the Director against the dealer.

People v. Pollution Control Bd.


No. 79-884


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


83 Ill. App. 3d 802; 404 N.E.2d 352; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 2793; 38 Ill. Dec. 928



April 10, 1980, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 15, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: PETITION for review of order of Pollution Control Board.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Pollution Control Board (Illinois) granted respondent corporation's motion to dismiss petitioner attorney general's complaint alleging that the corporation caused or allowed the emission of sound beyond the boundaries of its motor vehicle racing facility so as to cause noise pollution in violation of certain state statutes and regulations. The attorney general appealed the Pollution Control Board's (board) order of dismissal.


OVERVIEW: During the pendency of the board's hearings concerning the attorney general's complaint, the Environmental Protection Act (act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 1/2, para. 1001 et seq. (1977), was amended so as to totally exempt certain sporting events from noise emission standards and limitations. The board's order of dismissal was predicated on the amendment to the act, which essentially provided that without an endorsement from one of certain private organizations, any motor racing event had to comply with the board's noise pollution standards and regulations. Moreover, in granting the corporation's motion to dismiss, the board did not consider the attorney general's arguments concerning the alleged unconstitutionality of the amendment. On appeal, the attorney general again argued, inter alia, that the amendment unconstitutionally delegated legislative power. After rejecting the corporation's argument that the attorney general lacked standing to challenge the constitutionality of the amendment, the court reversed and remanded for further proceedings. The amendment improperly delegated to private groups the right to determine which events would be exempt from the act and which would not.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the board's order and remanded for further proceedings.

Schwarzbach v. Highland Park


No. 79-93


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


82 Ill. App. 3d 807; 403 N.E.2d 102; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 2605; 38 Ill. Dec. 87



April 3, 1980, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 11, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. LLOYD A. VAN DEUSEN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city appealed from a declaratory judgment issued by the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which, in plaintiff landowners' suit, found that a special service area was properly created by the city, but which enjoined the city from passing ordinances for the issuance of bonds or the levy of annual taxes for special services without holding further hearings.


OVERVIEW: The city council adopted an ordinance proposing establishment of the service area, and sent notice of the hearing to all persons in whose name the general taxes for the last preceding year were paid on each parcel of land lying within the special service area. The landowners argued that the notices were improperly sent, that the form of the notice deprived them of due process, that a sufficient number of objections in each category was filed, and that the city erred in determining the number of objections filed by the electors and property owners. The trial court determined those issues in the city's favor, but found that both the ordinance proposing and that establishing the service area included only the maximum amount of bonds which could be issued and only the maximum rate of taxes which could be extended, and were thus illegal and invalid. The court held that the notice given was not appropriate to the combined proceedings which both formed the special service area and purported to advise the landowners of their obligation, and that the notice was not sent to all persons owning real estate or taxable personalty as required by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 1304 (1977).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and remanded the case with directions that there be further hearings limited to the right of owners of real estate and electors in the service area to object to the issuance of bonds in the amount specified and the levy of taxes.

Cable Television Co. v. Illinois Commerce Com.


No. 79-308


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


82 Ill. App. 3d 814; 403 N.E.2d 287; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 2606; 38 Ill. Dec. 199



April 3, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of McHenry County; the Hon. ROLAND HERRMANN, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant cable companies challenged an order of the Circuit Court of McHenry County (Illinois), which ruled that appellee Illinois Commerce Commission (ICC) had the authority to regulate pole agreements under § 27 of the Illinois Public Utility Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 2/3, para. 27 (1977).


OVERVIEW: The cable companies entered into contracts with public utilities to lease space on utility poles in order to string transmission cables. The cable companies sought to enjoin the ICC from exercising jurisdiction over the pole attachment agreements. The trial court ruled that the ICC had the authority to regulate the agreements under § 27. The court affirmed and held that because the ICC had the power to regulate leasing activities, it was under the mandate to assure that the charges were just and reasonable. The ICC had the basic duty to protect the utility and the public. Therefore, it was reasonable that the ICC was given jurisdiction over pole attachment rates in order to insure that persons desiring to use the facilities bore reasonable shares of the costs incurred by the utilities in maintaining and owning them. The ICC had been given authority to regulate, among other things, the lease or other encumbrance of the whole or any part of its equipment. The poles were tangible personal property that were necessary to fulfill the utilities' duties. Therefore, considering a proposal to lease or encumber any part of them properly belonged to the ICC and required its approval.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order ruling that the ICC had the authority to regulate pole agreements under the Illinois Public Utility Act.

 

1598 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Collinsville v. Seiber


No. 79-275


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


82 Ill. App. 3d 719; 403 N.E.2d 90; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 2593; 38 Ill. Dec. 75



April 1, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Madison County; the Hon. THOMAS GIBBONS, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Madison County (Illinois), which, upon the complaints filed by the city, found him guilty of committing a nuisance at two separate locations, a violation of Collinsville, Ill., Code § 9.16.140.


OVERVIEW: Defendant operated a sanitation service, which consisted of garbage and trash collection and buying and selling scrap iron, metal, and similar items. A city police officer went to defendant's residential and business properties on two separate dates and observed a variety of items scattered about the premises. The city filed complaints against defendant alleging that he had committed a nuisance on the properties by permitting or maintaining an unsightly yard in violation of the city's nuisance ordinance. Defendant was found guilty. The court affirmed. The court held that the ordinance was constitutional. The ordinance was clearly related to the public health; thus, it was a permissible exercise of the city's authority. Moreover, the ordinance was a reasonable exercise of the city's police power, as it did not prohibit sanitation services or junk yards, but required that all property be maintained in a sanitary manner. Defendant made no showing that he could not have conducted his business without violating the ordinance. The jury's finding that a nuisance in fact existed was not against the manifest weight of the evidence. There was no basis for a claim of selective prosecution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Cary v. Pollution Control Bd.


No. 79-314


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


82 Ill. App. 3d 793; 403 N.E.2d 83; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 2603; 38 Ill. Dec. 68

PRIOR HISTORY: PETITION for review of order of Pollution Control Board.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner village sought review of an order of the Illinois Pollution Control Board (board) that denied its petition for a variance from compliance with the barium limitation standard established by Illinois Pollution Control Board Rules and Regulations, chapter 6, Public Water Supplies, Rule 304B(4).


OVERVIEW: The village sought a variance from compliance with the barium limitation standard established by Illinois Pollution Control Board Rules and Regulations, chapter 6, Public Water Supplies, Rule 304B(4). The board denied that petition, and the village appealed. Further, the court noted that the record was insufficient for the court to review the order. Accordingly, the court reversed the board's order and remanded the matter for further hearing pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 1/2, paras. 1035-1038 (1977).


OUTCOME: The board's order that denied the village's petition for a variance was vacated, and the matter remanded to the board for further proceedings.

People v. Nobles


No. 15396


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


83 Ill. App. 3d 711; 404 N.E.2d 330; 1980 Ill. App. LEXIS 2777; 38 Ill. Dec. 906



April 1, 1980, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus denied Nobles v. Welborn, 67 F.3d 301, 1995 U.S. App. LEXIS 32305 (7th Cir. Ill., 1995)
Post-conviction relief denied at People v. Nobles, 335 Ill. App. 3d 1214, 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 3356 (Ill. App. Ct. 4th Dist., 2003)
Post-conviction proceeding at People v. Nobles, 359 Ill. App. 3d 1219, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 4306 (Ill. App. Ct. 4th Dist., 2005)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at, Motion granted by People v. Nobles, 2012 IL App (4th) 100792-U, 2012 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1094 (2012)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Sharif v. Williams, 2015 IL App (3d) 140865-U, 2015 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1941 (2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from the Circuit Court of Macon County; the Hon. DONALD W. MORTHLAND, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Macon County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of the murders of his girlfriend and his cellmate after his arrest, for which defendant was sentenced to concurrent terms of 40 years and natural life.


OVERVIEW: Following an argument in his car, defendant shot his girlfriend. Following his arrest and detainment, defendant choked and killed his cellmate. Defendant was tried before a jury, convicted, and sentenced to concurrent terms of 40 years and natural life, respectively. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the absence of co-counsel during jury venire was not prejudicial as other competent counsel was present and that the exclusion of jurors for their beliefs on the death penalty did not make the jury more conviction prone. The court further held that defendant's behavior was not motivated by insanity to justify the killings under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1(b), and his sentence of natural life was not unconstitutional because the aggravating circumstances warranting its imposition were not vague and ambiguous. The court finally held that defendant's long history of drug use did not require that his sentence be reduced.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for the murders of his girlfriend and his cellmate following his arrest and detainment, and affirmed defendant's sentence to concurrent terms of 40 years and natural life.
